Francistown — second-largest city; former gold-rush town near the Shashe River. (2)

Maun — major tourist hub near the Okavango Delta and Makgadikgadi pans. (1)

Diamonds — Botswana is Africa's largest diamond producer; the Debswana mines are a joint venture between the government and De Beers; rough stones are exported to Surat and Antwerp. (2)

People

San Bushmen — indigenous hunter-gatherers; speak click-heavy Tuu/Ju|'hoan languages; rock art and a 70,000-year-old python-head artifact at the Tsodilo Hills; depicted in The Gods Must Be Crazy. (3)

Tswana — Bantu majority ethnic group and namesake of the country. (1)

Brazil 107
Federative Republic of Brazil · South America · Capital: Brasília
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Brasília — purpose-built planned capital that replaced Rio de Janeiro in 1960; ordered by Juscelino Kubitschek to fulfill a campaign promise. (3)

Borders: more nations than any other Western Hemisphere country — includes both Suriname and Paraguay; the only major South American countries it doesn't border are Chile and Ecuador. (2)

Demographics: second-largest population in the Americas; largest Catholic country in the world; thousands of Pentecostal 'Assemblies of God' churches; Macumba is a broad term for syncretic Yoruba-based religions including Candomblé, Quimbanda and Umbanda. (2)

Language: the only Portuguese-speaking country in the Americas. (2)

Aerospace & airlines: the Alcântara Space Center in Maranhão is the closest launch site to the equator; Embraer is HQ'd in São José dos Campos; TAM merged with Chile's LAN. (1)

Brasília

Designers: master plan by Lúcio Costa; signature buildings by Oscar Niemeyer; landscape by Burle Marx; original plan known as Plano Piloto; James Holston's The Modernist City is a famous critique. (2)

Shape & axes: city laid out in an airplane shape with the Monumental Axis and the Highway Axis. (2)

Lake Paranoá — artificial reservoir; submerged the former town of Vila Amaury; crossed by the Juscelino Kubitschek Bridge. (2)

Praça dos Três Poderes — central square housing the Palácio do Planalto (presidency), Palácio da Alvorada (presidential residence), and the National Congress twin towers with bowl and dome. (2)

Cathedral of Brasília — crown-shaped hyperboloid with 3-m statues of the four evangelists. (1)

Itamaraty Palace ('Palace of the Arches') — foreign ministry. (1)

Major Rivers & Wetlands

Amazon River — world's largest river by discharge; rises in Peru and crosses northern Brazil; mouth at the island of Marajó (largest river island in the world); flows past Santarém in Pará state; connected to the Orinoco via the natural Casiquiare Canal; meets the Rio Negro at the Meeting of Waters in Manaus. (4)

Pantanal — world's largest tropical wetland; mostly in Mato Grosso do Sul; ~80% submerged in the rainy season; supports the highest crocodilian (yacare caiman) population on Earth; threatened by fazendas and gold-mercury runoff; the Three Brothers River flows through it. (3)

Itaipu Dam — on the Paraná River; shared with Paraguay; world's largest hydroelectric producer; name means 'singing stone' in Ava-Guarani; submerged the formerly massive Guaíra Falls during construction; tens of thousands of Ava-Guarani were displaced; 2009 storms blacked out all of Paraguay for 15 minutes. (2)

São Francisco River — runs through a rift valley in Minas Gerais's western border. (1)

Regions & Key States

Pernambuco — northeastern state with capital Recife (formerly Mauritsstad; first Atlantic slave port; site of Kahal Zur Israel, the oldest synagogue in the Americas; home of the Frevo dance; administers Fernando de Noronha); also hosted 2014 FIFA World Cup matches. (2)

Espírito Santo — east-coast state; capital Vitória; Vila Velha hosts Garoto, Latin America's largest chocolate factory; Guarapari beach is famous for radioactive sand; controls remote Trindade and Martim Vaz islands. (2)

Santa Catarina — southern state; capital Florianópolis (island city); Blumenau hosts the Americas' largest Oktoberfest; site of Beto Carrero World (Latin America's largest theme park); affected by South Atlantic's only recorded hurricane. (1)

Mato Grosso & Mato Grosso do Sul — central-west states; contain most of the Pantanal and Brazilian Amazon savanna; home of the Kawahiva people. (2)

Rio Grande do Sul — southernmost state; capital Porto Alegre; Gaucho culture; Italian and German immigrant communities. (2)

Fernando de Noronha Archipelago — UNESCO Atlantic island group administered by Pernambuco. (1)

Economy & Culture

Coffee — Brazil has dominated world production since 1852; the 'Café com leite' ('coffee with milk') political era was named for the alliance of São Paulo (coffee) and Minas Gerais (dairy). (3)

Football — five-time World Cup winners; rivalry with Italy; legends include Pelé and Ronaldo Nazário; Maracanã stadium in Rio is iconic. (2)

Carnival — major celebrations in Rio, Salvador, and Recife. (2)

Regional Files

Rio de Janeiro (city/state) — see `brazil_rio_de_janeiro.json`. (8)

São Paulo (city/state) — see `brazil_sao_paulo.json`. (4)

Amazonas — Manaus, Amazon basin — see `brazil_amazonas.json`. (4)

Bahia — Salvador, northeast — see `brazil_bahia.json`. (4)

Minas Gerais — Belo Horizonte, mining country — see `brazil_minas_gerais.json`. (2)

British Columbia 14
Pacific province · Capital: Victoria · Largest city: Vancouver
Canada (Provinces & Territories)

At a Glance

Capital: Victoria on Vancouver Island. (1)

Largest city: Vancouver — largest port on the Salish Sea; named for British Captain George Vancouver who surveyed the area in the 1790s. (5)

Hosted the 2010 Winter Olympics (Whistler and Vancouver). (1)

Vancouver

Stanley Park — 1,000-acre urban forest; the Lions Gate Bridge crosses its north end. (2)

Gastown — historic neighborhood named for 'Gassy Jack' Deighton. (1)

Coal Harbour — modern glass-clad downtown; Living Shangri-La is the tallest building. (1)

Marine Building — Art-Deco landmark that doubled as Daily Planet HQ in films. (1)

99 B-Line — Canada's busiest bus corridor (Point Grey ↔ Kitsilano). (1)

Cypress Mountain — overlooking ski area; Sea-to-Sky Highway climbs to Whistler. (1)

Coast & Islands

Vancouver Island — separated from the mainland by the Strait of Georgia and from Washington by the Strait of Juan de Fuca; Nanaimo is its main mainland-side city; Blackcomb ski resort. (3)

Haida Gwaii (Queen Charlotte Islands) — archipelago renamed for the Haida indigenous people. (2)

Nootka Sound — site of the 1789 seizure of British ships by Spain that nearly led to war. (1)

Prince Rupert — BC's largest port directly on the open Pacific. (1)

Interior

Fraser River — major river; merges with the Nechako at Prince George; Hells Gate narrow canyon; site of the 1858 Fraser Canyon Gold Rush at Lytton where it meets the Thompson River. (3)

Kamloops — at the confluence of the North and South Thompson; Sun Peaks ski resort; Peter Wing elected the first Chinese-Canadian mayor here in 1966. (2)

Selkirk Mountains — interior range; town of Nelson went from silver-mining to hippie hub. (1)

Coast Mountains / Fraser Plateau — major interior ranges. (1)

Brunei 15
Brunei Darussalam ('Abode of Peace') · Borneo · Capital: Bandar Seri Begawan
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Bandar Seri Begawan — renamed in 1970 after Sultan Omar Ali Saifuddien III; contains Kampong Ayer, the 'Venice of the East' stilt village. (3)

Sultan: Hassanal Bolkiah lives in the Istana Nurul Iman, the world's largest residential palace. (3)

State ideology: Melayu Islam Beraja ('Malay Islamic Monarchy'). (1)

Smallest country on Borneo; surrounded on land by Malaysian Sarawak; only port city is Muara. (4)

Currency — the Brunei dollar is pegged to the Singapore dollar. (1)

Geography & Districts

Four districts: Brunei-Muara (containing the capital), Tutong, Belait (oil-producing), and the geographically separated Temburong. (4)

Limbang District — ceded to Sarawak, splitting Brunei into two land parcels (despite being on the same landmass). (2)

Sultan Omar Saifuddien Bridge — connects the main territory to the Temburong exclave; capital of Temburong is Bangar. (2)

Brunei Bay — entrance guarded by the Malaysian Labuan Federal Territory; receives the Brunei River that flows through the capital; contains the deepwater port of Muara and the port of Sipitang. (1)

Economy & Resources

Petroleum — refining drives the economy; Seria in Belait District is the main producing region; target of a 1962 uprising. (3)

ASEAN — Brunei hosts the ASEAN Business Council secretariat. (1)

History

James Brooke — British adventurer who helped an early Brunei ruler against the Iban; later became the 'White Rajah' of Sarawak. (1)

Spratly Islands — Brunei is one of the claimants to portions of this disputed archipelago in the South China Sea. (1)

Bulgaria 17
Republic of Bulgaria · Balkans · Capital: Sofia
Balkans

At a Glance

Capital: Sofia — founded over 2,400 years ago; on the Iskar River near Vitosha Mountain; surrounded by the Balkan Mountains. (4)

Borders: Romania (north, across the Danube), Serbia and North Macedonia (west), Greece (south), Turkey (southeast), Black Sea (east). (3)

History: lost its Aegean coast in the Second Balkan War; gained independence after the Russo-Turkish War of 1877 (commemorated by Sofia's gold-domed national cathedral). (2)

Sofia Landmarks

Alexander Nevsky Cathedral — gold-domed national cathedral. (2)

Boyana Church — UNESCO-listed medieval church with frescoes. (2)

Physical Geography

Balkan Mountains (Stara Planina) — give the peninsula its name; divided into thirds by the Arabakonak and Vratnik Passes; Shipka Pass connects Gabrovo and Kazanluk; climaxes at Mt. Botev; crossed by the Iskar River. (3)

Rila Mountains — contain Mt. Musala, the country's (and the Balkans') highest peak; home to the iconic white-striped Rila Monastery. (2)

Rhodope Mountains — southern range home to many of Europe's bats and birds of prey. (3)

Osogovo & Vlahina Mountains — mark the western border. (1)

Belogradchik Rocks — distinctive sandstone formations near the town of Belogradchik in Vidin Province. (2)

Devetashka Cave — eroded by the Osam River. (1)

Black Sea coast — features Lake Varna, the Kamchia Biosphere Reserve, and the Thracian Plain agricultural region. (2)

Cities & Regions

Plovdiv — second-largest city; on the Maritsa River; gateway to the Rhodope Mountains; known as Philippopolis under Rome; old town has a Roman amphitheater, the Dhumaya Mosque, and the Church of St. Constantine and Elena; Stolipinovo is the Balkans' largest Roma neighborhood. (3)

Varna — third-largest city; major Black Sea port; gateway to the Golden Sands resort; sits on a liman fed by the Devnya and Provadiyska Rivers and crossed by the Asparuhov Bridge. (2)

Veliko Tarnovo — medieval capital in the Yantra Gorge of the Balkan foothills. (1)

Vidin & Ruse — northern Danube ports. (1)

Dobrudzha — fruit-producing region; northern half is in Romania. (1)

History & Culture

Thrace — ancient region shared with Greece and Turkey; archaeological sites yield Thracian gold. (2)

Burkina Faso 5
West Africa (landlocked, Sahel) · Capital: Ouagadougou
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Ouagadougou — largest city of the Mossi people; in Kadiogo Province; landmarks include the Moro-Naba Palace and the presidential Kosyam Palace; hosts the biennial FESPACO film festival. (2)

Name: formerly Upper Volta; renamed Burkina Faso ('Land of Incorruptible People') in 1984. (2)

Alliance of Sahel States — formed with Mali and Niger after recent coups, in opposition to ECOWAS. (1)

Geography

Mount Tenakourou — country's highest point; near the source of the Black Volta River. (2)

Volta River system — the Black, White, and Red Volta tributaries originate in Burkina Faso before flowing south to Ghana. (2)

Culture

Mossi people — dominant ethnic group; the Moro-Naba is their traditional king (Friday ceremonies in Ouagadougou involve the king first appearing in red on horseback, then returning in white after an oath of allegiance and a cannon blast). (2)

FESPACO — the Pan-African Film and Television Festival of Ouagadougou; Africa's largest film festival. (1)

Burundi 10
Republic of Burundi · East Africa (Great Lakes) · Capital: Gitega
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital change: Gitega became the political capital in January 2019, replacing Bujumbura (which remains the largest city and seat of government); promised by then-leader Pierre Nkurunziza. (3)

Government: ruled by Évariste Ndayishimiye after Pierre Nkurunziza (who became the first world leader to die of COVID-19). (1)

Ethnic groups: majority Hutu and minority Tutsi, mirroring neighboring Rwanda; the Tutsi-affiliated Kingdom of Burundi was based in Gitega. (2)

Language: Kirundi. (1)

Economy: coffee is the main export. (1)

Bujumbura

Largest city — on the shores of Lake Tanganyika. (4)

Rusizi National Park lies nearby. (1)

Stanley–Livingstone monument — marks the controversial site where Henry Morton Stanley supposedly met Dr. Livingstone (just south of the city, actually at Ujiji, 1871). (1)

Geography

Lake Tanganyika — forms the western border; world's second-deepest lake and second-largest by volume; largest rift lake in Africa; shared with Tanzania, DRC, and Zambia; receives the Ruzizi River from Lake Kivu; drained by the Lukuga River to the Congo headwaters. (5)

Ruvyironza River — considered by some the most remote source of the Nile. (1)

Mt. Kikizi — Burundi claims a spring on this peak as the southernmost source of the Nile. (1)

Diaspora & Conflict

Banyamulenge — community of Burundian-descended Abatutsi (Tutsi) in South Kivu in the eastern DRC; their persecution helped fuel the Great Lakes Refugee Crisis. (1)

California 128
'The Golden State' · Pacific Coast · Capital: Sacramento
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Sacramento. (1)

Largest city: Los Angeles — Hollywood; Long Beach (oil field at Signal Hill, Walter Pyramid, RMS Queen Mary), Pasadena, Anaheim (Disneyland); ports of LA/Long Beach. (1)

Bay Area: San Francisco (Golden Gate Bridge, Ocean Beach, Alcatraz), San Jose (Silicon Valley), Oakland, Berkeley, Stanford (Palo Alto). (1)

Other major cities: San Diego (UCSD; Geisel Library with the Snake Path), Fresno, Bakersfield. (1)

Most populous US state (~39 million). (1)

Mountains & Deserts

Sierra Nevada — eastern mountain range; Mount Whitney is the highest peak in the lower 48; Lake Tahoe at the Nevada border. (2)

Yosemite National Park — Sierra-Nevada park; Half Dome, El Capitan, Tuolumne Meadows; O'Shaughnessy Dam in Hetch Hetchy. (1)

Sequoia & Kings Canyon National Parks — giant sequoia groves including the General Sherman Tree (world's largest single-stem tree). (1)

Death Valley National Park — Mojave Desert; Badwater Basin is the lowest land elevation in North America (-282 ft). (1)

Joshua Tree National Park — named for the yucca brevifolia. (1)

Mojave Desert — vast southern desert. (1)

Coast Ranges — coastal mountains. (1)

Coast & Geography

Pacific Coast Highway (Hwy 1) — winds along the entire coast. (1)

Big Sur — dramatic coastal stretch in Central California. (1)

Channel Islands — eight Pacific islands, five protected as a National Park. (1)

Central Valley — vast agricultural valley between the Sierra and the Coast Ranges. (1)

San Andreas Fault — runs through the state. (1)

Aerospace & Industry

Vandenberg Space Force Base — polar-orbit launches; adjoined by Point Arguello Light. (1)

Silicon Valley — global tech industry center. (1)

Hollywood — global film industry. (1)

Cambodia 25
Kingdom of Cambodia · Southeast Asia · Capital: Phnom Penh
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Phnom Penh — once known as Krong Chaktomuk ('City of the Four Faces'); at the confluence of the Mekong, Tonlé Sap, and Bassac Rivers; Monivong Bridge crosses the Bassac origin. (4)

Language & people: mostly Khmer (~17 million); Khmer is the official Austroasiatic language; Apsara classical dance. (2)

Borders: Thailand (W), Laos (N), Vietnam (E), Gulf of Thailand (S). (2)

Phnom Penh

Royal Palace — renovated by King Sisorath; includes the Khemarin Palace and Moonlight Pavilion. (2)

Silver Pagoda — houses the Emerald Buddha of Cambodia. (2)

Dubai Mosque — sits next to Boeng Kak lake in the city's north, near Camko City. (2)

Angkor & Siem Reap

Angkor Wat — the world's largest religious monument; built by Suryavarman II; faces west (unusual for Hindu temples); features the 'Churning of the Sea of Milk' bas-relief; represents Mount Meru; appears on Cambodia's flag. (5)

Angkor (Yasodharapura) — ancient Khmer capital; sacked by the Ayutthaya Kingdom; Jayavarman II declared himself 'universal monarch' here; contains East and West Baray reservoirs; first European sighting by Henri Mouhot. (3)

Bayon — Buddhist temple built by Jayavarman VII, famed for its giant smiling faces. (3)

Siem Reap — tourist gateway to Angkor; Psah Chas old market; Apsara dance shows; Sombai rice wine; landmine museum. (3)

Preah Vihear Temple — Hindu temple on the Thai border; ICJ ruled in Cambodia's favor in a longstanding dispute. (1)

Tonlé Sap & Rivers

Tonlé Sap — largest lake in Southeast Asia; famous for seasonal flow reversal that swells it 6× during the monsoon; supports floating Cham villages; fed by the Sekong, Sesan, and Srepok rivers; ringed by ancient Khmer cities; once home to a record 670-lb giant catfish. (5)

Water and Moon Festival — annual celebration of the Tonlé Sap's reversal; honors the naga tooth myth. (1)

Mekong River — crosses eastern Cambodia from Laos to Vietnam; forms part of the Mekong River Commission with Laos, Cambodia, and Vietnam. (4)

Other Geography

Cardamom Mountains (Damrei Mountains) — southwestern range; highest point Phnom Aural (a.k.a. Kravanh). (2)

Yak Loum — crater lake in the northeast. (1)

Kirirom National Park — pine-forested upland park. (1)

Sihanoukville — major port city named for former King Norodom Sihanouk. (1)

Battambang — second-largest city, on the Tonlé Sap. (1)

Kouprey — endangered forest ox; national animal. (1)

Cameroon 18
Republic of Cameroon · Central Africa / Gulf of Guinea · Capital: Yaoundé
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Yaoundé — political capital; Douala is the largest port in Central Africa. (3)

Colonial split: part French / part British colony; Anglophone northwest/southwest regions retain English law. (2)

Anglophone Crisis — separatists declared the unrecognized Federal Republic of Ambazonia (capital Bambara, biggest city Buea); supported by some Biafran sympathizers; leadership dispute between Samuel Ikome Sako and the kidnapped Julius Ayuk Tabe. (2)

Government: ruled by Paul Biya since 1982. (1)

Physical Geography

Mount Cameroon — highest and most prominent peak in West Africa; rises over 13,000 ft above the Gulf of Guinea; chief crater Fako (most active); other vents include Meyer and Waldau; Buea at its base; Debundscha is the 5th-wettest community on Earth. (2)

Cameroon Line — volcanic chain extending from Mount Cameroon offshore through Bioko, Annobón, and São Tomé and Príncipe. (1)

Adamawa Highlands — east-west plateau extending to the Central African Republic; source of the Benue River; named for an emirate of the Sokoto Caliphate. (1)

Bakossi Mountains, Mount Kupe, Mount Manengouba — volcanic peaks in the southwest. (1)

Waza National Park — Far North Region park along the Yaeré floodplain. (1)

Bouba Njida National Park — site of the 2012 elephant massacre (650 killed for their ivory). (1)

Killer Lakes

Lake Nyos — volcanic crater lake in the NW Region; in 1986 a CO₂ limnic eruption ('mazuku' / 'evil wind') killed over 1,000 villagers; venting pipes installed by George Kling and Bill Evans; its natural dam is deteriorating, threatening Nigeria's Taraba and Benue states. (2)

Lake Monoun — also experienced a limnic eruption (1984); one of only three known such lakes worldwide. (1)

Rivers & Coast

Sanaga River — largest river; powers the Edéa hydroelectric plant; supplies the aluminum smelter at Douala. (1)

Wouri River estuary — Douala's port; namesake of Cameroon's 'ghost shrimp'. (1)

Bight of Biafra / Bight of Bonny — Cameroon's coast on the Gulf of Guinea. (1)

Canada 116
Constitutional monarchy & federal parliamentary democracy · North America · Capital: Ottawa
North America

At a Glance

Capital: Ottawa — in Ontario on the Rideau Canal; connected to Gatineau (Quebec); Parliament Hill with the Peace Tower; Château Laurier; ChaudièreFalls hydropower. (3)

Languages: English and French (official bilingual); Algonquian and Inuit languages widely spoken. (1)

Geography records: longest coastline in the world; second-largest country by area; Mount Logan in Yukon is the second-tallest mountain in North America. (3)

EEZ hole — the French territory of Saint-Pierre and Miquelon creates a notch in Canada's Atlantic EEZ; Hans Island in the Arctic is shared with Denmark (split 2022; tradition of leaving schnapps/whisky). (2)

Border: the US–Canada border is partly the 49th parallel; established by the Treaty of Paris (1783), refined by the Jay and Oregon Treaties. (2)

Cities (cross-province): Windsor sits at the Ambassador Bridge (blocked by 2022 Freedom Convoy protests); Niagara Falls straddles the Ontario–New York border (Horseshoe + Bridal Veil falls). (2)

Major Geography

Great Lakes — Canada shares Superior, Huron, Erie, Ontario with the US; Lake Ontario drains via Niagara Falls to the St. Lawrence. (2)

St. Lawrence River — flows from Lake Ontario through Quebec into the Gulf of St. Lawrence (contains Anticosti Island and the PEI peninsula); estuary off the Gaspé Peninsula; navigable via the Seaway. (2)

Hudson Bay & James Bay — vast inland seas surrounded by Nunavut, Manitoba, Ontario, Quebec. (2)

Mackenzie River — Canada's longest river ('Deh Cho' in Dene); flows from Great Slave Lake through the NWT to the Beaufort Sea; receives the Liard at Fort Simpson; passes the Sans Sault Rapids; explored by Alexander Mackenzie. (3)

Great Bear Lake / Great Slave Lake — Canada's two largest lakes, both in the NWT; Great Bear hosts the former Port Radium / Eldorado uranium mine. (4)

Rocky Mountains / Canadian Rockies — cross Alberta and BC; contain Banff, Jasper, Yoho, Kootenay, and Waterton Lakes National Parks; Icefields Parkway. (2)

Regional Files

Ontario — Toronto, the Great Lakes south — see `canada_ontario.json`. (9)

Quebec — Montreal, Quebec City, Gaspé — see `canada_quebec.json`. (11)

British Columbia — Vancouver, Victoria, the Pacific Coast — see `canada_british_columbia.json`. (12)

Alberta — Calgary, Edmonton, Banff/Jasper — see `canada_alberta.json`. (9)

Atlantic Provinces — Nova Scotia, New Brunswick, PEI, Newfoundland & Labrador — see `canada_atlantic.json`. (14)

Prairie Provinces — Saskatchewan, Manitoba — see `canada_prairies.json`. (3)

Northern Territories — Yukon, Northwest Territories, Nunavut — see `canada_north.json`. (15)

Cape Verde 4
Republic of Cabo Verde · Atlantic island nation · Capital: Praia
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Praia — on Santiago island; contains the Sucupira Market in the Plato district and the Fortaleza of São Filipe in Cidade Velha. (1)

Two island groups: Barlavento (Windward) in the north and Sotavento (Leeward) in the south. (2)

Mainland namesake: the Cap-Vert Peninsula in Senegal — westernmost point of mainland Africa, with the Deux Mamelles volcanoes. (1)

Geography & Culture

Islands: Santiago, Santo Antão, São Vicente, Fogo (active volcano), Boa Vista, Sal, Maio, Santa Luzia (only uninhabited Barlavento island). (2)

Tope de Coroa — highest point in the northern (Barlavento) archipelago. (2)

Serra da Malagueta — Santiago's mountain range. (1)

Music: Cesária Évora's morna, the polyrhythmic batuque, uptempo funaná; the bowed cimboa chordophone. (1)

Endemic birds: Raso lark and cane warbler. (1)

Central African Republic 10
Landlocked Central Africa · Capital: Bangui
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Bangui — on the north bank of the Ubangi River; sits at the center of Africa's largest magnetic anomaly; largest suburb Bimbo. (4)

Boganda National Museum — Bangui museum featuring pygmy peoples exhibits. (2)

History: under French colonial rule was named for the Ubangi and Chari rivers; nicknamed la colonie poubelle ('trashcan colony'); in 1977 Jean-Bédel Bokassa crowned himself Emperor in near-copy of Napoleon's 1804 ceremony; Séléka forces captured Bangui in 2013. (3)

Languages: French and Sango are official. (1)

Geography

Ubangi River — major southern river forming the border with the DRC; flows past Bangui; tributary of the Congo. (5)

Sangha River — formed at Nola from the Mabéré and Kadéï rivers; joins the Congo. (2)

Mbomou + Uele rivers — combine to form the Ubangi. (1)

Mont Ngaoui — highest point; on the Cameroon border. (1)

Fertit Hills and Yade Massif — northern uplands. (1)

Manovo-Gounda St. Floris National Park — UNESCO park on the Vakaga River. (1)

Dzanga-Ndoki National Park — part of the trinational Sangha Trinational UNESCO site. (1)

Chinko Nature Reserve — major wildlife reserve. (1)

Bakouma subprefecture — large uranium deposits. (1)

Chad 16
Republic of Chad · Landlocked Central Africa / Sahel · Capital: N'Djamena
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: N'Djamena — name means 'place of peace' in Arabic; formerly Fort-Lamy under French rule; at the confluence of the Chari and Logone rivers; forms a trans-border agglomeration with Kousseri (Cameroon); airport named for Hassan Djamous. (3)

Flag: very similar to Romania's (blue-yellow-red triband). (1)

Government: former French colony; Aozou Strip northern border with Libya was disputed in the Toyota War. (2)

Lake Chad

Lake Chad — namesake lake on the western border; fed by the Chari and Logone rivers; Sahel lake that has lost over 95% of its volume since the 1960s. (4)

Transaqua Scheme — proposed diversion from the Ubangi River to refill Lake Chad and irrigate the Sahara. (2)

Bogomerom Archipelago — islands in the lake; reached by a Roman expedition under Septimius Flaccus through Garamantes territory. (1)

Mountains & Desert

Tibesti Mountains — massive volcanic range in the northern Sahara; Emi Koussi is the highest peak; the Trou au Natron caldera; Soborom hot springs; Tarso Voon stratovolcano; inhabited by the Toubou people. (3)

Aozou Strip — disputed northern border with Libya; libya occupied this area until the Toyota War ruling; main town an oasis of the Toubou. (2)

Sahara Desert — covers most of the north. (1)

Bodélé Depression — endorheic dust source; supplies nutrients to the Amazon via Trans-Atlantic dust. (1)

Other Geography

Chari River — main southern river; tributaries include the Ouham River and Bahr Salamat; flows past Sarh. (2)

Zakouma National Park — biodiversity hotspot in the southeast. (1)

'Useful Chad' — southern part was nicknamed for its agricultural value under French rule. (1)

People

Sara people — largest ethnic group; namesake of the Moyen-Chari region's capital Sarh; practice the Yondo initiation ritual. (1)

Toumai hominid — early human skull (Sahelanthropus tchadensis) housed in the national museum. (1)

Chile 55
Republic of Chile · Southern South America (Pacific coast) · Capital: Santiago
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Santiago de Chile — home to the Moneda Palace, the presidential seat. (2)

Valparaíso — main port and congressional seat; second-largest city; home of Pablo Neruda's La Sebastiana house on Cerro Florida; Horcon Bay's wish-bridge; legendary New Year's fireworks. (3)

Shape & extent: the world's most elongated country; stretches 4,300 km north-south on the Pacific. (1)

Indigenous languages: Mapudungun (spoken by the Mapuche) and Rapa Nui (on Easter Island). (2)

Colonia Dignidad — infamous German enclave; German immigrants settled the Araucanía region. (1)

Historical conflicts: War of the Pacific captured Antofagasta from Bolivia, giving Chile its present northern coast. (1)

Atacama Desert

Atacama Desert — the driest non-polar desert on Earth; rain-shadow of the Andes; record sodium nitrate deposits; the Camanchaca rainless coastal fog; Mars-analog testing site. (4)

Chuquicamata — world's largest open-pit copper mine. (2)

Observatories: Paranal (Very Large Telescope) and La Silla sit on Atacama peaks; the world's clearest skies. (2)

El Tatio — world's third-largest geyser field, largest in the Southern Hemisphere. (1)

2010 Copiapó mining accident — 33 miners trapped and rescued. (1)

Pampa del Tamarugal — formerly forested area now devoid of vegetation. (1)

Loa River — Atacama's longest river and main water source. (2)

Andes & Volcanoes

Mount Aconcagua — highest peak in the Southern/Western Hemisphere; on the Chile–Argentina border. (3)

Ojos del Salado — world's tallest volcano; 2nd-tallest peak in the Americas; on the Argentine border south of the San Francisco Pass; contains the world's highest lake. (2)

Cordillera Domeyko — coastal mountain range in the north. (1)

Andes Mountains — form the entire eastern border with Argentina, Bolivia, and Peru. (2)

Patagonia & Far South

Patagonia — shared with Argentina; Antoine de Saint-Exupéry set Night Flight here; the Benetton Group controversially owns land; the Mapuche are the major indigenous people. (3)

Tierra del Fuego — archipelago at the southern tip; bounded by the Beagle Channel, Drake Passage, and Strait of Magellan; main town Ushuaia on the Argentine side; Isla Martillo penguin colony. (2)

Chiloé Island — separated from the mainland by the Chacao Channel; capital Castro. (1)

Diego Ramírez Islands — in the Drake Passage, the southernmost Chilean territory. (1)

Valdivia — site of the most intense earthquake ever recorded (1960, magnitude 9.5). (1)

Puerto Montt — southern city near several earthquake epicenters. (1)

Pacific Islands

Easter Island (Rapa Nui / Isla de Pascua) — Chilean possession; famous Moai statues built by the Rapa Nui people; capital Hanga Roa; Mataveri International Airport is the world's most remote airport; Maunga Terevaka highest point; the Rano Raraku volcano was a quarry; Motu Nui islet of the bird-man cult; rongorongo undeciphered script; toromiro tree nearly extinct. (4)

Juan Fernández Islands — contain Robinson Crusoe Island (where Alexander Selkirk was marooned) and Alejandro Selkirk Island. (3)

China 281
People's Republic of China · East Asia · Capital: Beijing
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Beijing — name means 'Northern Capital'. (4)

Largest city: Shanghai — world's busiest container port. (4)

Provinces & autonomous regions: 23 provinces, 5 autonomous regions (Xinjiang, Tibet, Inner Mongolia, Ningxia Hui, Guangxi Zhuang), 4 direct-controlled municipalities (Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, Chongqing), and 2 SARs (Hong Kong, Macau). (2)

Borders: more countries than any other (14, tied with Russia): Mongolia, Russia, North Korea, Vietnam, Laos, Myanmar, India, Bhutan, Nepal, Pakistan, Afghanistan (via the Wakhan Corridor), Tajikistan, Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan. (4)

Hu Line / Heihe–Tengchong Line — demographic divide; ~94% of China's population lives east of it. (1)

Shanghai Cooperation Organization — China-led security bloc with members Russia, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Tajikistan, Uzbekistan, India, Pakistan, Iran (joined 2023). (1)

Major Rivers

Yangtze River (Chang Jiang) — China's longest; flows from the Tanggula Mountains in Tibet through Yunnan (via Tiger Leaping Gorge as the Jinsha), past Wuhan, the Three Gorges Dam in Hubei, Nanjing, and Shanghai; receives Lake Poyang (the largest freshwater lake) and the Han River; host of the possibly-extinct baiji river dolphin. (6)

Yellow River (Huang He) — second-longest; named for its yellow silt; flows around the Ordos Plateau through the Loess Plateau; encounters the Wei River below Hua Mountain after Hukou Falls; empties into the Bo Hai Gulf via Shandong (since the last channel shift from Jiangsu); 'China's Sorrow' for its floods; Xia Dynasty allegedly founded along it. (6)

Pearl River (Zhu Jiang) — flows through the southern coastal regions to the South China Sea via the Pearl River Delta (Guangzhou-Shenzhen-Hong Kong-Macau). (3)

Amur River (Heilong Jiang / 'Black Dragon River') — forms much of the border with Russia; formed by the Shilka + Argun confluence; home to the kaluga sturgeon; runs along the Sikhote-Alin range; passes Heihe (China) and Blagoveshchensk (Russia). (5)

Mekong River — known as the Lancang in China; flows from Tibet through Yunnan as one of the Three Parallel Rivers (with the Salween and Jinsha). (2)

Major Mountains & Deserts

Mount Everest / Chomolungma — on the Nepal/Tibet border; world's highest peak. (4)

K2 / Mount Godwin-Austen — on the China–Pakistan border in the Karakoram; second-highest peak. (3)

Tibetan Plateau — 'Roof of the World'. (2)

Kunlun Mountains — divide the Tibetan Plateau from the Taklamakan/Tarim Basin. (2)

Tian Shan / Pamir — northwestern ranges; Pamirs touch the Wakhan Corridor. (2)

Altai Mountains — northwest, touching Mongolia, Russia, and Kazakhstan. (3)

Gobi Desert — shared with Mongolia; contains the Nemegt Basin ('Valley of the Dragons'), Khongoryn Els 'singing sands', Yadan National Geopark; bounded by the Altai (NW), Yin Mountains (E), Helan/Alashan (S); habitat of Bactrian camel and Przewalski's horse. (6)

Taklamakan Desert — 'place of ruins'; in the Tarim Basin of Xinjiang; home to Bronze Age Tarim mummies; Lop Nur lake; crossed by the planned Golmud–Korla railway. (3)

Iconic Sites

Great Wall of China — easternmost end at Old Dragon's Head where it meets the Bo Hai Sea; westernmost end at Jiayu Pass / Lintao; Juyongguan Pass is the most-visited section near Beijing; built across the Warring States and consolidated under Qin Shi Huang. (5)

Forbidden City — Ming/Qing imperial palace in Beijing; built by the Yongle Emperor; centered on the Hall of Supreme Harmony; razed and rebuilt several times after 1421 lightning strike and Li Zicheng's 1644 sacking. (4)

Spratly and Paracel Islands — disputed South China Sea archipelagos. (2)

Regional Files

Beijing — see `china_beijing.json`. (5)

Shanghai — see `china_shanghai.json`. (7)

Hong Kong SAR — see `china_hong_kong.json`. (5)

Macau SAR — see `china_macau.json`. (5)

Tibet Autonomous Region — see `china_tibet.json`. (3)

Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region — see `china_xinjiang.json`. (4)

Inner Mongolia — see `china_inner_mongolia.json`. (3)

Manchuria / Northeast (Dongbei) — Heilongjiang / Jilin / Liaoning — see `china_manchuria.json`. (4)

Guangdong & Pearl River Delta — Guangzhou, Shenzhen — see `china_guangdong.json`. (5)

Fujian — see `china_fujian.json`. (4)

Southwest China — Yunnan, Sichuan, Chongqing — see `china_southwest.json`. (5)

Shandong & Hainan — coastal provinces — see `china_coastal.json`. (4)

Colombia 44
Republic of Colombia · Northern South America · Capital: Bogotá
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Bogotá — former capital of the Viceroyalty of New Granada; world's highest capital north of the equator; La Candelaria historic quarter; served by El Dorado Airport; Museo del Oro has the world's largest collection of gold artifacts. (3)

Borders: Venezuela, Brazil, Peru, Ecuador, Panama; the only South American country with both Atlantic (Caribbean) and Pacific coastlines. (2)

Languages: Spanish dominant; the African-creole Palenquero language is spoken. (1)

Major Cities

Medellín — capital of Antioquia; in the Aburrá Valley on the Medellín River; HQ of the Pablo Escobar cartel. (3)

Cali — third-largest city; salsa capital. (1)

Cartagena de Indias — colonial walled city; Castillo San Felipe de Barajas with secret tunnels; Puerta del Reloj main gate; Bocagrande and Getsemaní districts; capital of Bolívar Department. (1)

Popayán — colonial 'white city'. (1)

Geography

Andes Mountains — Colombia is the most northerly Andean country. (3)

Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta — isolated coastal massif; together with the Paramillo Massif forms one of the world's most distant intervisible pairs. (1)

Magdalena River — major north-flowing river; Antioquia's Puerto Triunfo is home to invasive hippos (originally Escobar's private zoo). (2)

Guajira Peninsula — northernmost point of South America; ecotourism destination. (1)

San Andrés y Providencia — Colombian Caribbean islands. (1)

Yacopí region — global emerald mining center. (1)

Culture & History

Muisca Confederacy — pre-Columbian civilization conquered by Spain in the 16th century. (1)

Coffee — major export; Colombia is the world's #3 producer after Brazil and Vietnam. (2)

Marquetalia Republic — guerrilla independent zone that birthed the FARC. (1)

Macondo — fictional Gabriel García Márquez town; namesake of the BP Deepwater Horizon oil prospect. (1)

Colorado 67
'The Centennial State' · Mountain West · Capital: Denver
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Denver — 'Mile High City'; on the South Platte River; suburbs Aurora, Lakewood; Denver International Airport with ominous murals and the iconic 'Blue Mustang' (Blucifer) statue. (2)

Other cities: Colorado Springs (US Air Force Academy; Garden of the Gods), Boulder (CU), Fort Collins, Grand Junction (now BLM HQ). (1)

Geography

Rocky Mountains — cover much of the state; Mount Elbert is the highest peak in the Rockies; Pikes Peak ('America the Beautiful' inspiration); Mount Evans Road is the highest paved road in the US. (2)

Continental Divide — bisects the state along the Rockies. (1)

Source of major rivers: the Colorado (flows southwest to the Gulf of California), Rio Grande, Arkansas, and South Platte all rise here. (2)

Rocky Mountain National Park — north-central park. (1)

Black Canyon of the Gunnison National Park — dramatic narrow canyon in the west. (1)

Mesa Verde National Park — ancient Ancestral Puebloan cliff dwellings. (1)

Great Sand Dunes National Park — tallest dunes in North America; in the Sangre de Cristo Range. (1)

Heritage

Ludlow Massacre (1914) — striking coal miners and their families killed; major labor-history event. (1)

Comoros 11
Union of the Comoros · Indian Ocean (Mozambique Channel) · Capital: Moroni
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Moroni — on Grand Comore (Ngazidja). (1)

Three constituent islands: Ngazidja (Grande Comore), Mwali (Mohéli), and Nzwani (Anjouan); the fourth island Mahoré (Mayotte) voted to remain a French overseas department. (2)

Religion & status: the southernmost Muslim-majority country. (1)

Position: in the Mozambique Channel between Madagascar and Mozambique. (1)

Geography

Mount Karthala — active volcano on Grand Comore; alternating lava lakes and crater lakes; the Massif du Badjini is its southernmost extension. (1)

La Grille — second volcanic vent on Grand Comore. (1)

Mayotte (French) — administered separately; capital Mamoudzou on Grande-Terre; Petite-Terre holds the Dzaoudzi–Pamandzi airport; languages Shimaore and Bushi. (3)

Economy & Culture

Ylang-ylang — Comoros is the world's largest producer of this perfumery tree. (1)

Vanilla — major export, alongside Madagascar and Réunion. (1)

Msindanu — sandalwood-and-coral facial paste worn by Comorian women. (1)

Connecticut 15
'The Constitution State' · Northeast US · Capital: Hartford
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Hartford — home of Armsmear (Samuel Colt's estate), Dunkin' Donuts Park, and the XL Center; suburb Bristol is the home of ESPN. (1)

Other cities: Bridgeport (largest), New Haven (Yale University), Stamford, New London. (1)

Geography

Connecticut River — eponymous river runs north-south through the state. (2)

Long Island Sound — southern coast (separating from New York's Long Island). (1)

Mount Frissell — country's only state high point that is not the highest peak; the highest point in CT lies on its slope, but the actual summit is in Massachusetts. (1)

Heritage

Yale University — in New Haven; John W. Sterling & Dwight Hall libraries. (1)

Mystic Seaport — historic maritime village museum. (1)

Mashantucket Pequot Foxwoods & Mohegan Sun — major tribal casinos. (1)

Costa Rica 15
Republic of Costa Rica · Central America · Capital: San José
Central America

At a Glance

Capital: San José — transit system built by fruit magnate Minor Keith (United Fruit). (2)

'Pura vida' slogan — nicknamed the 'Switzerland of Central America'. (1)

No army — Costa Rica abolished its standing army in 1948 (commonly cited as 1954). (1)

International airport — main hub in Liberia (and SJO in the capital). (1)

Coasts & Peninsulas

West (Pacific) coast — the Nicoya Peninsula and the Osa Peninsula. (3)

East (Caribbean) coast — Limón Province has the country's largest Afro-Costa-Rican population. (2)

Cocos Island — Pacific island; supposedly where the stolen Treasure of Lima is buried; UNESCO World Heritage Site. (2)

Volcanoes, Parks & Wildlife

Arenal Volcano — active in the northwest; Lake Arenal is the country's largest lake; La Fortuna Waterfall nearby. (2)

Poás and Irazú volcanoes — caldera viewpoints. (1)

Corcovado National Park — old-growth rainforest on the Osa Peninsula; largest Pacific-coast old-growth in the Americas. (2)

Tortuguero National Park — Caribbean-coast park; the world's largest green sea turtle nesting beach. (2)

Monteverde Cloud Forest Reserve — protected by SINAC. (1)

Sierra de Talamanca — mountainous spine. (1)

Heritage & Curiosities

Diquís stone spheres — perfectly round pre-Columbian carved stones uncovered by United Fruit in the Diquís Valley. (1)

Costa Verde — resort with an elevated Boeing 727 restaurant. (1)

Tempisque River Bridge — connects mainland to the Nicoya Peninsula; funded in part by Taiwan. (1)

National football team — Los Ticos. (1)

Croatia 29
Republic of Croatia · Western Balkans / Adriatic · Capital: Zagreb
Balkans

At a Glance

Capital: Zagreb — northern continental capital on the Sava River. (1)

Four traditional regions: Slavonia (east), Istria (NW peninsula), Dalmatia (southern coast), and Central Croatia. (1)

Operation Storm (1995) — military offensive that retook the Lika region during the Croatian War of Independence. (1)

Islands: more than 1,000 administered; largest are Krk and Cres; party islands Pag and Hvar. (3)

Adriatic Sea — Croatia controls most of its eastern shore (split only by Bosnia's Neum strip). (2)

Coast & Islands

Dubrovnik — UNESCO walled coastal city; once the Republic of Ragusa; established a 16th-century trading colony at Fes; Pile Gate, Rector's Palace, Sponza Palace, Stradun main road, Onofrio Fountains; main cruise dock at Gruz; the Summer Festival starts on Luža Square. (3)

Dalmatia — historic region; longest river Cetina; Fortress of Klis separates Mosor and Kozjak mountains; Roman ruins of Salona. (2)

Pelješac Peninsula — bookended by Ston and Orebić; 2016 Chinese-built bridge. (1)

Krk Island — home of the igloo-like Church of St. Donat; site of a 16th-century martyrdom by Julian the Apostate. (1)

Diocletian's Palace — Roman emperor's retirement complex in Split. (1)

Istrian Peninsula — northwestern peninsula; the Motovun Forest is a popular source of white truffles. (2)

Inland Geography

Plitvice Lakes National Park — chain of 16 turquoise terraced lakes joined by waterfalls in a karst landscape. (2)

Dinaric Alps — mountain range traversing the interior. (1)

Sava River — flows through Zagreb to Belgrade; receives the Drina, Kupa, Una, and Vrbas from the south. (1)

Vuka River — flows through eastern Croatia. (1)

Danube River — forms part of the eastern border. (1)

Cuba 49
Republic of Cuba · Caribbean · Capital: Havana
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Havana — the iconic Malecón sea wall is the main tourist attraction; Granma newspaper is the state-run daily; the yacht Granma (Castro's landing boat) is displayed at the former presidential palace. (2)

Largest island in the Caribbean (after Cuba comes Hispaniola). (1)

Borders & relations: US embargoes; 90 miles south of Florida; Guantanamo Bay US lease pays a token check sent each year to the defunct 'Treasurer General' position. (2)

Geography

Sierra Maestra Mountains — southeastern range; Castro's revolutionary base; geological extension reaching the Cayman Islands. (2)

Nipe-Sagua-Baracoa Mountains — easternmost range in the Guantánamo Province area. (1)

Bay of Pigs (Bahía de los Cochinos) — site of the 1961 CIA-backed Brigade 2506 invasion landing at Playa Girón; east of the Zapata Peninsula in Matanzas Province; Brezhnev allegedly gifted Castro a yacht docked at the Cayo Piedra island. (2)

Cienfuegos — major southern port. (1)

Provinces & Cities

Granma Province — eastern province sharing its name with the state newspaper. (1)

Santiago de Cuba — second-largest city; in the southeast. (1)

Matanzas Province — central province containing the Bay of Pigs. (1)

Diaspora

Little Havana (Miami) — Cuban-American neighborhood; Calle Ocho Festival (world's longest conga line in 1988); José Martí Park; 'Walk of Fame' honors artists like Celia Cruz. (2)

Ybor City (Tampa) — historic Cuban-immigrant cigar-making quarter. (1)

Cyprus 13
Republic of Cyprus · Eastern Mediterranean island · Capital: Nicosia
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Nicosia — the world's last divided capital city; Venetian Walls, St. John's Cathedral; on the Pedieos River in the central Mesaoria Plain. (2)

Divided island — split between the Greek-Cypriot Republic of Cyprus (south) and the Turkish-occupied Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus since 1974. (2)

British Sovereign Base Areas — UK retains military bases at Akrotiri and Dhekelia. (2)

Famagusta — historic city setting of Shakespeare's Othello. (1)

Limassol — second-largest city; Trilogy Towers & The ONE skyscrapers; City of Dreams Mediterranean is the EU's largest integrated resort. (1)

Geography

Troodos Mountains — copper-rich central range; contains the UNESCO Kykkos Monastery and Mount Olympus (the Cypriot one, namesake of the Greek peak). (3)

Kyrenia Range / Pentadaktylos — northern coastal range. (1)

Mesaoria Plain — central plain stretching from Morphou Bay to Famagusta Bay. (1)

Karpas Peninsula — narrow easternmost projection. (1)

Akrotiri sand dunes — coastal dune system. (1)

Heritage

Copper — Cyprus is the world's namesake of the metal (Latin cuprum from Cyprium aes 'Cyprian ore'). (1)

Cinyras — mythical king of Cyprus slain by Apollo for a singing contest; namesake of the place. (1)

Czechia 29
Czech Republic · Central Europe · Capital: Prague
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Prague — on the Vltava River; largest Jewish cemetery in Europe; site of the medieval Astronomical Clock (6 centuries old). (4)

Historical regions: Bohemia (west), Moravia (east), and Czech Silesia (small northeastern strip). (1)

Languages: Czech is official; Vietnamese is recognized as a minority language (one of the few non-European such recognitions in Europe). (1)

Czech Legion — defended sections of the Trans-Siberian Railway under Kolchak in the Russian Civil War. (1)

Prague

Charles Bridge — medieval bridge across the Vltava lined with 30 statues; leads to Malá Strana. (4)

Old Town — begins at the dark Powder Tower; coronation route to Prague Castle; landmark Church of Our Lady before Týn (with the slightly mismatched Adam & Eve towers); Old-New Synagogue. (2)

Prague Castle complex — contains St. Vitus Cathedral and St. Wenceslas Chapel; centerpiece of the coronation route. (1)

Lennon Wall — site of Beatles-inspired graffiti. (1)

Petřín Hill — funicular to Strahov Stadium, the world's largest stadium. (1)

National Gallery — holds Alphonse Mucha's Slav Epic 20-canvas cycle. (1)

Other Cities

Brno — Moravia's capital; Villa Tugendhat (Mies van der Rohe / Lilly Reich); at the confluence of the Svitava and Svratka rivers. (1)

Geography

Elbe River — flows north into Germany; 2002 flood nearly damaged Raphael's Sistine Madonna at Dresden's Semper Gallery; receives the Mulde ('mill') and Vltava tributaries. (1)

Vltava — Prague's river; longest entirely within Czechia. (1)

Bohemian Forest / Šumava — mountain border with Bavaria; remnant of the ancient Hercynian Forest. (1)

Regen River — flows from Czechia into Bavaria. (1)

Côte d'Ivoire 6
République de Côte d'Ivoire · West Africa · Capitals: Yamoussoukro (de jure) / Abidjan (de facto)
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Two capitals: Yamoussoukro is the political capital (since 1983); Abidjan remains the economic capital and largest city. (2)

Basilica of Our Lady of Peace of Yamoussoukro — the world's largest church building by area; modeled on St. Peter's. (1)

Language: French is official; many indigenous languages including Akan, Senufo, Mande. (1)

Borders: Liberia and Guinea (W), Mali and Burkina Faso (N), Ghana (E), Atlantic Ocean (S). (1)

Economy & Geography

World's largest cocoa producer — produces ~40% of global cocoa. (1)

Coffee, palm oil, rubber, cashews — other major commodity exports. (1)

Mount Nimba — UNESCO Strict Nature Reserve on the borders with Guinea and Liberia. (1)

Abidjan lagoon system — Ébrié Lagoon hosts the port; bridges connect Plateau (CBD), Treichville and Cocody. (1)

Delaware 24
'The First State' · Mid-Atlantic · Capital: Dover
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Dover. (1)

Largest city: Wilmington. (1)

Three counties only: New Castle (north), Kent (middle), Sussex (south). (1)

History: first state to ratify the US Constitution (1787); was a Swedish and Dutch colony before England. (1)

Geography

Delaware River & Bay — eastern border; opens to the Atlantic. (2)

Bombay Hook National Wildlife Refuge — major waterfowl migration stop. (1)

Economy

DuPont Company — historic chemical industry HQ in Wilmington. (1)

Delhi NCT 9
National Capital Territory · Capital of India: New Delhi
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Status: Union Territory of New Delhi / Delhi — capital of India. (5)

Setting: Surrounded on three sides by the state of Haryana; part of the National Capital Region with suburbs such as Faridabad and Ghaziabad. (1)

River: Sits on the Yamuna River. (2)

Former capital: Was capital of the Mughal Empire; before becoming British India's capital, Kolkata served in that role. (2)

Landmarks

Red Fort — Mughal-era fortified palace in Old Delhi. (2)

Qutb Minar — minaret modelled on the Minaret of Jam; built by Iltutmish (whose tomb is also in the city). (3)

Tomb of Humayun — major Mughal-era mausoleum. (1)

Lotus Temple — Baha'i House of Worship, known for its flower-like shape. (2)

Parliament House — circular colonnaded structure housing the Lok Sabha and Rajya Sabha; on Raisina Hill beside Connaught Circus and the War Memorial Arch. (2)

Hyderabad House — state guest house; connected to Faridabad via Mathura Road / Grand Trunk Road. (1)

Modern Issues

Implemented a lockdown in 2021 due to severe air pollution. (1)

Denmark 45
Kingdom of Denmark · Scandinavia · Capital: Copenhagen
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Copenhagen — landmarks include the Nyhavn Canal, Amalienborg Palace, Frederik's Church, Tivoli Gardens, the CopenHill (Amager Bakke) ski-slope-on-a-waste-plant; Islands Brygge harbor baths. (2)

Composition: Denmark proper plus the autonomous Faroe Islands and Greenland form the Kingdom of Denmark. (2)

Hans Island dispute — settled 2022 split with Canada; tradition of leaving schnapps/whisky. (1)

Geography

Jutland Peninsula — Danish mainland; only land border (with Germany). (1)

Zealand & Funen — main Danish islands; Copenhagen sits on Zealand; Funen contains H.C. Andersen's birthplace Odense. (1)

Frisian Islands — Wadden Sea barrier islands shared with Germany and the Netherlands. (1)

Øresund Bridge — connects Copenhagen with Malmö, Sweden. (1)

Faroe Islands

Capital: Tórshavn on the largest island, Streymoy. (1)

Islands: Streymoy, Eysturoy, Vágar (with the airport served by Atlantic Airways). (1)

'Grindadráp' — traditional pilot whale hunt; the 2021 'Dolphin Hunt' slaughtered nearly 1,500 dolphins on Eysturoy. (1)

Shetland Islands — closest inhabited neighbors (Scottish). (1)

Greenland

Capital: Nuuk — largest city, on the southwestern coast. (1)

Largest island in the world (sovereign Denmark territory but not a country). (1)

Kalaallit Nunaat — Greenlandic name; Inuit Greenlanders are the Kalaallit people. (1)

Former Colonies

Danish West Indies — sold to the US in 1917 to become the US Virgin Islands; islands include St. Thomas, St. John, St. Croix; Charlotte Amalie is named for a Danish queen. (1)

Djibouti 19
Republic of Djibouti · Horn of Africa · Capital: Djibouti City
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Djibouti City — on the Gulf of Tadjoura. (2)

Strategic location: on the Bab-el-Mandeb Strait at the southern end of the Red Sea, controlling access to the Suez Canal. (3)

Military bases: Camp Lemonnier is the only permanent U.S. base in Africa; China's only Indian Ocean naval base is also here; Japan and France also maintain bases. (2)

Former name: French Territory of the Afars and Issas; renamed to suppress Somali nationalism. (1)

Population: majority Somali (Issa clan) and Afar. (1)

Geography

Lake Assal — 'Honey Lake'; world's most saline lake outside Antarctica; lowest point in Africa at over 500 ft below sea level; on the Arta/Tadjoura/Dikhil triple junction; salt harvested historically by the Issa clan. (3)

Lake Abbe — shared with Ethiopia; famous limestone chimneys. (1)

Afar Triangle / Depression — tectonic triple junction; lowest part of the East African Rift. (1)

Moussa Ali — highest peak; volcano on the Eritrean border. (1)

Ghoubbet-el-Kharab — saltwater cove separated from Lake Assal by the Ardoukoba volcano. (1)

Gulf of Tadjoura — Indian Ocean inlet that nearly bisects the country. (2)

Infrastructure & Borders

Bridge of the Horns — proposed Bab-el-Mandeb crossing to Yemen (unbuilt). (1)

Obock — northern port; site of planned Chinese naval base development. (1)

Borders: Eritrea (north), Ethiopia (west and south), Somalia/Somaliland (southeast). (1)

Dominica 9
Commonwealth of Dominica · Caribbean (Lesser Antilles) · Capital: Roseau
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Roseau. (1)

Position: Windward Islands of the Lesser Antilles; not to be confused with the Dominican Republic. (1)

Flag: green with yellow/black/white stripes and the endemic sisserou parrot at center; one of only two world flags with purple on it. (2)

Indigenous people: home to the last remaining population of Kalinago (Island Carib) in the Salybia / St. David Parish. (2)

Geography & Parks

Morne Trois Pitons National Park — sole UNESCO World Heritage Site; contains the Boiling Lake (world's second-largest hot spring) and Emerald Pool. (3)

Morne Diablotins — country's highest peak; habitat of the endemic red-necked amazon (jaco) parrot. (2)

Isulukati Waterfall — flows into the Crayfish River. (1)

Wildlife: also home to the giant ditch frog ('mountain chicken') shared with Montserrat. (1)

Dominican Republic 20
República Dominicana · Caribbean (Hispaniola) · Capital: Santo Domingo
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Santo Domingo — first permanent European settlement in the Americas (1496); on the Ozama River. (1)

Shares the island of Hispaniola with Haiti (east of the Mona Passage from Puerto Rico). (5)

Larger Spanish-speaking population than Haiti; bigger and more eastern of the two countries on Hispaniola. (2)

Geography

Pico Duarte — highest peak in the Caribbean; in the Cordillera Central range. (2)

Lake Enriquillo — world's largest population of American crocodiles; covers a depression shared with Haiti's Étang Saumâtre; near the Neiba Mountains in Independencia Province; the Las Caritas national park offers views. (3)

Samaná Peninsula — separated from the mainland by the Gulf of Arrows (named by Columbus). (1)

Hispaniola interior: Cordillera Central crosses the country. (1)

La Isabela (Puerto Plata Province) — site of the first Spanish settlement in the New World. (1)

Cities & Tourism

Santiago de los Caballeros — second city; in the Cibao region. (1)

Punta Cana — major resort town in La Altagracia Province (governed from Higüey); first privately owned international airport (palm-frond roof); daytrips to Saona and Catalina islands. (2)

Pomier Caves — extensive Taíno rock art (~6,000 drawings). (1)

Moca — capital of Espaillat Province. (1)

DR Congo 34
Formerly Zaire · Central Africa · Capital: Kinshasa
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Kinshasa — largest French-speaking city in the world (surpassing Paris); street children are called shegues; Matadi is the main seaport on the Congo, some 90 mi inland; Lingala is the lingua franca. (2)

Second-largest African country by area (after Algeria). (1)

Capital change: Lubumbashi was capital of the former Katanga Province until 2015. (1)

Mining & Economy

World's largest tantalum & niobium reserves; cobalt capital of the world; major copper producer. (1)

Kisanfu mine — one of the world's largest cobalt deposits; east of Kolwezi in Lualaba Province. (1)

Copperbelt — straddles the border with Zambia; runs through Katanga Province. (2)

Gécamines — state-run mining company headquartered in Katanga. (1)

Geography

Congo River — second-longest in Africa; most powerful in flow; passes Kinshasa-Brazzaville; receives the Ubangi, Kasai, and Lualaba; final flow plunges through Inga Falls. (2)

Boyoma Falls — series of seven cataracts upstream of Kisangani (capital of Tshopo Province, formerly Orientale Province). (1)

Lake Tanganyika — forms the eastern border (shared with Tanzania, Burundi, Zambia); the Lukuga River drains it back into the Congo. (2)

Lake Kivu — northern part of the eastern border (with Rwanda); CO₂-saturated 'killer lake' that could experience limnic eruptions; largest island Idjwi; ports Goma and Bukavu; drains via the Ruzizi into Lake Tanganyika. (2)

Lake Albert — northern part of the eastern border (with Uganda); receives the Semliki; emits the White Nile via Lake Kyoga. (1)

Lake Mweru — southeastern border lake with Zambia. (1)

Rwenzori Mountains — 'Mountains of the Moon' on the Uganda border; contains Mount Stanley with Margherita Peak. (1)

Virunga Mountains — volcanic range on the Rwanda/Uganda border; Mount Nyiragongo (an active lava lake) and Mount Nyamuragira. (1)

Equator — gives its name to the northern Équateur Province. (1)

East Timor 3
Timor-Leste · Maritime Southeast Asia · Capital: Dili
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Dili — site of the Cristo Rei statue at Cape Fatucama (by Mochamad Syaiful 'Bolli'); Motael Church was central to the 1999 INTERFET-deployed wave of violence. (1)

Independence: restored sovereignty from Indonesia in 2002 after the 1999 UN-supervised referendum. (1)

Joined ASEAN in 2022 (admitted as the 11th member). (1)

Geography

Mount Ramelau (Tatamailau) — highest peak; most of the country's rainfall hits this range. (1)

Oecusse Ambeno — exclave on the Indonesian (West Timor) coast; Baikeno-speaking sandalwood forest area. (1)

Languages: Tetum and Portuguese are official; Indonesian and English are working languages. (1)

Arafura Sea — bounds the south coast. (1)

Ecuador 31
Republic of Ecuador · Northwestern South America · Capital: Quito
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Quito — divided into 32 cabildos; in the basin of the Guayllabamba River; connected to Cruz Loma by the Teleférico gondola; presidential Carondelet Palace; Mitad del Mundo equator monument; the Church of the Company of Jesus anchors the historic Road of the Seven Crosses. (4)

Currency: uses the US dollar as legal tender (since 2000, replacing the sucre). (1)

Equator runs through the country and gives it its name. (1)

Cities

Santiago de Guayaquil — largest city; on the Guayas River (formed by the Daule + Babahoyo confluence) at the Gulf of Guayaquil; contains Estadio Monumental Banco Pichincha; Urdesa neighborhood; site of 1822 meeting between Bolívar and San Martín. (3)

Cuenca — UNESCO-listed colonial highland city. (1)

Andes & Volcanoes

Mount Chimborazo — highest peak in Ecuador; the world's farthest point from Earth's center (due to equatorial bulge); summited 1880 by Edward Whymper; merchants called hieleros harvest its ice; the Bolívar Province is named for it. (3)

Cotopaxi — iconic snow-capped active volcano south of Quito; one of the world's highest active volcanoes. (1)

Pichincha — stratovolcano overlooking Quito. (1)

Galápagos Islands

Galápagos archipelago — Ecuadorian province; site of Charles Darwin's Voyage of the Beagle observations; the largest volcano is on Fernandina Island; largest island is Isabela; sits atop the Cocos Ridge at the Nazca/Cocos plate junction. (3)

Pinta Island Tortoise — 'Lonesome George' was the last of his subspecies; died 2012. (2)

Other islands: Baltra (South Seymour), San Cristóbal, Santa Cruz. (1)

MV Jessica — oil-tanker crash caused major 2001 ecological damage. (1)

Endemic wildlife: only home of the flightless cormorant and marine iguana. (1)

Egypt 75
Arab Republic of Egypt · North Africa / Middle East · Capital: Cairo
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Cairo — largest city in Africa; Gezira Island in the Nile; Al-Azhar Mosque with the Gate of the Barbers; Hanging Church; zabbaleen informal garbage collectors. (3)

Alexandria — Mediterranean port founded by Alexander the Great; once home to the Pharos Lighthouse (Wonder of the Ancient World, on Pharos Island; later rebuilt as the Citadel of Qaitbay); Great Library built by Ptolemy I; Coptic patriarchy. (4)

Government: capital relocation planned to the New Administrative Capital east of Cairo. (1)

The Nile

Nile River — world's longest river; Blue Nile (from Ethiopia's Lake Tana) and White Nile (from the African Great Lakes via the Sudd swamp) meet at Khartoum; the river's flooding sustained ancient Egypt. (3)

Aswan High Dam — Soviet-supported dam designed in part by Austrian architect Walter Jurecka; created Lake Nasser; required relocation of Abu Simbel and Philae temples; displaced the Hungarian-descended Magyarab people. (2)

Lake Nasser — vast reservoir behind the High Dam; Wadi Halfa lies on it; the Toshka Lakes were created by the Mubarak/Sadat canal diversion. (2)

Nile Delta — fan-shaped river mouth on the Mediterranean; ancient grain breadbasket. (1)

Pyramids & Monuments

Pyramids of Giza — built for Khufu, Khafre, and Menkaure; near the Great Sphinx. (2)

Step Pyramid of Djoser at Saqqara — first pyramid, designed by Imhotep; evolved from the mastaba. (1)

Valley of the Kings — royal necropolis near Luxor (ancient Thebes). (1)

Abu Simbel — Ramses II rock temples relocated above Lake Nasser. (1)

Geography

Sahara Desert — covers most of Egypt; includes the Western Desert (with the Qattara Depression and Siwa Oasis) and the Eastern Desert (along the Red Sea). (1)

Sinai Peninsula — connects Africa to Asia; site of Mount Sinai (Jabal Musa) and St. Catherine's Monastery. (1)

Suez Canal — 1869 Lesseps canal connecting the Mediterranean to the Red Sea through Port Said and Suez; 2021 Ever Given grounding closed it for 6 days. (1)

Red Sea coast — resorts at Hurghada and Sharm el-Sheikh. (1)

El Salvador 13
Republic of El Salvador · Central America · Capital: San Salvador
Central America

At a Glance

Capital: San Salvador — Plaza of the Savior of the World with the Salvador del Mundo monument; St. Óscar Romero was the canonized archbishop. (1)

Smallest country on the North American continental mainland. (1)

Only Central American country without a Caribbean coast — Pacific-only coastline. (2)

Calling code: 503 — used by gangs as a tag, along with the devil-horns hand sign. (1)

1969 'Football War' — fought with Honduras after a World Cup qualifier. (1)

Currency: uses the US dollar since 2001 (replaced the colón). (1)

Volcanoes & Lakes

Izalco volcano — 'Lighthouse of the Pacific'; in the Cordillera de Apaneca; featured on the old 10-colón note. (1)

Santa Ana volcano (Ilamatepec) — country's highest stratovolcano; 2005 eruption. (1)

Lake Ilopango & Lake Coatepeque — caldera lakes; Lake Güija is shared with Guatemala. (1)

Cerro El Pital — highest peak (cloud forest). (1)

Cities & Coast

San Miguel & Santa Ana — major cities. (1)

El Sunzal — Pacific surfing hotspot. (1)

Gulf of Fonseca — shared with Honduras and Nicaragua; Meanguera island awarded to El Salvador (Honduras got El Tigre). (1)

Pupusa — national stuffed-corn-tortilla dish. (1)

Equatorial Guinea 11
Republic of Equatorial Guinea · Central Africa · Capital: Malabo (current) / Ciudad de la Paz (planned)
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Current capital: Malabo — on Bioko island. (1)

Planned new capital: Ciudad de la Paz / Djibloho (formerly Oyala) — being built on the mainland; connected by highway to the Mengomeyén airport (President Obiang's birthplace). (2)

Only Spanish-speaking sovereign country in Africa — Spanish is one of three official languages (with French and Portuguese). (2)

Government: ruled since 1979 by Teodoro Obiang. (1)

Oil wealth & OPEC — joined OPEC in 2017; one of OPEC's few sub-Saharan members. (2)

Geography & Islands

Río Muni (Mbini) — mainland region; chief city the port of Bata. (2)

Bioko — main island in the Gulf of Guinea (offshore from Cameroon); contains Malabo; named for the Portuguese explorer Fernão do Pó; the Fernandino creole people are named for him; popular beaches and the indigenous Ndowe ('Beach People'). (3)

Annobón — small southern island in the Gulf of Guinea. (1)

Corisco — small island; home of the intermarried Kombe and Benga peoples. (1)

Eritrea 7
State of Eritrea · Horn of Africa · Capital: Asmara
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Asmara — at the top of the Pendice Orientale escarpment; founded by the merger of the Shelele, Sherenser, and Gurtom tribes; name means 'the four women made them unite' in Tigrinya; UNESCO World Heritage for its modernist Italian architecture. (1)

Independence: seceded from Ethiopia in 1993; war with Ethiopia (1998-2000); made Ethiopia landlocked. (1)

Languages: Tigrinya, Arabic, English; nine recognized ethnic languages. (1)

Government: one-party state under Isaias Afwerki. (1)

Geography

Red Sea coast — major Eritrean coastline; gives Ethiopia no sea access. (1)

Dahlak Archipelago — Red Sea island group with diving sites. (1)

Danakil / Afar Depression — northern extension shared with Ethiopia and Djibouti; one of the hottest places on earth. (1)

Massawa — historic Red Sea port. (1)

Borders: Sudan (west), Ethiopia (south), Djibouti (southeast), Red Sea (east). (1)

Den Den Camp — former liberation-front mountain stronghold. (1)

Estonia 18
Republic of Estonia · Baltic state · Capital: Tallinn
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Tallinn — medieval Old Town; Toompea Castle (parliament); Alexander Nevsky Cathedral; on the Gulf of Finland; the Pirita River flows through; Song Festival Grounds. (2)

NATO Cooperative Cyber Defence Centre of Excellence — Tallinn houses the alliance's cyber-defence hub; namesake Tallinn Manual on cyberwarfare law. (1)

Language: Finno-Ugric Estonian, related to Finnish. (1)

Cities

Tartu — second-largest city; on the Emajõgi River between Lake Võrtsjärv and Lake Peipus; Gunpowder Cellar pub; 'Kissing Students' Fountain; conquered by Russia in 1538. (1)

Geography

Lake Peipus — large border lake shared with Russia; Lake Lämmi connects it to its southern Lake Pihkva. (3)

Väinameri (Moonsund) — separates the mainland coast (Virtsu, Haapsalu) from the western archipelago. (1)

Saaremaa — largest island; Sõrve Peninsula in the south facing the Irbe Strait; Kaali craters from a Bronze Age meteorite strike; Kuressaare Episcopal Castle. (1)

Hiiumaa — second-largest island. (1)

Baltic Sea — Estonia sits on the eastern shore; arms include the Gulf of Finland and the Gulf of Riga. (3)

Eswatini 5
Kingdom of Eswatini (formerly Swaziland) · Southern Africa · Capitals: Mbabane (administrative) / Lobamba (royal)
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capitals: Mbabane (administrative) and Lobamba (royal/legislative). (2)

Name change: renamed from Swaziland to eSwatini in 2018 for the country's 50th independence anniversary; lawyer Darren Olivier estimated the change cost ~$6M. (1)

Monarchy: ruled by Mswati III ('the lion-king') alongside the Ndlovukati (queen mother, 'She-Elephant'); his father Sobhuza II designed the flag (black-and-white shield, staff and two spears). (2)

One of the last absolute monarchies in the world. (1)

Geography & Parks

Borders: entirely landlocked between South Africa (north/west/south) and Mozambique (east). (1)

Hlane Royal National Park — major wildlife reserve. (2)

Drakensberg-related uplands — high western highveld; sloping eastern lowveld. (1)

Ethiopia 55
Federal Democratic Republic of Ethiopia · Horn of Africa · Capital: Addis Ababa
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Addis Ababa — name means 'new flower' (alternate name Finfinne means 'natural spring'); on the slopes of Mount Entoto; only mainland sub-Saharan light-rail; Holy Trinity Cathedral (Kidist Selassie); HQ of the African Union. (4)

Population: the world's most populous landlocked country (~120 million); second-most populous African country. (3)

Independence: the only African country that was never colonized (except the 1936-41 Italian occupation). (1)

Languages: Amharic is the working language; Tigrinya, Oromo, and many others are widely spoken. (1)

Tigray War (2020-22) — civil war between the federal government and the Tigray People's Liberation Front. (1)

Geography

Simien Mountains — northern range with Ras Dashen, the country's highest peak; home to the Ethiopian wolf. (2)

Bale Mountains — southeastern highlands. (1)

Great Rift Valley — splits the country diagonally; contains a string of lakes (Awasa, Langano, Abijatta, etc.). (1)

Danakil / Afar Depression — one of the hottest, lowest, most volcanic places on Earth; contains the abandoned Dallol salt town (hottest annual average) and Erta Ale lava-lake volcano; site of Lucy and Gawis cranium fossils. (2)

Lake Tana — Ethiopia's largest lake; source of the Blue Nile; near Bahir Dar. (2)

Lake Turkana — shared with Kenya (the 'Jade Sea'); fed by Ethiopia's Omo River; the Gibe III Dam threatens its water level. (1)

Lake Abbe — shared with Djibouti; in the Afar Triangle. (1)

Heritage

Aksum / Axum — ancient empire and city; obelisks; claimed home of the Ark of the Covenant. (1)

Lalibela — town of 11 rock-hewn UNESCO churches; Bete Giyorgis (church of St. George) is the most famous. (1)

Ethiopian Orthodox Tewahedo Church — largest Oriental Orthodox church. (1)

People & Culture

Oromo — largest ethnic group; concentrated in the Oromia Region that surrounds Addis Ababa as an enclave. (1)

Amhara, Tigray, Somali, Gurage — major ethnic groups. (1)

Gursha — traditional act of feeding food to another person with one's own hands as a sign of love. (1)

Cuisine: injera flatbread; doro wat chicken stew. (1)

Federated States of Micronesia 10
FSM · Pacific Ocean (Caroline Islands) · Capital: Palikir
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Palikir — on Pohnpei island. (1)

Four states: Yap, Chuuk (formerly Truk), Pohnpei, and Kosrae. (1)

Position: spans ~1,700 mi of the Caroline Islands northeast of New Guinea. (2)

Status: in Compact of Free Association with the United States. (1)

Notable Sites

Yap — famous for giant Rai stone money discs. (1)

Chuuk Lagoon — WWII Japanese naval base; iconic dive site full of warship wrecks. (1)

Pohnpei — wettest place in Micronesia; site of the Nan Madol UNESCO ruined city. (1)

Pingelap Atoll — ~5% of inhabitants have the rare visual disorder achromatopsia ('island of the colorblind'). (1)

Weno — largest city, on Chuuk. (1)

Fiji 18
Republic of Fiji · Melanesia (South Pacific) · Capital: Suva
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Suva — on the Laucala Bay in Viti Levu. (1)

Population: mixed Melanesian native Fijians (iTaukei) and a large Indo-Fijian community descended from indentured laborers. (2)

Languages: Fijian, Fiji Hindi, and English are all official. (1)

Flag debate: PM Frank Bainimarama announced a 2015 competition to drop the British Union Jack from the flag. (1)

Geography

Two main islands: Viti Levu (largest, contains Suva) and Vanua Levu (second-largest); separated by the Bligh Water. (3)

Koro Sea — between the main islands and the eastern Lau Archipelago. (2)

Mount Tomanivi — highest peak, on Viti Levu. (1)

Great Astrolabe Reef — world's fourth-largest barrier reef; surrounds Kadavu island. (1)

Taveuni — third-largest island; contains Lake Tagimaucia; nearby Qamea and Matagi islands are home to the Rainbow and Vuna Reefs. (1)

Mamanuca & Yasawa — popular tourist archipelagoes. (1)

Rotuma — northernmost island; discovered by the Pandora searching for Bounty mutineers. (1)

History & Culture

Ratu Udre Udre — listed in Guinness as the most prolific cannibal in history (~872 victims). (2)

'Fiji mermaid' — fake creature exhibited by P.T. Barnum. (1)

Finland 31
Republic of Finland · Nordic country · Capital: Helsinki
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Helsinki — on the Gulf of Finland; built around the harbor of Suomenlinna sea fortress (UNESCO). (1)

Language: Finnish is a Uralic (Finno-Ugric) language related to Estonian; Swedish is also official. (1)

NATO: joined NATO in 2023 following the Russian invasion of Ukraine. (1)

Geography

'Land of a Thousand Lakes' — actually ~188,000 lakes. (1)

Lake Saimaa — Finland's largest lake; home to ~300 endemic ringed seals; connected to Lake Ladoga (Russia) by the Vuoksi River. (2)

Lapland — northernmost region; capital Rovaniemi (Santa Village just south of the Arctic Circle); the town of Kemi builds the world's largest snow fort; lost ocean access when Petsamo was ceded to the USSR. (2)

Karelia — most was ceded to the USSR after the 1939-44 wars; the Karelian Isthmus lost to Russia. (2)

Gulf of Bothnia — northern arm of the Baltic, between Finland and Sweden; Kvarken Archipelago continues to rise from post-glacial rebound. (2)

Åland Islands — Swedish-speaking autonomous archipelago in the Baltic. (2)

Cities & Culture

Turku — historic old capital on the Aura River; Sibelius Museum. (1)

Tampere — third-largest city; industrial hub. (1)

Reijo Kela's 1,000 scarecrows — landscape art along Highway 5. (1)

Florida 66
'The Sunshine State' · Southeast US (peninsula) · Capital: Tallahassee
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Tallahassee — northern panhandle capital. (1)

Largest city: Jacksonville (largest US city by area in the lower 48). (1)

Major metros: Miami (Little Havana, Calle Ocho), Orlando (Walt Disney World), Tampa (Tampa Bay), St. Petersburg, Fort Lauderdale, Hialeah. (1)

Geography

Everglades National Park — vast sub-tropical wetland; 'River of Grass' that abuts Lake Okeechobee; outlaw Ed Watson hid in the settlement of Chokoloskee. (2)

Lake Okeechobee — large central lake; the heart of the Everglades watershed. (1)

Florida Keys — coral-island chain extending southwest from the mainland; Key West is the southernmost US city in the continental US. (1)

Tampa Bay — major Gulf coast bay; receives the Manatee River; Sunshine Skyway Bridge (1980 Summit Venture collision); Ybor City Cuban district; St. Petersburg. (2)

Sugarloaf Mountain — highest peak in peninsular Florida; shares name with peaks in Maine and Rio. (1)

Apalachicola River — flows through the Panhandle to the Emerald Coast. (1)

Theme Parks & Tourism

Walt Disney World Resort (Orlando) — largest amusement-park complex in the world. (1)

Universal Orlando Resort — second-largest theme-park complex. (1)

Kennedy Space Center — at Cape Canaveral on Merritt Island; the Vehicle Assembly Building is the tallest one-story building in the US. (1)

Heritage

St. Augustine — oldest continuously inhabited European-founded city in the US (1565). (1)

Calle Ocho Festival — annual Cuban-American festival in Miami's Little Havana. (1)

France 126
French Republic · Western Europe · Capital: Paris
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Paris — on the Seine with islands Île de la Cité and Île Saint-Louis; landmarks Eiffel Tower, Louvre, Notre-Dame, Arc de Triomphe, Sacré-Cœur on Montmartre. (6)

18 regions — 13 in metropolitan France plus 5 overseas (Guadeloupe, Martinique, French Guiana, Réunion, Mayotte). (1)

Metropolitan Regions

Occitanie — Mediterranean-Pyrenees region; Béziers on the Canal du Midi; Pont du Gard Roman aqueduct; cities include Toulouse and Montpellier. (1)

Île-de-France — Paris metro region. (1)

Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur — Mediterranean; Marseille is France's second city; Nice, Avignon. (1)

Auvergne-Rhône-Alpes — Lyon, Grenoble, Mont Blanc; the Rhône River. (1)

Bourgogne (Burgundy) — wine country; Dijon. (1)

Bretagne (Brittany) — Celtic peninsula; Mont Saint-Michel on the Normandy border. (1)

Normandy — D-Day beaches (Omaha, Utah, Sword, Juno, Gold). (1)

Hauts-de-France — Nord department; capital Lille ('Capital of Flanders'); the Calais 'Jungle' refugee camp. (1)

Alsace — German-influenced eastern region; Strasbourg seat of the European Parliament. (1)

Corsica — Mediterranean island; birthplace of Napoleon. (1)

Rivers & Mountains

Seine — flows through Paris to the English Channel at Le Havre. (2)

Loire — longest river entirely in France; châteaux country. (1)

Rhône — flows from Lake Geneva through Lyon to the Mediterranean delta (Camargue). (1)

Garonne — flows through Bordeaux and into the Gironde estuary. (1)

Pyrenees — border range with Spain. (1)

Alps — eastern Alps; Mont Blanc highest peak in Western Europe. (2)

Massif Central — central highlands and extinct volcanoes. (1)

Overseas France

French Guiana — Amazon basin department on South American mainland; Kourou spaceport. (4)

Guadeloupe & Martinique — Caribbean departments; Mount Pelée in Martinique destroyed Saint-Pierre in 1902. (1)

Réunion — Indian Ocean; Piton des Neiges and Piton de la Fournaise volcanoes; coral reef from Saint-Leu to Saint-Gilles. (1)

Mayotte — Comoros archipelago; Mamoudzou capital. (1)

Saint Pierre and Miquelon — North Atlantic; creates a notch in Canada's EEZ. (2)

French Polynesia — overseas collectivity; Tahiti, Bora Bora (Society Islands), the Marquesas (including Hiva Oa), Tuamotu atolls. (2)

Wallis and Futuna — Hoorn Islands divided into the Kingdoms of Alo and Singave. (1)

New Caledonia — Melanesia; copper-rich; independence referendums. (1)

Peoples & Heritage

Basque Country — straddles the western Pyrenees; Euskara is non-Indo-European; tricolor red-white-green flag. (1)

Carcassonne — UNESCO walled medieval city. (1)

Cuisine: baguette, cheese, wine — Bordeaux, Burgundy, Champagne, Loire wine regions. (1)

Coastal province across from Taiwan · Capital: Fuzhou
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Fuzhou. (1)

Largest city: Xiamen (Amoy) — major port and one of China's four original Special Economic Zones. (2)

Hokkien-speaking diaspora hub — major historical source of Chinese emigration to Southeast Asia. (1)
