Gabon 8
Gabonese Republic · Central Africa (Gulf of Guinea) · Capital: Libreville
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Libreville. (1)

Religion: indigenous Bwiti faith uses the iboga shrub root in open-sided mbandja temples. (1)

Geography

Ogooué River — main river; discovered by Mary Kingsley; rises in the Batéké Plateau; flows past Franceville, Ndjolé, Lambaréné, Port-Gentil; receives the Ngounié and Ivindo tributaries; empties into the Gulf of Guinea via the Nkomi Lagoon. (3)

Loango National Park — National Geographic dubbed it 'Africa's Last Eden'; famous for surfing hippos. (2)

Ivindo National Park — features the Kongou Falls. (1)

Crystal Mountains — coastal range in the north. (1)

Cape Lopez — westernmost point of the African continent, near Port-Gentil. (1)

Mining & Heritage

Oklo natural nuclear reactor — uranium deposits in the Mounana area created the only known natural nuclear fission reactor (~2 billion years ago). (2)

Lambaréné — site of Albert Schweitzer's hospital on the Ogooué. (1)

Gambia 14
The Republic of the Gambia · West Africa (Atlantic) · Capital: Banjul
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Banjul — on St. Mary's Island at the mouth of the Gambia River; formerly known as Bathurst under British rule; leased from the King of Kombi in 1651; landmarks Albert Market and Arch 22 (commemorating Yahya Jammeh's 1994 coup); Denton Bridge; Tanbi Wetland Complex to the southwest. (4)

Shape: narrow country wrapping around the lower Gambia River, almost completely surrounded by Senegal. (1)

Independence: from Britain in 1965; the only mainland African country to have been a British colony surrounded by French ones. (1)

Gambia River

Gambia River — namesake river; rises in the Fouta Djallon highlands (Guinea); only permanent crossing connects Farafenni and Soma. (4)

Kunta Kinteh Island (formerly St. Andrew's / James Island) — former slave-trading hub renamed by Yahya Jammeh for Roots protagonist Kunta Kinte; Fort James ruins. (4)

Juffure — town visited in Alex Haley's memoir Roots. (1)

Wassu & Wanar stone circles — megalithic UNESCO sites. (1)

Georgia 74
Georgia (Sakartvelo) · South Caucasus / Transcaucasia · Capital: Tbilisi
Caucasus

At a Glance

Capital: Tbilisi — old town and sulphur baths. (1)

Government: former Soviet republic; toppled the Eduard Shevardnadze government in the 2003 Rose Revolution. (1)

Borders: Russia (north), Azerbaijan (east/southeast), Armenia (south), Turkey (southwest), Black Sea (west). (1)

Language: Georgian uses a unique Kartvelian script. (1)

Cities

Batumi — capital of Adjara; resort town on the Black Sea; nicknamed 'Las Vegas of the Black Sea'; Alphabetic Tower in DNA-helix shape honors the Kartvelian script; where Joseph Stalin organized labor strikes. (1)

Sukhumi — capital of the breakaway Abkhazia region. (1)

Gori — birthplace of Joseph Stalin. (1)

Breakaway Regions

Abkhazia — northwestern breakaway region on the Black Sea; flag is a red canton with a white hand and seven green/white stripes; Lake Rista held a Stalin summer home; Veryovkina Cave is the world's deepest cave. (2)

South Ossetia — northern breakaway region recognized only by Russia and a few allies after the 2008 war. (2)

Geography

Caucasus Mountains — northern border with Russia; contains some of Europe's highest peaks. (1)

Khevsur people — semi-pagan highlanders. (1)

Culture

Wine — birthplace of viticulture; 8,000-year-old qvevri tradition. (1)

Georgia (US) 57
'The Peach State' · South Atlantic · Capital: Atlanta
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Atlanta — largest city; home of CNN, Coca-Cola HQ, Hartsfield-Jackson (world's busiest airport); Peachtree Center; Centennial Olympic Park (1996 Olympics bombing site under Eric Robert Rudolph); represented in Congress by civil-rights leader John Lewis. (2)

Other cities: Savannah (historic colonial port), Augusta (Masters Tournament), Columbus, Athens (UGA). (1)

Geography

Golden Isles — Atlantic barrier-island chain that includes St. Simons Island near Brunswick. (2)

Okefenokee Swamp — UNESCO-considered peat-bog swamp on the Florida border; one of America's primary examples of a swamp ecosystem. (1)

Stone Mountain — Confederate-bas-relief monolith east of Atlanta. (1)

Appalachian Mountains — northern Blue Ridge; Brasstown Bald is the highest peak. (1)

Chattahoochee River — flows through Atlanta; forms part of the western border with Alabama. (1)

Savannah River — forms the eastern border with South Carolina. (1)

Heritage

Worcester v. Georgia (1832) — Supreme Court case over Cherokee tribal lands. (1)

Oglethorpe Barracks — colonial-era fort in Savannah. (1)

Martin Luther King Jr. — born in Atlanta; King Center. (1)

Germany 87
Federal Republic of Germany · Central Europe · Capital: Berlin
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Berlin — reunified capital since 1990; Brandenburg Gate, Reichstag with the Norman Foster glass dome, Holocaust Memorial, Berlin Wall remnants at East Side Gallery. (4)

**16 federal states (Bundesländer) — including city-states Berlin, Hamburg, Bremen**. (1)

Major Cities

Hamburg — second city; major North Sea port on the Elbe; Speicherstadt warehouse district. (2)

Munich — Bavarian capital; Oktoberfest; Marienplatz; BMW HQ. (2)

Frankfurt am Main — financial capital; Cathedral of St. Bartholomew; ECB HQ; on the Main River in Hesse. (1)

Cologne (Köln) — Gothic cathedral; on the Rhine. (1)

Dresden — Saxon capital; Semper Gallery (almost flooded in 2002 Elbe disaster); historic Frauenkirche. (1)

Rivers & Mountains

Rhine River — flows from Switzerland past Cologne and Düsseldorf to the Netherlands; the Lorelei Rock legendarily lured sailors; tributaries Neckar, Main, Moselle, Ruhr. (3)

Danube River — rises in the Black Forest; flows east through Bavaria to Austria. (2)

Elbe River — flows from Czechia through Saxony to Hamburg. (2)

Black Forest — wooded highland in Baden-Württemberg; source of the Danube; Feldberg highest peak; Cego/Bourgeois Tarot card-playing origin. (2)

Bavarian Alps — south of Munich; Zugspitze is Germany's highest peak; Neuschwanstein Castle. (2)

Harz Mountains — central; Brocken peak (Walpurgisnacht). (1)

Regions & Heritage

Bavaria — largest state; Munich capital; conservative Catholic heartland; Rothenburg ob der Tauber touristy town; Nuremberg trial city. (1)

Saxony — eastern state with Dresden; site of the Sistine Madonna at the Semper Gallery. (1)

Ruhr Valley — industrial Rhine-Westphalian heartland. (1)

Frisian Islands — Wadden Sea barrier islands shared with the Netherlands and Denmark; Heligoland (former British colony; where the national anthem was written). (1)

Reunification — East and West Germany merged 1990 after the Fall of the Berlin Wall. (1)

Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Accra. (1)

Former name: Gold Coast under British rule. (2)

'Jollof Wars' — friendly rivalry over jollof rice with Nigeria, Cameroon, and Senegal. (1)

Geography

Lake Bosumtwi — Ghana's only natural lake; in an impact crater. (1)

Cities & Heritage

Balkans

At a Glance

Macedonia (Greek region) — northern Greece; the town of Vergina is near ancient Aigai; Pella was capital of Alexander's kingdom; gives its name to the country to the north (now North Macedonia). (1)

Mountains & Mainland

Mount Olympus — highest peak; home of the Olympian gods; highest peak Mytikas; Chapel of the Prophet Elias is the highest Orthodox church. (3)

Peloponnese — southern peninsula; contains Sparta, Olympia, Mycenae (Bronze Age 'tholoi' beehive tombs discovered by Heinrich Schliemann; Lion Gate), Epidaurus theater. (2)

Meteora — UNESCO monasteries atop sandstone pillars. (1)

Islands

Dodecanese — eastern Aegean group; Rhodes, Kos, Patmos; some near Turkey. (1)

Ionian Islands — west of mainland; Corfu, Kefalonia, Zakynthos (with the famous shipwreck cove). (1)

Crete — largest Greek island; Knossos Minoan palace; Mount Ida. (2)

Geography & History

Aegean Sea — east coast; arms include the Saronic Gulf (Athens) and the Thermaic Gulf (Thessaloniki). (1)

Strait of Otranto — separates Greek Ionian Sea from Italy/Albania. (1)

Metaxas Line — Greek copy of the Maginot Line along the Bulgarian border. (1)

Gujarat 9
Western India · Capital: Gandhinagar (Largest city: Ahmedabad)
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Coast: Faces the Arabian Sea; the Kathiawar Peninsula juts southward; the Rann of Kutch salt marshes lie in the northwest. (3)

Borders: Rajasthan (N), Madhya Pradesh (E), Maharashtra (S); the Pakistani province of Sindh borders it to the NW. (2)

Indus discharge: Part of the Indus River once discharged into Gujarat's Rann of Kutch salt marshes. (1)

Ancient & Trade History

Lothal — the oldest port in India and one of the southernmost Indus Valley civilization sites. (1)

Gir National Park

Wildlife sanctuary between Amreli and Junagadh; home to most of the remaining Asiatic lions. (1)

Thar Desert (Indian portion)

The Thar reaches into Gujarat from the north; it stretches from the Rann of Kutch up to Haryana, with the bulk in Rajasthan. (3)

Daman & Diu

Former Portuguese enclaves on/near Gujarat's coast; separated from each other by the Gulf of Khambhat; one sits off the Kathiawar Peninsula, the other south of Surat; a creole called Língua da Casa is spoken there; in 2020 merged into the Dadra & Nagar Haveli and Daman & Diu UT. (1)

South America

At a Glance

Capital: Georgetown — Atlantic coast capital. (1)

Mashramani — national holiday with large float parades. (1)

Coat of arms — depicts a crown flanked by two jaguars, one holding a pickaxe. (1)

Only English-speaking country in South America. (1)

Geography

Essequibo River — major river; runs through the Cuyuni-Mazaruni region with the Omai gold mine. (2)

Kaieteur Falls — single-drop waterfall on the Potaro River; one of the most powerful waterfalls in the world by volume. (1)

Guiana Highlands / Guyana Shield — interior plateau; the Rio Negro's upper section (called the Guainía) crosses here. (1)

Port Kaituma — airstrip where U.S. Congressman Leo Ryan was assassinated en route from Jonestown. (1)

Essequibo / Guayana Esequiba — vast region west of the Essequibo River, claimed by Venezuela; dispute resolved by the 1966 Geneva Agreement (though revived since 2023). (1)

Economy

Bauxite — historic top export; aluminum ore drives the mining sector. (1)

Oil boom — major offshore discoveries (ExxonMobil) since 2015 have rapidly transformed the economy. (1)

Caribbean

At a Glance

Independence: first independent Black-led republic and second-oldest republic in the Americas (1804); only successful slave revolution in history (led by Toussaint Louverture and Jean-Jacques Dessalines). (1)

Languages: French and Haitian Creole. (1)

Gulf of Gonâve — large indentation on the western shore. (2)

Île de la Gonâve — large island in the gulf. (1)

Tortuga (Île de la Tortue) — historic haven for the 'Brethren of the Coast' pirates. (1)

Tiburon Peninsula — long southwestern peninsula. (1)

Étang Saumâtre — largest lake; brackish; bordering DR's Lake Enriquillo. (2)

Artibonite River — country's longest river; site of fort Crête à Pierrot where rebels held off thousands in 1802. (2)

Plain of the Cul-de-Sac — densely populated fertile lowland. (1)

Windward Passage — separates Haiti from Cuba. (1)

Heritage

Citadelle Laferrière — mountaintop fortress on the Bonnet à l'Évêque ('Bishop's Hat') above Cap-Haïtien ('Le Cap'); largest fortress in the Americas; built after independence to resist French re-invasion. (2)

Sans-Souci Palace — ruins of King Henri Christophe's palace, near the Citadelle. (2)

La Navidad — first European settlement in the Americas; founded after the Santa María ran aground (Columbus's first voyage). (1)

Labadee — Royal Caribbean cruise port; protests turned away ships. (1)

Voodoo (Vodou) — syncretic Afro-Caribbean religion. (1)

Music: kompa, twoubadou, and méringue are native genres. (1)

United States (States)

At a Glance

Statehood: 50th state (1959). (1)

Main Islands (East to West)

Hawaii ('Big Island') — youngest and largest; contains Mauna Kea (tallest mountain on Earth from seafloor) and Mauna Loa (largest volcano by volume); Kilauea active volcano; Hawaii Volcanoes National Park. (1)

Maui — second-largest; whaling town of Lahaina (devastated by 2023 wildfire); Haleakala (massive shield volcano); Honolua Bay. (1)

Oahu — most populous; contains Honolulu; Pearl Harbor; Diamond Head; Ka'ala highest peak; administers the Laysan and Kure outlying atolls. (2)

Lanai — small island once owned almost entirely by Dole (pineapple). (1)

Niihau ('Forbidden Island') and Kahoolawe (uninhabited) — restricted islands. (1)

Geography & Culture

Hawaiian Islands — only US state outside North America; located on the Pacific Hot Spot. (1)

Filipino labor — Vibora Luviminda labor union historically organized in the islands. (1)

Hula & Lei — traditional cultural symbols. (1)

Hungary 42
Magyarország · Central Europe · Capital: Budapest
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Budapest — on the Danube; formed 1873 from Buda + Pest. (5)

Highest point: Kékes, in the Mátra Mountains. (1)

Largest lake: Lake Balaton — largest lake in Central Europe. (7)

Main rivers: Danube, Tisza, Zala, Körös, Maros. (6)

Major plain: Great Alföld (Great Hungarian Plain), in the larger Pannonian Plain. (4)

Language: Hungarian / Magyar — a Uralic language (kin to Finnish & Estonian). (2)

Historical state: Austria-Hungary under Franz Joseph I. (2)

Physical Geography

()

Danube — Europe's 2nd-longest river; bisects the Pannonian Basin; flows through Vienna, Bratislava, Budapest; tributaries include the Tisza, Sava, Inn; passes through the Iron Gates gorge downstream. (6)

Tisza — runs along Hungary's border with Ukraine; flows through Szeged. (5)

Zala — feeds Lake Balaton. (5)

Körös & Maros — cut through the eastern Alföld. (1)

()

Lake Balaton — largest lake in Central Europe; fed by the Zala; sits at the foot of the Bakony Mountains; Tihany Peninsula juts into it; Tihany Abbey is famed for its echo (the legend of the 'Shouting Girl'); resort towns: Siófok, Keszthely, Fonyód; the Badacsony wine region lies on its shore. (7)

Lake Hévíz — the largest thermal lake in the world; ~2 hr bus ride from Budapest. (1)

Hot springs / thermal baths — a defining Hungarian feature; the Széchenyi Baths in Budapest are famous for chess played in the warm water. (2)

()

Mátra Mountains — contain Kékes, Hungary's highest point. (1)

Bükk Mountains — in the north of the country. (1)

Mecsek Mountains — in the region of Baranya; German settlers brought here under the 1699 Treaty of Karlowitz. (1)

Bakony Mountains — the range at whose base Lake Balaton lies. (1)

()

Great Alföld (Great Hungarian Plain) — dominates eastern Hungary; part of the larger Pannonian Plain. Western portion: the wind-blown loess Kiskunság plain, centered on Kecskemét. Eastern portion: extends to the Apuseni Range, cut by the Körös & Maros, centered on Debrecen. (5)

Transdanubia — the country's western region. (1)

Southern Great Plain — a southern administrative region. (1)

Hortobágy National Park — protects a signature stretch of the Alföld puszta. (1)

Tihany Peninsula — peninsula on Lake Balaton with Tihany Abbey. (2)

Political Geography

()

Formed 1873 from Buda (west bank) + Pest (east bank); 2nd-largest city on the Danube. (2)

Buda Castle, Castle Hill, Church of Mary Magdalene (in the Várkerület District). (2)

Parliament Building, Kossuth Lajos Square, Sándor Palace (presidential residence). (2)

Széchenyi Chain Bridge — designed by William Tierney Clark; flown under upside-down by a stunt pilot in 2001. (3)

Andrássy Avenue — boulevard housing a museum to composer Zoltán Kodály. (2)

Heroes' Square — features statues of the seven chieftains of the Magyars. (1)

Margaret Island — in the Danube, connected by the Árpád Bridge. (1)

Liszt Ferenc Int'l Airport (Ferihegy) — renamed for Franz Liszt in 2011. (1)

Theodor Herzl's birthplace — preserved as a museum. (1)

()

Szeged — on the Tisza, on the Great Hungarian Plain; Votive Church, Szeged National Theatre, annual Open Air Festival. (2)

Debrecen — chief city of the eastern Alföld. (1)

Kecskemét — center of the Kiskunság. (1)

Eger — produces the red wine Bull's Blood. (2)

Siófok, Keszthely, Fonyód, Badacsony — Lake Balaton resort towns; Helicon Hall (palace of George Festetics) in Keszthely. (3)

()

Austria-Hungary — dual monarchy under Franz Joseph I; his name was given to a Russian Arctic archipelago (Franz Josef Land). (2)

Treaty of Trianon (1920) — redrew Hungary's borders; stranded the Székely Hungarians of Transylvania outside the new state. (2)

Treaty of Karlowitz (1699) — brought German settlers into the Mecsek mountains. (1)

Andrew II of Hungary — in 1211 invited the Teutonic Knights into Transylvania. (1)

People, Food & Wine

Magyars (Hungarians) — the most populous ethnic group in Europe speaking a Uralic language (surpassing the Finns). (1)

Székelys — Hungarian sub-group in Transylvania (today's Romania), displaced from Hungary by Trianon. (2)

Magyarab people — Hungarian-descended community along the Nile, displaced by the Aswan High Dam. (1)

Orban the engineer — Hungarian cannon-maker whose bombards helped take Constantinople in 1453. (1)

Goulash — paprika-seasoned stew; signature Hungarian dish. (3)

Halászlé — spicy red 'fisherman's soup' made from carp. (1)

Esterházy torte — named after a Hungarian prince; built on almond meringue. (1)

Bull's Blood of Eger (Egri Bikavér) — Hungary's famous red wine. (2)

Tokaj — wine region shared with Slovakia, famed for sweet wines from noble-rot grapes. (1)

Iceland 47
Republic of Iceland · North Atlantic island · Capital: Reykjavík
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Reykjavík — world's northernmost capital of a sovereign state; Hallgrímskirkja church; Öskjuhlíð hill (with Perlan exhibition hall); served by Keflavík International Airport. (2)

Settlement: founded by Norse and Celtic settlers in the 9th century; Althing (parliament) at Thingvellir is the world's oldest continuously functioning legislature. (2)

Flag: Nordic Cross; blue field with red cross outlined in white. (2)

Language: Icelandic — one of the most archaic surviving North Germanic languages. (1)

Volcanoes & Glaciers

Mid-Atlantic Ridge — splits the island; visible at Thingvellir where the North American and Eurasian plates pull apart. (1)

Eyjafjallajökull — 2010 eruption disrupted European air travel. (2)

Hekla — historically Iceland's most active volcano; called the 'Gateway to Hell' in medieval times. (1)

Vatnajökull — Europe's largest glacier by volume; lies over multiple subglacial volcanoes (including Grímsvötn). (1)

Skjaldbreiður — eponymous shield volcano that produced the Plains of Thingvellir. (1)

Surtsey — UNESCO-listed island formed by a 1963-67 eruption off the south coast. (1)

Geography

Westman Islands (Vestmannaeyjar) — small archipelago south of the mainland. (1)

Látrabjarg — Europe's largest bird cliff. (1)

Blue Lagoon — famous geothermal spa near Reykjavík. (1)

Gulf Stream — warms the south coast despite Iceland's high latitude. (1)

India 159

Region: South Asia. (2)

Major rivers: Ganges, Brahmaputra, Indus, Yamuna, Cauvery, Krishna, Godavari, Narmada. (18)

Major landforms: Himalayas (north), Deccan Plateau (south), Thar Desert (NW), Western Ghats and Eastern Ghats, Vindhya Range. (10)

Coasts: Malabar Coast (SW), Konkan (W), Coromandel (SE); flanked by the Arabian Sea, Bay of Bengal, and Indian Ocean. (8)

Majority religion: Hinduism — third-largest world religion; gods include Shiva and Vishnu. (3)

Major neighbors / disputes: Pakistan, China (border lines McMahon, Johnson, Macartney-Macdonald); Nepal, Bhutan, Bangladesh, Myanmar. (2)

Physical Geography

()

Ganges (Ganga) — sacred river; site of the Kumbh Mela pilgrimage; flows through Varanasi where Hindus cremate their dead on its banks; sources include Nanda Devi; tributaries include the Yamuna and Brahmaputra; distributaries include the Hooghly and Padma; empties into the world's largest river delta (the Sundarbans); home to the gharial and the Susu (Ganges river dolphin). (7)

Brahmaputra — rises from the Angsi Glacier; called the Yarlung Tsangpo in Tibet; flows through Kaziranga National Park (Assam, famed for one-horned rhinos); its Sikkim basin holds Kanchenjunga. (1)

Indus — forms from the Sengge Zangbo + Gar Tsangpo; only river in the Rig Veda personified with a male deity; banks include Mohenjo-Daro ('Dancing Girl' bronze); flows mostly through Pakistan but rises in/near India. (3)

Cauvery — south Indian river at the heart of long-running water disputes between Indian states (Karnataka & Tamil Nadu). (1)

Krishna, Godavari, Yamuna, Narmada — major peninsular rivers; the Godavari bisects the Deccan; the Narmada divides the Deccan from the Vindhya Range. (3)

()

Himalayas — the great northern mountain wall along the China-India border; contains Nepal, Bhutan, and much of Tibet. (2)

Deccan Plateau — dominates southern India; bounded by the Eastern and Western Ghats; northeastern extension is Chota Nagpur (mineral-rich); the Deccan Traps are stair-step basalt landforms from a major volcanic eruption ~66 Mya at the K/Pg boundary; source of the Koh-i-Noor diamond; highest point at Anamudi; Bhor Ghat links it to the Konkan plain. (3)

Thar Desert — straddles Rajasthan, Gujarat, Haryana and Pakistan; stretches from the Rann of Kutch north; the 'Blue City' of Jodhpur lies at its edge; the Cholistan section in Pakistan contains the Derawar Fort. (2)

Western & Eastern Ghats — parallel mountain chains framing the Deccan; the Malabar Coast lies west of the Western Ghats. (2)

()

Bay of Bengal — east of the Indian peninsula; receives the Ganges & Brahmaputra; home to the Sundarbans mangrove forest (Bengal tigers) and Bangladesh's Cox's Bazar (longest sea beach). (1)

Arabian Sea — west of India; the Indus drains into it at Karachi (Pakistan); major ports include Mumbai. (1)

Indian Ocean — names India; major ports: Mumbai, Durban, Colombo; contains the Chagos Archipelago, Seychelles, Mauritius, Comoros. (4)

Malabar Coast — SW coastal strip including Kerala and southern Karnataka; cities of Mangalore, Cochin, Trivandrum; predominantly Malayalam-speaking; setting of Arundhati Roy's The God of Small Things. (1)

Andaman & Nicobar Islands — union territory in the Bay of Bengal; capital Port Blair; home of the Sentinelese, an uncontacted people. (18)

Lakshadweep — Arabian Sea union territory; formed from the Amindivi and Laccadive island groups. (3)

()

Sundarbans — vast mangrove delta of the Ganges-Brahmaputra shared with Bangladesh; habitat of the white Bengal tiger. (1)

Asia-India collision — the tectonic event that built the Himalayas; preceded by rapid northward drift of the Indian plate past the Kerguelen hotspot. (1)

Political Geography

()

New Delhi — capital and seat of national government; part of the National Capital Territory of Delhi. (4)

National flag — the Tiranga; saffron / white / green with the Ashoka Chakra at center. (2)

()

Federal structure — 28 states + 8 union territories. The Seven Sister States of the northeast plus the 'brother' state of Sikkim form the NE region. (1)

Dadra & Nagar Haveli and Daman & Diu — an eight-word union territory formed from four former Portuguese colonies. (1)

Annexation of Goa — annexed from Portugal in 1961 via Operation Vijay. (1)

Major cities — Mumbai (Maharashtra), Delhi, Bengaluru (Karnataka), Chennai (Tamil Nadu), Kolkata (West Bengal), Hyderabad (Telangana). (8)

Regional film industries — Bollywood (Hindi, in Mumbai); Tamil cinema (in Chennai); Bengali cinema (in Kolkata). (1)

()

Pakistan — partition in 1947; ongoing disputes including Kashmir, first partitioned between the two in 1948. (2)

China — border defined in parts by the inaccurate Johnson Line (later replaced by the Macartney-Macdonald Line) and by the McMahon Line set in the 1914 Simla Accord. (1)

People, Culture & History

()

Hinduism — majority faith; major gods include Shiva and Vishnu; holy cities include Ayodhya, Kanchipuram, Varanasi; the religion has notable diaspora populations in Trinidad & Tobago, Fiji, and Mauritius. (2)

Sikhism — centered in Punjab; Amritsar is its holiest city (Golden Temple). (2)

Other faiths — significant Muslim, Christian, Buddhist, Jain, and Zoroastrian (Parsi) communities; Bodh Gaya (Bihar) is the site of the Buddha's enlightenment; Catholicism in Goa. (1)

()

Cattle slaughter — illegal in many states due to Hindu tradition; McDonald's serves no beef or pork in India. (1)

Maharaja Mac — India's chicken/lamb stand-in for the Big Mac. (1)

Dabbawalas — Mumbai's renowned tiffin (lunchbox) delivery workers. (1)

Vegetarian McDonald's — the world's first opened in Amritsar. (1)

()

Indus Valley civilization — Mohenjo-Daro yielded the bronze 'Dancing Girl' figurine; on the Indus, today in Pakistan. (1)

Mughal Empire — built the Taj Mahal in Agra; left a deep architectural legacy across north India. (3)

Battle of the Tennis Court (1944) — pivotal WWII battle at Kohima, now capital of Nagaland. (1)

Padmanabhaswamy Temple — in Kerala; the world's wealthiest temple by gold holdings. (1)

Indiana 15
'The Crossroads of America' / 'The Hoosier State' · Midwest US · Capital: Indianapolis
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Indianapolis — home of the Indianapolis 500. (1)

Flag: dark blue with a torch surrounded by a circle of stars. (1)

Other cities: South Bend (Notre Dame University), Fort Wayne, Evansville, Gary, Muncie (Ball State University), Lafayette (Purdue), Bloomington (IU). (1)

Geography

Lake Michigan — short northwestern shoreline. (1)

Ohio River — southern border with Kentucky. (1)

Wabash River — main river (the state song's namesake); flows from Ohio into the Ohio. (1)

Indiana Dunes National Park — Lake Michigan shoreline dunes. (1)

Wabash & Erie Canal — historic canal that once connected Junction to Terre Haute. (1)

Indonesia 87
Republic of Indonesia · Maritime Southeast Asia · Capital: Jakarta (current) / Nusantara (planned)
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capitals: Jakarta (current, on Java) being replaced by Nusantara in East Kalimantan (Borneo) — capital relocation underway. (2)

Population: world's fourth-most populous country; largest Muslim-majority nation. (1)

Archipelago: more than 17,000 islands across the Malay Archipelago — largest island nation by area. (2)

Languages: Indonesian (Bahasa Indonesia) is official; hundreds of regional languages. (1)

Major Islands

Java — most populous island; capital Jakarta; Mount Lawu (Candi Cetho route); Lake Bandung; Borobudur (world's largest Buddhist monument); 'Great Post Road' colonial highway; Mount Merapi active volcano near Yogyakarta; Prambanan Hindu temples. (3)

Sumatra — sixth-largest island; inhabited by the Batak and Minangkabau; contains the Toba supervolcano in the Barisan Mountains (75,000-year-old eruption); Banda Aceh (Boxing Day Tsunami epicenter, sharia-ruled separatist region); Riau Archipelago off the east; Strait of Malacca (NE); Sunda Strait (S, separating from Java). (3)

Borneo (Kalimantan) — Indonesia controls the southern two-thirds; Mahakam River; Mount Trusmadi; the Dayak people; Sepilok Orangutan Rehabilitation Centre. (2)

Sulawesi (Celebes) — orchid-shaped island; separated from Borneo by the Makassar Strait; Tana Toraja burial culture. (1)

Bali — Hindu-majority island in the SW corner of the Coral Triangle; Mount Agung (2017-19 eruption); capital Denpasar; Bukit Peninsula. (2)

West Papua (Irian Jaya) — Indonesian half of New Guinea; site of the Free Papua Movement (OPM) that attacked the Grasberg Mine pipeline in 1977; Morning Star flag; Timika city. (2)

Lesser Sunda Islands: Lombok, Flores, Sumba, Sumbawa, Komodo (home of the dragon), Timor (split with East Timor). (1)

Maluku (Spice Islands) — historic clove and nutmeg islands. (1)

Volcanoes & Disasters

Mount Tambora — Sumbawa Island volcano; 1815 eruption was the largest in recorded history, causing the global 'Year Without a Summer'; bounded by Saleh Bay forming the Sangaar Peninsula. (2)

Krakatoa (Krakatau) — Sunda Strait volcano; catastrophic 1883 eruption; replaced by Anak Krakatau. (1)

Mount Toba — Sumatra supervolcano; caused a 6-10 year volcanic winter 75,000 years ago. (1)

2004 Boxing Day Tsunami — devastated Banda Aceh; ~230,000 killed across the Indian Ocean. (1)

Straits & Seas

Strait of Malacca — between Sumatra and the Malay Peninsula; world's busiest shipping lane. (2)

Sunda Strait — separates Java from Sumatra. (2)

Makassar Strait — separates Borneo from Sulawesi. (1)

Banda Sea / Arafura Sea — eastern Indonesian waters. (1)

Inner Mongolia 5
Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region · Capital: Hohhot
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Hohhot. (1)

Third-largest autonomous region (after Xinjiang and Tibet) — long, narrow region along China's northern border. (1)

Traditional Mongol script — the only region still widely using the vertically-written script created by Tatatonga; 2020 protests over Mandarin instruction. (1)

Geography

Yellow River — bends in a great rectangular arc around the Ordos Plateau here. (2)

Ordos Desert / Mu Us Desert — southern arid expanses; Ordos Prefecture claims to hold the mausoleum of Genghis Khan. (1)

Gobi Desert — covers much of the north; shared with Mongolia. (2)

Hulunbuir — northern grassland area; home to Daur and Oroqen ethnic groups; site of the trans-Argun border with Russia. (1)

Economy & Cities

Baotou — surroundings host Bayan Obo, the world's largest rare earth metal mine. (2)

Manzhouli — major port of entry on the Russian border. (1)

Jiuquan Satellite Launch Center — near the border with Gansu. (1)

Dasht-e Kavir & Dasht-e Lut — central salt deserts (Lut has recorded the highest surface temperatures on Earth). (1)

Cities & Heritage

People

Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Geography

Shatt al-Arab — confluence flowing to the Persian Gulf via the al-Faw Peninsula; site of the Arvand Free Zone. (2)

Iraqi Kurdistan — semi-autonomous region in the north; capital Erbil; major cities Sulaymaniyah and Dohuk; site of fighting between Talabani and Barzani families; Peshmerga militia. (2)

Mosul — northern city on the Tigris; near Nineveh ruins. (1)

Basra — major southern port on the Shatt al-Arab. (1)

Marshes of Iraq (Mesopotamian Marshes) — UNESCO wetlands of the Marsh Arabs; partially restored after Saddam-era draining. (1)

Ancient Heritage

Babylon — ruins south of Baghdad; ancient capital of Mesopotamia. (1)

Ur — Sumerian city near Nasiriyah. (1)

People

Europe

At a Glance

Cities

Geography

Disputed Territories

Italy 81
Italian Republic · Southern Europe (Mediterranean) · Capital: Rome
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Rome — built on Seven Hills (Palatine, Aventine, Caelian, Capitoline, Esquiline, Quirinal, Viminal); Colosseum, Roman Forum, Pantheon, Vatican City enclave (Pope's St. Peter's Basilica). (3)

Shape: boot-shaped peninsula extending into the Mediterranean. (1)

Major Cities

Milan — fashion and finance capital; Duomo; La Scala opera; Galleria Vittorio Emanuele II. (1)

Naples (Napoli) — southern port; founded as Neapolis; Mount Vesuvius overlooks the bay; Pompeii and Herculaneum nearby; pizza birthplace. (1)

Venice — built on the Venetian Lagoon islands; St. Mark's Basilica, Doge's Palace; MOSE flood barrier; the lagoon's Burano island is famous for lace. (2)

Florence (Firenze) — Tuscan capital on the Arno; Renaissance birthplace; Duomo (Cathedral of Santa Maria del Fiore), Uffizi, Ponte Vecchio. (1)

Turin (Torino) — capital of Piedmont; on the Po River. (1)

Bologna — capital of Emilia-Romagna; oldest university in the Western world. (1)

Regions

Tuscany — Florence, Pisa, Siena; Tuscan Archipelago including Isola del Giglio (Costa Concordia disaster site) and Elba (Napoleon's first exile). (2)

Sicily — largest Mediterranean island; Mount Etna is Europe's most active volcano; capital Palermo; Messina across the strait from Calabria. (1)

Sardinia — second-largest Med island; Gennargentu Range with Punta La Marmora highest peak; Strait of Bonifacio separates it from Corsica; pane carasau flatbread; capital Cagliari with the Bastione di Saint Remy. (1)

Lombardy — northern lakes region (Como, Garda, Maggiore); Milan-centered. (1)

Rivers & Mountains

Po River — longest Italian river; source at Monte Viso in the Cottian Alps; mouth near Adria; main tributary the Ticino. (2)

Tiber (Tevere) — runs through Rome. (1)

Arno — runs through Florence and Pisa. (1)

Alps — northern border; contain Mont Blanc, Matterhorn (border with Switzerland; Whymper's 1865 first-ascent tragedy), Monte Rosa. (2)

Apennines — backbone range running the length of the peninsula. (1)

Dolomites — UNESCO-listed Alpine range in the northeast. (1)

Surrounding Seas & Islands

Adriatic Sea — east coast; the MOSE project protects Venice; major cities Bari, Ancona, Trieste. (2)

Tyrrhenian Sea — west coast. (1)

Ionian Sea — southern arch. (1)

Ligurian Sea — northwest; Genoa is the major port. (1)

Aeolian Islands — north of Sicily; Stromboli active volcano. (1)

Lampedusa — southernmost Italian island; gateway for migrants from North Africa. (1)

Microstates Within

Vatican City — Pope's enclave in Rome; smallest country in the world. (1)

San Marino — independent enclave in central Italy; one of the world's oldest republics. (1)

Cockpit Country — steep karst topography of central Jamaica; refuge for escaped slaves who founded Cudjoe's Town. (2)

Disputed Himalayan region · UT capitals: Srinagar (summer) & Jammu (winter); Ladakh UT: Leh / Kargil
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Status: A region disputed among India, Pakistan and China; partitioned between India and Pakistan in 1948. (4)

Pakistani-administered: Includes Azad Kashmir, administered from Muzaffarabad — near the confluence of the Neelam and Jhelum Rivers. (2)

Chinese-claimed: Aksai Chin. (3)

Physical Geography

Karakoram Range — contains K2, the world's second-tallest mountain. (2)

Pir Panjal Range — frames the region with the Karakoram. (1)

Saltoro Mountains lie south of the Baltoro Glacier; the Vale of Kashmir concentrates most of the population. (1)

Wular Lake — site of the controversial Tulbul Project dam. (1)

Siachen Glacier — the world's highest battlefield; captured in Operation Meghdoot; second-longest non-polar glacier; disputed between Gilgit-Baltistan and Ladakh. (1)

History & Society

Ladakh — Leh was the capital of the historic Buddhist kingdom of Ladakh. (2)

Insurgent groups — Jaish-e-Muhammad and Lashkar-e-Taiba have been active in the region. (1)

Japan 167
Nippon / Nihon · East Asia archipelago · Capital: Tokyo
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Tokyo — world's largest urban agglomeration; landmarks include the Imperial Palace, Tokyo Tower, Tokyo Skytree (tallest tower), Shibuya Crossing, the Tsukiji/Toyosu fish markets. (4)

Four main islands: Honshu (largest), Hokkaido (north), Kyushu (southwest), Shikoku (south of Honshu). (3)

Government: parliamentary monarchy under the Emperor; PM in Tokyo. (1)

Major Cities

Kyoto — ancient capital; thousands of temples and shrines; Kiyomizu-dera, Fushimi Inari, Kinkaku-ji. (1)

Yokohama — second-largest city; Tokyo port suburb. (1)

Sapporo — Hokkaido capital; 1972 Winter Olympics. (1)

Islands & Geography

Hokkaido — northernmost main island; Akan-Mashu National Park with crystal-clear lake and Marimo algae balls; home of the Ainu indigenous people; Seikan Tunnel (world's longest underwater rail tunnel) crosses the Tsugaru Strait from Honshu. (2)

Honshu — main island; contains Tokyo, Osaka, Kyoto. (1)

Mount Fuji — Japan's highest peak and iconic stratovolcano on Honshu. (2)

Okinawa — southernmost prefecture (Ryukyu Islands). (1)

Sakhalin Strait & Sea of Japan — bound the western coast. (1)

Mount Aso — Kyushu's massive caldera volcano. (1)

Disasters & Nature

2011 Tōhoku earthquake & tsunami — caused the Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster. (1)

Ring of Fire — Japan sits on the Pacific Ring of Fire; frequent earthquakes and over 100 active volcanoes. (1)

Culture

Cherry blossoms (sakura) — hanami festivals each spring. (1)

Shinto & Buddhism — coexist; Shinto shrines and Buddhist temples. (1)

At a Glance

Capital: Amman. (1)

Wadi Rum — vast sandstone desert in the south; setting for Lawrence of Arabia and many sci-fi films. (1)

Jerash — extensive Roman ruins. (1)

Karnataka 12
Southwestern India · Capital: Bengaluru
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital & largest city: Bengaluru (Bangalore) — Kannada-speaking; built on a high ridge of the Karnataka Plateau. (4)

Borders: Maharashtra (N), Goa (NW), Kerala (SW), Tamil Nadu (SE), Andhra Pradesh / Telangana (E). (4)

Coast: Faces the Arabian Sea / Laccadive Sea; the Malabar Coast includes Karnataka's coastline (with Mangalore). (2)

Bengaluru (Bangalore)

'Silicon Valley of India' — vast information-technology industry; districts of Whitefield and Electronic City; Bagmane Tech Park. (2)

Sits on the Mysore Plateau; large lakes include Bellandur Lake. (1)

Bugle Rock — geological formation over 3 billion years old. (1)

Lal Bagh — botanical garden completed by Tipu Sultan; home to non-native trees incl. the African Baobab and American Cypress. (1)

Cubbon Park — features the neoclassical Attara Chateri. (1)

Vidhana Soudha — the state legislature, built on the site of a Tipu Sultan fort. (1)

The waning Mughal Empire sold Bangalore in the 18th century; Nandi Hills nearby hold British summer homes built by Mark Cubbon. (1)

Namma Metro — Bengaluru's rapid-transit system. (1)

Cultural & Regional Geography

Deccan Plateau — Karnataka cities of Mysore and the Maharashtra city of Pune lie on it. (2)

Cauvery dispute — Karnataka and Tamil Nadu have feuded for decades over the river. (1)

Mysore — historic Wodeyar capital; sold Bangalore to a powerful nawab in the 18th c. (1)

Kazakhstan 47
Republic of Kazakhstan · Central Asia · Capital: Astana
Central Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Astana (briefly Nur-Sultan, 2019-2022) — on the Ishim River; redesigned by Japanese architect Kisho Kurokawa; Bayterek Tower (based on the country's mythology); pyramidal Palace of Peace and Reconciliation. (2)

Largest city: Almaty — former capital (until 1997); near the Tian Shan mountains. (1)

Size: the world's largest landlocked country and ninth-largest country overall. (1)

Geography

Caspian Sea — western coast (also the largest enclosed body of water). (1)

Lake Balkhash — large central lake; half fresh, half saline. (1)

Aral Sea — shared with Uzbekistan; once the world's 4th-largest lake but now severely shrunk. (1)

Tian Shan Mountains — eastern border with Kyrgyzstan/China. (1)

Altai Mountains — northeastern border with Russia/China/Mongolia; Khüiten Peak; Belukha highest Russian peak; Denisova Cave (where all three known hominid species coexisted). (2)

Charyn Canyon — 'Grand Canyon of Kazakhstan' in the south. (1)

Irtysh / Ob River — drains the Altai through Kazakhstan into Russia. (1)

Aerospace & Industry

Baikonur Cosmodrome — world's oldest and largest active spaceport (leased to Russia). (3)

Semipalatinsk Polygon — former Soviet nuclear test site. (1)

Kentucky 26
'The Bluegrass State' · Upper South · Capital: Frankfort
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Frankfort. (1)

Largest city: Louisville — on the Ohio River; Muhammad Ali International Airport (UPS Worldport hub); 'World's Largest Baseball Bat' outside the Louisville Slugger factory; Churchill Downs (Kentucky Derby); Abraham Lincoln Bridge spans the Ohio. (4)

Other cities: Lexington (horse country), Bowling Green (Corvette Museum), Fort Knox (US Bullion Depository). (1)

Geography

Ohio River — forms the northern border. (1)

Mississippi River — small western border; creates the Kentucky Bend exclave (irregularity in the river's course). (1)

Cumberland Plateau / Appalachian Mountains — eastern part of the state; Pike County site of the Hatfield-McCoy feud. (1)

Mammoth Cave National Park — world's longest cave system (over 420 mi explored). (1)

Land Between the Lakes — recreation area between Lake Barkley and Kentucky Lake. (1)

Culture

Kentucky Bourbon — produced along the Bourbon Trail. (1)

Bluegrass music — originated here. (1)

Kenya 45
Republic of Kenya · East Africa · Capital: Nairobi
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Nairobi — home of the only UN main offices outside Europe/USA; Kibera is one of the world's largest slums; sits on the highlands. (2)

Mombasa — main port on the Indian Ocean; ancient Swahili trading center. (1)

Lamu Archipelago — one of Kenya's few Muslim-majority regions; UNESCO Swahili old town. (1)

Geography

Mount Kenya — country's highest peak; second-highest in Africa. (1)

Great Rift Valley — splits the country; contains soda lakes Bogoria, Naivasha, Nakuru, Magadi. (1)

Lake Victoria — Kenya shares a corner; world's 2nd-largest freshwater lake; source of the White Nile; receives the Kagera and Katonga Rivers; the Katonga links it to Lake George. (2)

Lake Turkana — the 'Jade Sea'; formerly Lake Rudolf; world's largest desert/alkaline lake; in Sibiloi National Park; fed by Ethiopia's Omo River. (2)

Chalbi Desert — adjoins Lake Turkana. (1)

Wildlife & Parks

Maasai Mara Game Reserve — contiguous with Tanzania's Serengeti; site of the Great Migration. (1)

Amboseli National Park — elephants framed by Mount Kilimanjaro across the border. (1)

Tsavo East & Tsavo West — large game parks. (1)

Society

Maasai people — pastoral semi-nomadic ethnic group shared with Tanzania. (1)

Kikuyu — largest ethnic group; concentrated in the central highlands. (1)

White Highlands — colonial-era plantation region off-limits to native Africans. (1)

Kerala 10
Southwest coast of India · Capital: Thiruvananthapuram (Trivandrum)
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Thiruvananthapuram (Trivandrum) — Mahatma Gandhi called it 'the evergreen city of India'. (3)

Coast: Lies along the Malabar Coast on the Laccadive Sea; the union territory of Lakshadweep sits off this state's coast. (3)

Position: At the southern end of the Western Ghats; borders Tamil Nadu and Karnataka. (4)

Highest peak in South India: Anamudi, in Kerala. (2)

Major port: Kochi (Cochin) — home of the International Pepper Exchange (the only one in the world). (3)

People & Society

Highest sex ratio in India — 1,084 women per 1,000 men. (1)

Mundu — popular Kerala garment. (1)

Religious diversity — India's oldest Jewish population; the Mappila Muslims; the Saint Thomas Christians ('Nasranis') who convene at the Maramon Convention on the Pamba River and worship in the Malankara Church. (3)

Language: Malayalam — the dominant tongue of the Malabar Coast. (2)

Physical Geography

Lakes: Ashtamudi Lake and Sasthamkotta Lake (near Karunagappalli). (2)

Rivers: Pamba River flows through the historic Travancore region (with Kollam, an ancient trade centre). (2)

Monsoon — the Indian summer monsoon typically arrives in Kerala in early June and progresses northward. (1)

Landmarks & Sites

Padmanabhaswamy Temple — the wealthiest temple in the world by gold holdings. (2)

Muzhappilangad — Asia's longest drive-in beach, between Kannur and Thalassery. (2)

Setting of Arundhati Roy's The God of Small Things. (1)

Kiribati 15
Republic of Kiribati · Central Pacific Ocean · Capital: Tarawa
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Tarawa — atoll in the Gilbert Islands; site of a brutal WWII battle. (1)

Pronunciation: 'KEE-ree-bass' — adopted from the local Gilbertese pronunciation of 'Gilberts'. (1)

International Date Line — moved east in 1995 to put all of Kiribati on the same day; the Line Islands are now the world's earliest time zone. (2)

Three Island Groups

Gilbert Islands — westernmost group; contains the capital Tarawa. (2)

Phoenix Islands — central group; Phoenix Islands Protected Area UNESCO site. (2)

Line Islands — easternmost group; contain Kiritimati (Christmas Island) — the world's largest coral atoll; 'Joe's Hill' is topographically isolated; the closest higher peak is in Hawaii; towns include Tabwakea, London, Banana. (3)

Banaba (Ocean Island) — only raised-limestone island and Kiribati's highest point; closest neighbor is Nauru. (3)

Culture

Kaimatoa ('Dance of Strength') — endurance dance, participants often weep during. (1)

Flag — frigatebird above a stylized sun and ocean stripes. (1)

Climate threat: one of the most low-lying nations; future submersion is a major concern. (1)

Kuwait 8
State of Kuwait · Persian Gulf monarchy · Capital: Kuwait City
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Kuwait City — landmarks include the Liberation Tower, the iconic Kuwait Towers (3 sphere-and-obelisk water towers), and Seif Palace (emir's residence). (2)

Government: only Persian Gulf state still ruled by an Emir (Al Sabah dynasty); the merchant Banu Utub clan rules from Seif Palace. (1)

Currency: the Kuwaiti dinar is the world's most highly valued currency. (2)

Geography & History

Failaka Island — named Icarus by Alexander the Great; site of a Huwala population. (2)

'Silk City' project — planned new urban development north of Kuwait Bay; includes the Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah Causeway, the longest bridge in the Middle East. (2)

Burgan oil field — second-largest oil field in the world; source of Kuwait's wealth. (1)

Highway 80 / 'Highway of Death' — bombed in the 1991 Gulf War as Iraqi forces fled Kuwait via Mutla Ridge toward Safwan. (1)

Kyrgyzstan 16
Kyrgyz Republic · Central Asia · Capital: Bishkek
Central Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Bishkek — formerly Frunze; on the Chuy River at the foot of the Tian Shan; Ala-Too Square with the Statue of Manas (the legendary hero of the namesake epic); the White House presidential office was the site of the 2005 Tulip Revolution; airport named for Manas. (3)

Language & people: Kyrgyz (Turkic); the Manas epic is the cornerstone of cultural identity. (1)

Geography

Tian Shan Mountains — cover much of the country. (2)

Pik Pobedy (Jengish Chokusu) — country's highest point at ~24,000 ft; on the China border. (1)

Issyk-Kul (Ysyk-Köl) — large endorheic mountain lake; second-largest alpine lake in the world (after Titicaca). (1)

Karakol — eastern ski-resort town near Issyk-Kul; formerly named for explorer Nikolai Przewalski. (1)

Fergana Valley — fertile region shared with Uzbekistan and Tajikistan; Naryn and Kara Darya rivers meet near Namangan to form the Syr Darya. (1)

Culture

Yurts (boz üy) — traditional dwellings; depicted on the flag. (1)

SCO — member of the Shanghai Cooperation Organization. (1)

Laos 25
Lao People's Democratic Republic · Southeast Asia (landlocked) · Capital: Vientiane
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Vientiane — on the Mekong River, opposite Thailand. (1)

History: medieval kingdom of Lan Xang ('Land of a Million Elephants'). (1)

Secret War: intense US bombing campaign during the Vietnam War exposed by Fred Branfman; most-bombed country per capita in history. (1)

Geography & Heritage

Mekong River — forms most of the western border with Thailand; flows past Vientiane and Luang Prabang. (2)

Golden Triangle — tri-border area with Thailand and Myanmar where the Mekong meets the Ruak River; historic opium production zone. (1)

Luang Prabang — UNESCO former royal capital on the Mekong; Buddhist temples (Wat Xieng Thong). (1)

Plain of Jars — Iron Age megalithic site on the Xiangkhoang Plateau; thousands of stone jars; damaged by US bombing. (1)

Muang Khoun — ruins largely destroyed by 1960s US bombing. (1)

Pak Ou Caves — riverside caves containing miniature Buddha statues. (1)

People

Hmong — major ethnic minority; supported US forces during the Secret War (General Vang Pao); many emigrated to the US. (2)

Republic of Latvia · Baltic state · Capital: Riga
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Riga — on the Daugava River; Old Town with the House of the Brotherhood of Blackheads; Castle of Light national library by Gunnar Birkerts; Corner House former KGB HQ. (2)

Language: Latvian (Indo-European Baltic family). (1)

Geography

Daugava River (Western Dvina) — runs through Riga; rises in Russia and Belarus. (1)

Gulf of Riga — arm of the Baltic Sea. (1)

Courland (Kurzeme) — historical western region with the Curonian Spit; populated in the far north by the Livonians. (2)

Borders: Estonia (N), Lithuania (S), Russia (E), Belarus (SE), Baltic Sea (W). (1)

Lebanon 14
Lebanese Republic · Eastern Mediterranean · Capital: Beirut
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Beirut — ancient Phoenician port; landmarks include the Roman Cardo Decumanus crossing, the Garden of Forgiveness, the wartime Green Line, and the brutalist 'Egg' cinema; devastated by the 2020 ammonium-nitrate Port of Beirut explosion. (1)

Population: Lebanese diaspora in Brazil is larger than the home population; introduced sfiha to the country. (1)

Government: confessional power-sharing among Maronite Christians, Sunnis, and Shias. (1)

Geography

Mount Lebanon Range — central mountain spine. (1)

Anti-Lebanon Mountains — eastern border with Syria. (1)

Qurnat as Sawda ('Black Peak') — country's highest point. (1)

Beqaa Valley — fertile agricultural valley between the two mountain ranges; 'Sound of Resilience' 2020 cultural event in Sidon District. (2)

Nahr al-Kabir ('Great River') — northern border with Syria; separates from the Al-Ansariyah Mountains. (1)

Heritage

Baalbek — UNESCO Roman ruins in the Beqaa Valley; massive temples of Jupiter, Bacchus, Venus; Baalbeck International Festival held here. (1)

Cedars of God — small grove of ancient cedars; cedar appears on the flag. (1)

Beaufort Castle — captured by the Mamluk sultan Baibars. (1)

Sidon (Saida) and Tyre (Sour) — ancient Phoenician cities. (1)

Lesotho 15
Kingdom of Lesotho · Southern Africa · Capital: Maseru
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Maseru. (1)

Enclave: entirely surrounded by South Africa; world's largest country-within-a-country. (2)

'Mountain Kingdom': the world's only country entirely above 1,400 m (4,593 ft) elevation. (1)

Geography

Maloti Mountains — central highlands; Thabana Ntlenyana is the country's highest peak. (1)

Drakensberg Mountains — eastern border; Tiffindell ski resort lies just over the South African side. (1)

Caledon / Mohokare River — forms the northern and western borders with South Africa. (1)

Orange River — Lesotho contains the Orange's headwaters; flows west across South Africa. (1)

Thaba Bosiu — sandstone plateau; founding fortress of King Moshoeshoe I. (1)

Culture

Basotho people — wear distinctive conical Basotho hats and brightly colored blankets. (1)

Likahare — popular dish made from animal stomach lining. (1)

Liberia 12
Republic of Liberia · West Africa · Capital: Monrovia
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Monrovia — named for U.S. President James Monroe. (1)

Founding: Africa's oldest republic; founded in 1822 by the American Colonization Society to resettle freed African-American slaves; declared independence in 1847. (1)

Government: former President Ellen Johnson Sirleaf was Africa's first elected female head of state (2005); 1927 elections were the most fraudulent in history (Charles D.B. King 'won' 200,000 votes in a country with 15,000 voters). (2)

Geography

Counties: Montserrado, Maryland, River Gee, Bomi, etc. — many county flags are noted (mocked) for their cartoonish quality. (2)

Mount Nimba — UNESCO Strict Nature Reserve on the borders with Guinea and Côte d'Ivoire. (1)

Cavalla River — southeastern border with Côte d'Ivoire. (1)

Mano, Moro, Moa Rivers — southwestern border with Sierra Leone. (1)

Tubmanburg — town in the iron-ore mining country northwest of Monrovia. (1)

Culture

Americo-Liberians — descendants of African-American freed-slave settlers; historically dominated politics until the 1980 coup. (1)

English is the official language; Vai, Bassa, and Kpelle indigenous languages. (1)

Libya 24
State of Libya · North Africa · Capital: Tripoli
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Tripoli — on the Mediterranean; Wheelus Air Base outside the city was occupied by Italy, Nazi Germany, the UK, and the US during the 20th century. (1)

Three historical regions: Tripolitania (west), Cyrenaica (east, around Benghazi), and Fezzan (southwest, the Saharan interior). (2)

Government: post-Gaddafi instability; the country has been politically divided since 2014 between rival governments in Tripoli (GNU) and Tobruk. (1)

Geography

Sahara Desert — covers >90% of the country. (1)

Gulf of Sidra — large Mediterranean bay; site of US bombing raids in the 1980s. (1)

Great Man-Made River — Gaddafi-era canal project supplying water from the Nubian Sandstone Aquifer to the coast. (1)

Tibesti Mountains — far southern border with Chad. (1)

Aozou Strip — northern Chadian region briefly occupied by Libya. (1)

Heritage

Leptis Magna — UNESCO Roman ruins near Khoms (Al-Khums); birthplace of Septimius Severus. (1)

Cyrene — UNESCO Greek ruins in Cyrenaica. (1)

Sabratha — UNESCO Roman amphitheatre west of Tripoli. (1)

Cities

Benghazi — second city in Cyrenaica; Maydan al Shajara square on Gamal Abdel al-Nasser Street; execution site of the 'Lion of the Desert' (Omar Mukhtar); 2012 US consulate attack. (2)

Misrata — major port; Qasr Ahmad harbor. (1)

Liechtenstein 12
Principality of Liechtenstein · Alpine microstate · Capital: Vaduz
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Vaduz — on the Rhine River; Cathedral of St. Florin (became its own archdiocese in 1997, separate from Chur); residence of Prince Hans-Adam II; controls exclaves in the Triesenberg and Schaan municipalities. (3)

Most populous municipality: Schaan. (1)

Doubly landlocked: one of only two doubly landlocked countries in the world (with Uzbekistan). (1)

Smallest nation to border two countries — Austria (east) and Switzerland (west). (1)

Geography

Grauspitz — country's highest peak; visible from Vaduz. (2)

Alps — cover the eastern two-thirds of the country. (1)

Rhine — forms the western border with Switzerland. (1)

Economy

Customs union with Switzerland — uses the Swiss franc; world's highest GDP per capita. (1)

Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Vilnius — UNESCO Baroque Old Town. (1)

Language: Lithuanian — one of the most archaic surviving Indo-European languages. (1)

Lost to Russia: the Kaliningrad Oblast to the southwest is a Russian exclave on the Baltic. (1)

Geography

Baltic Sea coast — the Curonian Spit (UNESCO) separates the Curonian Lagoon from the Baltic; Klaipėda is the only major Baltic port. (2)

Neman (Nemunas) River — flows through the country into the Baltic via Kaliningrad. (1)

Curonian Lagoon — shared with Kaliningrad; named for the historical region of Courland. (1)

Heritage

Louisiana 29
'The Pelican State' · Gulf South · Capital: Baton Rouge
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Baton Rouge — on the Mississippi River. (1)

Largest city: New Orleans — on the Mississippi delta; French Quarter (Vieux Carré); St. Louis Cathedral; Bourbon Street; Mardi Gras; Canal Street (legendary 'Seven Gates to Guinée' voodoo lore); Marie Laveau's tomb in St. Louis Cemetery. (2)

Parishes — Louisiana uses 'parishes' instead of counties (French colonial heritage). (1)

Geography

Mississippi River Delta — vast wetland delta on the Gulf of Mexico. (1)

Red River of the South — flows through northwestern Louisiana; Shreveport and Bossier City straddle it. (1)

Sabine River — western border with Texas; Toledo Bend Reservoir; the Motiva Port Arthur refinery sits at the mouth (largest US oil refinery). (2)

Lake Pontchartrain — large brackish lake bordering New Orleans; the Lake Pontchartrain Causeway is one of the world's longest bridges. (1)

Atchafalaya Basin — large central swamp; alternate Mississippi distributary. (1)

Culture

Cajun & Creole — distinct Louisiana French heritage; Acadiana region around Lafayette. (1)

Jazz — born in New Orleans. (1)

Civil law — only US state using French/Spanish-derived civil-law tradition rather than common law. (1)

Luxembourg 15
Grand Duchy of Luxembourg · Benelux microstate · Capital: Luxembourg City
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Luxembourg City — on the Alzette River; Grand Ducal Palace; Adolphe Bridge; major EU institutions (the Court of Justice of the European Union, European Parliament secretariat). (2)

Government: ruled by Grand Duke Henri. (1)

Motto: Mir wëlle bleiwe wat mir sinn ('we want to remain what we are'). (1)

Geography

Oesling (Éislek) — northern third dominated by hills and low mountains; highest point Kneiff near Wilwerdange (in the Ardennes). (2)

Gutland — southern two-thirds with denser settlement; cities like Esch-sur-Alzette, Dudelange, Bettembourg. (2)

Red Lands — iron-rich region; HQ of ArcelorMittal (world's largest steel producer). (2)

Moselle Valley — southeastern wine region; the Moselle is a tributary of the Rhine. (1)

Echternach Abbey — founded by St. Willibrord. (1)

Vianden — attacked by the 5th Parachute Division during the Battle of the Bulge; relieved by Patton's Third Army. (1)

Valley of the Seven Castles — string of medieval fortresses near Mersch. (1)

Heritage

Schengen — village where the 1985 Schengen Agreement allowing free travel within the EU was signed. (1)

Macau 7
Macau Special Administrative Region · Former Portuguese colony · 1999 handover
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Most densely populated polity equivalent on Earth. (1)

Composition: the Macau Peninsula extending off Zhuhai, plus the islands of Taipa, Coloane, and the reclaimed Cotai strip; Hengqin is a nearby Mainland island. (4)

Currency: the pataca. (1)

Languages: Portuguese remains co-official; Patuá (Portuguese-Cantonese creole) has only ~5,000 speakers. (1)

Bridges: the Governor Nobre de Carvalho Bridge appears on the flag; the Amizade Bridge crosses Praia Grande Bay. (1)

Tourism & Gambling

'Monte Carlo of the Orient' — center of the world's largest gambling industry. (2)

Casinos & resorts: Venetian Macau, Grand Lisboa, Casino Lisboa, Golden Dragon, MGM Cotai. (2)

Canidrome — Asia's only greyhound racing track until its 2018 closure. (1)

Heritage

Ruins of St. Paul's — Portuguese church facade; main symbol of Macau. (3)

Guia Fortress & Guia Lighthouse — colonial-era landmarks (UNESCO warned over a 2007 Liaison Office construction nearby). (2)

Fortaleza do Monte — overlooks the city. (1)

Portas do Cerco — historic gateway to the mainland. (1)

Senado Square — Historic Centre piazza named for the Portuguese council. (1)

Pastéis de nata — Portuguese egg-tart pastries; the local Cantonese version is the dan tat. (1)

Madagascar 29
Republic of Madagascar · Indian Ocean island · Capital: Antananarivo
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Antananarivo. (1)

Fourth-largest island in the world; second-largest island country (after Indonesia). (2)

People: Merina ethnic group descends from Polynesian/Austronesian migrants; Queen Ranavalona ruled the 19th-century kingdom; language Malagasy. (2)

Geography & Wildlife

Canal des Pangalanes — coastal lagoon canal along the eastern coast. (2)

Tsingy de Bemaraha National Park — limestone karst pinnacles; name means 'where one cannot walk barefoot'. (1)

Ranomafana National Park — UNESCO Rainforests of the Atsinanana site. (1)

Avenue of the Baobabs — iconic dirt road lined with massive Adansonia baobab trees. (1)

Lemurs — entire infraorder endemic to Madagascar; over 100 species. (1)

**Elephant bird (Aepyornis)** — formerly endemic; the world's largest bird, extinct ~1000 AD. (1)

Economy

Vanilla — world's largest producer. (1)

Air Madagascar — uses the Traveler's Palm as its logo. (1)

Maharashtra 27
Western India · Capital: Mumbai
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital & largest city: Mumbai (formerly Bombay) — financial capital of India and home of Bollywood. (12)

Second city: Pune — nicknamed the 'Oxford of the East'; final capital of the Maratha Empire. (1)

Coast: Faces the Arabian Sea along the Konkan plain. (3)

Landform: Western Maharashtra sits on the Deccan Plateau; the Bhor Ghat links it down to the Konkan plain. (3)

Mumbai (Bombay)

()

Built on the Seven Islands: Salsette, Colaba, Old Woman's Island, Thane Island, Trombay and others — now joined by the Colaba Causeway. (3)

Sits at the mouth of the Ulhas River; separated from the mainland by Thane & Vasai Creeks; harbor contains Elephanta Island, Butcher Island, Oyster Rock. (2)

Bandra-Worli Sea Link — double cable-stayed bridge connecting the Western Suburbs to the southern city. (2)

Bombay came to Britain in 1661 as part of the dowry of Catherine of Braganza; previously Portuguese under the Treaty of Bassein. (2)

()

Gateway of India — built to commemorate King George V's arrival. (1)

Taj Mahal Palace Hotel — iconic Colaba hotel; targeted in the 2008 Lashkar-e-Taiba terror attacks (also hit the Oberoi Trident). (3)

Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus — gothic-revival railway station. (1)

Elephanta Caves — administered by Navi Mumbai; UNESCO rock-cut temples. (3)

Kanheri Caves — Buddhist rock-cut caves inside Sanjay Gandhi National Park (formerly Borivili NP, the largest urban park in the world). (3)

Wellington Fountain, Rajabai Clock Tower (Big Ben-inspired), Bombay Stock Exchange on Dalal Street, World One skyscraper. (3)

Dharavi — one of the world's largest slums. (2)

Girgaon Chowpatty beach on Back Bay — hosts the Vinayaka Chaturthi festival (Ganesh idols immersed in the Arabian Sea). (2)

Pune

Sits on the Mula River, separated from Pimpri-Chinchwad by it. Nicknamed 'Oxford of the East'. (1)

The sport badminton was originally named for this city by British expatriates. (1)

Shaniwar Wada fortifications flanked by a statue of Baji Rao I, who ruled as Peshwa from here — the final capital of the Maratha Empire. (1)

Regional Geography

Deccan Plateau — bounded by the Eastern and Western Ghats; Deccan Traps (basalt stair-steps from a ~66 Mya eruption); mineral-rich Chota Nagpur extension northeast. (3)

Arabian Sea — borders Maharashtra to the west; Mumbai is its largest city. (3)

Marathi — the state language; Marathi cinema is based in Mumbai alongside Hindi-language Bollywood. (2)

Maine 27
'The Pine Tree State' · Northeast US · Capital: Augusta
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Augusta. (1)

Largest city: Portland. (1)

Madawaska — town with the highest percentage of French speakers in the US (Acadian descent). (1)

Geography

Mount Katahdin — tallest peak; in Baxter State Park; the northern terminus of the Appalachian Trail. (1)

Mount Desert Island — large coastal island; site of Acadia National Park (named for explorer Pierre Dugua, Sieur de Mons); contains Cadillac Mountain, the highest point on the US Atlantic Shore. (4)

Penobscot Bay — major mid-coast bay. (1)

Wabanaki Confederacy — Native peoples (Penobscot, Passamaquoddy, Maliseet, Mi'kmaq). (1)

Sugarloaf Mountain — tallest ski resort in Maine. (1)

Culture

Lobster — Maine produces the bulk of the US lobster catch. (1)

Stephen King — based in Bangor; many of his stories set in fictional Maine towns. (1)

Malawi 19
Republic of Malawi · 'Warm Heart of Africa' · Southeastern Africa · Capital: Lilongwe
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Lilongwe. (1)

Largest city: Blantyre — named after David Livingstone's birthplace in Scotland. (2)

Population: majority Chewa. (1)

Lake Malawi

Lake Malawi (Lake Nyasa) — dominates the country; world's ninth-largest lake; more fish species than any other lake including the kampango catfish and up to 1,000 species of cichlids ('mbuna' in Malawi); shared with Tanzania and Mozambique. (3)

Ruhuhu River — primary inflow; Shire River is the primary outflow (drains to the Zambezi). (2)

Inhabited islands: Likoma and Chizumulu (administered by Malawi but located in Mozambican waters). (1)

Monkey Bay — Lake Malawi port; commuter ferries link to Blantyre. (1)

Battle of Lake Tanganyika analogue — first WWI naval battle took place on Lake Nyasa. (1)

Malaysia 60
Federal constitutional monarchy · Southeast Asia · Capital: Kuala Lumpur
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Kuala Lumpur (KL) — landmark Petronas Twin Towers with Skybridge; Klang Valley bounded by the Titiwangsa Mountains; Starhill entertainment district; capital of Selangor 'Darul Ehsan' state (Klang is its royal capital). (3)

Putrajaya — administrative federal capital between KL and the airport. (1)

Three parts: Peninsular Malaysia plus the East Malaysian states of Sabah and Sarawak on Borneo. (3)

Bumiputera — affirmative-action category for ethnic Malays and indigenous peoples. (1)

Borders: Thailand (N), Singapore (S, across the Strait of Johor), Indonesia and Brunei (on Borneo). (1)

Peninsular Malaysia

Strait of Malacca — Indian Ocean-Pacific shortcut; Penang and Malacca are historic UNESCO ports. (2)

Johor Bahru — southernmost city; separated from Singapore by the Strait of Johor. (1)

Isthmus of Kra — narrow land linking Peninsular Malaysia to mainland Asia. (1)

Borneo (East Malaysia)

Sarawak — capital Kuching; longest river the Rajang; Gunung Mulu National Park (UNESCO; world's largest cave chamber); port Bintulu; surrounds Brunei. (2)

Sabah — capital Kota Kinabalu; on the northern tip of Borneo. (1)

Mount Kinabalu — Asia's highest mountain island; highest point Low's Peak; in the Crocker Range; 2015 earthquake killed 18 climbers. (2)

Economy

Petronas — national oil company; namesake of the Twin Towers and Sepang International Circuit. (1)

Palm Oil — major export; widespread clearing of rainforest blamed for Southeast Asian haze. (1)

Maldives 12
Republic of Maldives · Indian Ocean (south of India) · Capital: Malé
South Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Malé — densest national capital in the world; contains the coral-built Friday Mosque (Hukuru Miskiy) and the Muleeaage presidential palace. (2)

Smallest country in Asia by area and population. (1)

Lowest average elevation of any country on Earth (~1.5 m above sea level). (1)

Language: Thaana-script Dhivehi. (1)

Carbon neutrality: in 2009, President Mohammed Nasheed held a cabinet meeting underwater to highlight climate threats; pledged to become carbon-neutral. (1)

Geography

26 natural atolls stretched north-south across the equator; split by the One and a Half Degree Channel. (1)

Laamu Atoll — contains the largest inhabited island, Gan. (1)

Addu City — second-largest settlement; once capital of the short-lived Suvadive Republic. (1)

Giraavaru — indigenous people of the islands. (1)

Mali 24
Republic of Mali · West Africa (Sahel) · Capital: Bamako
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Bamako. (1)

Mali Empire — medieval West African power; legendary king Mansa Musa was reputedly the wealthiest individual in history. (1)

Modern instability: 2012 northern occupation by Ansar Dine Tuareg-Islamist militants; coups in 2020/2021/2023; aligned with Burkina Faso and Niger in the Alliance of Sahel States. (2)

Geography

Niger River — the great river crescent through Mali; serves the Inner Niger Delta wetlands. (1)

Sahara Desert — covers the north. (1)

Adrar des Ifoghas — northern mountain range in the Kidal Region. (1)

Taoudenni — northern salt-mining settlement; site of a former political prison. (1)

Heritage

Timbuktu — UNESCO Saharan city; ancient center of learning with the Sankore, Sidi Yahya, and Djinguereber mosques; manuscripts library. (2)

Great Mosque of Djenné — world's largest mudbrick building (UNESCO). (1)

Gao — Songhai Empire's former capital on the Niger. (1)

Dogon Country (Bandiagara Escarpment) — UNESCO cliffside Dogon villages. (1)

Malta 12
Republic of Malta · Mediterranean island country · Capital: Valletta
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Valletta — UNESCO World Heritage Site; on the Sciberras Peninsula between Grand Harbour and Marsamxett Harbour; St. John's Co-Cathedral holds Caravaggio's Beheading of St. John the Baptist (his only signed work); the Grandmaster's Palace once housed parliament; Upper Barrakka Gardens. (2)

Language: Maltese — the only Semitic language written in the Latin alphabet (descended from Sicilian Arabic). (1)

EU/Eurozone: member since 2004; English co-official language alongside Maltese. (1)

Geography

Three main islands: Malta, Gozo, and Comino. (1)

Other settlements: St. Paul's Bay and Qormi are major towns. (1)

Position: between Sicily (north) and Tunisia/Libya (south); the Virtu Ferries service connects to Pozzallo, Sicily. (1)

Heritage

Ġgantija temples on Gozo — among the oldest free-standing structures in the world. (1)

Manchuria (NE) 7
Heilongjiang · Jilin · Liaoning — China's northeastern provinces
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Manchuria — historic region (largely synonymous with Dongbei); name first used by the Japanese. (2)

Three provinces: Heilongjiang (capital Harbin), Jilin (capital Changchun), Liaoning (capital Shenyang). (1)

Original homeland of the Manchu (Tungusic Jurchen) people; site of the Qing dynasty's founding. (1)

Geography

Amur River (Heilong Jiang / 'Black Dragon River') — forms the northern border with Russia; receives the Ussuri (which contains Lake Khanka in its basin); endpoint of the Hu Line at Heihe (opposite Blagoveshchensk); home of the kaluga sturgeon. (4)

Mount Paektu / Heaven Lake (Changbai Mountains) — sacred volcano on the North Korean border; source of the Yalu (Amnok) and Tumen Rivers; Heaven Lake is its caldera. (3)

Greater Khingan Range — runs through Inner Mongolia and northern Heilongjiang. (1)

Sikhote-Alin Mountains — across the border in Russia; habitat of the Amur tiger. (1)

Cities & History

Harbin — Heilongjiang capital; famous for the St. Sophia Cathedral and winter ice and snow sculptures. (2)

Qiqihar & Daqing — major western Heilongjiang cities; Daqing is China's biggest oilfield. (1)

Zhalong Nature Reserve — wetland in Heilongjiang. (1)

Shangjing Longquanfu — historic capital of the Balhae Kingdom. (1)

Unit 731 — WWII Japanese chemical/biological warfare unit at Pingfang lumber mill, near Harbin. (1)

Jewish Autonomous Oblast — across the Russian border to the north of Heilongjiang. (1)

Marshall Islands 6
Republic of the Marshall Islands · Micronesia / Pacific Ocean · Capital: Majuro
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Majuro — capital atoll whose districts include Djarrit (Rita), Uliga, and Delap (DUD); outlying islands Laura and Djarrit are named for Hollywood actresses; Amata Kabua International Airport on Laura. (2)

Government: non-partisan Nitijela parliament; UDP vs Kabua Party blocs; in Compact of Free Association with the United States. (1)

Two island chains: Ralik ('Sunset') and Ratak ('Sunrise'). (2)

Major Atolls

Bikini Atoll — site of Castle Bravo and other US nuclear tests; partially flagged 'in the hands of God' inscription. (2)

Kwajalein — world's largest lagoon; site of the Ronald Reagan Ballistic Missile Defense Test Site; nearby Ebeye coral reef. (1)

Rongelap & Rongerik — evacuated due to fallout from the Castle Bravo H-bomb test. (1)

Ebon Atoll — site where a Salvadoran castaway emerged after drifting 6,700 mi from Chiapas. (1)

Wake Island — separately administered by the US but historically claimed by the Marshalls. (1)

Chesapeake Bay — largest US estuary; receives the Susquehanna, Potomac, York, James, Rappahannock, Patuxent; Calvert Cliffs with shark fossils; the Chesapeake Bay Bridge-Tunnel crosses its mouth. (2)

Tangier Island — speaks a distinct dialect of English largely unchanged since the 17th century. (1)

Assateague & Chincoteague Islands — barrier islands with wild ponies. (1)

Geography

Eastern Shore — Delmarva Peninsula portion of the state. (1)

Western Maryland panhandle — Appalachian Mountains; contains Deep Creek Lake, the state's largest freshwater lake. (1)

At a Glance

Mauritania 10

Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Nouakchott — Atlantic coast capital; served by Friendship Port (Chinese-built) and Oumtounsy International Airport; vibrant fish market run by Wolof and Fula traders. (1)

Modern slavery: the Haratin caste was historically enslaved; Mauritania was the last country to officially abolish slavery (1981) and criminalize it (2007). (1)

Geography

Senegal River — forms the southern border with Senegal; the Faidherbe Bridge crosses it. (1)

Hodh Ech Chargui — populous southeastern region; contains the Mbera refugee camp for Malian refugees. (1)

Heritage

Mauritius 13
Republic of Mauritius · Indian Ocean (Mascarene Islands) · Capital: Port Louis
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Port Louis — independence proclaimed at the Champ de Mars, which claims to be the second-oldest horse racetrack in the world; overlooked by Le Pouce mountain. (1)

Religion: Hinduism is practiced by ~half the population — the only African country with a Hindu plurality. (1)

History: Dutch, French, then British colony; uninhabited until the 1600s; possibly discovered by Arab sailors in 975 (who called it Dina Arobi). (1)

Outlying Islands

Mascarene Islands — including Réunion (French) and Rodrigues (Mauritian); former home of the namesake Rodrigues solitaire (an extinct flightless bird). (1)

Outer Islands: Agaléga and the St. Brandon (Cargados Carajos) archipelago. (1)

Chagos Islands — claimed by Mauritius but currently the British Indian Ocean Territory (Diego Garcia hosts a US military base). (1)

Wildlife & Economy

Dodo — extinct flightless bird endemic to Mauritius; international symbol of extinction. (1)

Pink Pigeon — Mauritius's only surviving native pigeon species (the others extinct). (1)

Vanilla & sugar — major exports. (1)

Mexico 148
United Mexican States · Southern North America · Capital: Mexico City
North America

At a Glance

Capital: Mexico City (CDMX) — built on the ruins of Aztec Tenochtitlán in the Valley of Mexico; Chapultepec Castle (Niños Héroes memorial); National Museum of History; Zócalo central plaza; Templo Mayor; Frida Kahlo's Blue House in Coyoacán. (4)

31 states + CDMX; second-largest by population in North America. (1)

US-Mexico border — partly demarcated by the Rio Grande; the historic El Camino del Diablo runs along it. (2)

Geography

Sierra Madre Oriental & Occidental — flank the central plateau. (1)

Pico de Orizaba (Citlaltépetl) — Mexico's highest peak; on the Veracruz/Puebla border. (1)

Popocatépetl & Iztaccíhuatl — paired volcanoes near Mexico City. (1)

Yucatán Peninsula — Caribbean-side limestone plateau; Chicxulub crater (66-million-year-old asteroid impact); states Yucatán, Quintana Roo (Cancún), Campeche. (2)

Gulf of California / Sea of Cortez — separates Baja California; Croatian missionary Ferdinand Konščak first mapped it. (2)

Baja California Peninsula — long western peninsula; Cabo San Lucas at the southern tip; El Vizcaíno Biosphere Reserve in the center. (1)

Sonoran Desert — northwest desert shared with the US; Yaqui and Tohono O'odham people; Yuma Desert sub-region. (1)

Copper Canyon — Sierra Madre Occidental canyon system; home of the Tarahumara. (1)

Isthmus of Tehuantepec — narrow waist between the Gulf of Mexico and the Pacific. (1)

Cities & Resorts

Guadalajara — capital of Jalisco; cradle of mariachi and tequila. (1)

Monterrey — major industrial city in Nuevo León. (1)

Cancún — Quintana Roo resort; gateway to the Yucatán Riviera Maya. (1)

Tijuana — busiest border city, opposite San Diego. (1)

Acapulco — Pacific Guerrero resort. (1)

Oaxaca — UNESCO colonial capital famous for cuisine and indigenous culture. (1)

States & Heritage

Chiapas — southern state; Toniná site in the Ocosingo Valley; site of the Zapatista uprising led by Subcomandante Marcos. (1)

Estadio Azteca in Mexico City — second-most capacious soccer stadium; site of Diego Maradona's 1986 'Hand of God' goal. (1)

Aguascalientes, Veracruz, Puebla, Querétaro — other major historic central states. (1)

Maya ruins — Chichén Itzá, Uxmal, Palenque, Tulum, Calakmul. (1)

Teotihuacán — pre-Aztec city north of Mexico City; Pyramids of the Sun and Moon. (1)

United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Lansing. (1)

Largest city: Detroit — 'Motor City' / 'Motown'; Hitsville USA (Motown Records HQ); Berry Gordy's label; destruction of Paradise Valley and Black Bottom in the 1960s drove blues musicians elsewhere. (2)

Other cities: Grand Rapids ('Furniture City'; Gerald R. Ford Presidential Museum; Spectrum Health HQ), Ann Arbor (UMich), Flint, Lansing. (1)

State of Brazil · 'General Mines' · Capital: Belo Horizonte
Brazil (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Belo Horizonte — central planned city. (2)

Name origin: Minas Gerais literally means 'General Mines'; the name refers to the historic 'general' and 'mining' districts. (1)

Size & rank: the largest Brazilian state without Amazon rainforest; second-most populous state. (1)

Brumadinho & Mariana — sites of catastrophic tailings-dam collapses in the iron-ore mining country. (1)

Geography

Economy & Culture

Café com leite era — the historic political alliance of São Paulo (coffee) and Minas Gerais (dairy) — 'milk' in the name came from this state. (1)

United States (States)

At a Glance

Mississippi River (the namesake)

Mississippi River — longest North American river by volume; the state's western border and namesake; source at Lake Itasca in Minnesota (named in 1832 by Henry Schoolcraft from Latin veritas caput + Nicollet Creek dispute); mouth on the Gulf of Mexico. (3)

Culture & Heritage

Civil War: Vicksburg siege (1863) was a major Union victory; Beauvoir was Jefferson Davis's home in Biloxi. (1)

Monaco 13
Principality of Monaco · French Riviera microstate · Capital: Monaco
Europe

At a Glance

Mongolia 45
Mongol Uls · East Asia (landlocked) · Capital: Ulaanbaatar
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Ulaanbaatar ('Red Hero') — coldest national capital on Earth; snow can fall in mid-summer. (2)

Population: ~3.5 million; world's most sparsely populated sovereign country. (1)

Geography

Khentii Mountains — northeastern range; legendary birthplace of Genghis Khan. (1)

People & Culture

Throat singing — shared with neighboring Tuvan people. (1)

Zud — winter natural disaster causing livestock die-offs. (1)

Mongolian barbecue (khorkhog) — meat cooked with hot rocks; HuHot restaurant chain originated in Missoula, Montana. (1)

World's largest Bactrian camel population. (1)

Balkans

Morocco 38
Kingdom of Morocco · Northwest Africa (Maghreb) · Capital: Rabat
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Rabat — on the Bou Regreg River; Kasbah of the Udayas (where deported Moriscos founded the Republic of Salé); Hassan Tower; Mausoleum of Mohammed V. (2)

Government: constitutional monarchy under the Alaouite dynasty. (1)

Position: controls the African side of the Strait of Gibraltar; the only African country with both Atlantic and Mediterranean coasts. (2)

Cities

Marrakech — Imperial city; Jemaa el-Fnaa UNESCO square; Koutoubia Mosque. (1)

Fez (Fès) — Imperial city with the world's oldest continuously operating university (Al-Qarawiyyin); medieval medina. (1)

Tangier — northern port on the Strait of Gibraltar. (1)

Chefchaouen — 'Blue Pearl' city in the Rif Mountains. (1)

Geography

Atlas Mountains — three subranges (High, Middle, Anti-Atlas) plus the Rif in the north. (1)

Jbel Toubkal — highest peak in North Africa (in the High Atlas). (1)

Sahara Desert — covers the southeast; Merzouga sand dunes (Erg Chebbi). (1)

Western Sahara — disputed territory administered as Morocco's 'Southern Provinces'. (1)

People

Berbers (Amazigh) — indigenous population; speak Tamazight; Tifinagh script; East Numidian and Guanche are historic Berber languages; ajouag flute used by the Kabyle. (3)

At a Glance

Mozambican Civil War — fought between FRELIMO (in power) and RENAMO. (1)

Myanmar (Burma) 35
