East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Naypyidaw — purpose-built capital in Pyinmana District (since 2005); contains the Uppatasanti Pagoda (almost an exact replica of the Shwedagon); 14-lane highways typically deserted; served by Ayelar Airport. (2)

Largest city: Yangon (Rangoon) — former capital; home of the Shwedagon Pagoda (gold-domed Buddhist stupa). (1)

Government: military junta since the 2021 coup ousted Aung San Suu Kyi's NLD government. (1)

Geography

Irrawaddy (Ayeyarwady) River — longest river; tributaries the Taping, Mali, and N'mai; threatened by the Myitsone Dam; flows into the Andaman Sea through the delta. (2)

Andaman Sea — southern coastline. (1)

Mergui Archipelago — island group home to the seafaring Moken people. (1)

Mandalay — second-largest city; ancient royal capital on the Irrawaddy. (1)

People & Heritage

Bagan — UNESCO ancient temple plain with thousands of Buddhist pagodas. (1)

Rakhine State — site of the persecution and exodus of the Rohingya Muslims. (1)

Hill tribes: Shan, Wa, Karen, Kachin, Chin — major ethnic minorities, many in armed conflict with the central government. (1)

Theravada Buddhism — practiced by ~90% of the population. (1)

Namibia 31
Republic of Namibia · Southwestern Africa · Capital: Windhoek
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Windhoek. (1)

Independence: from South Africa in 1990; was the colony of German South-West Africa. (1)

History: the Herero and Nama were the targets of a 20th century German genocide. (1)

Geography

Namib Desert — coastal desert; oldest desert in the world; namesake of the country; Skeleton Coast noted for shipwrecks. (2)

Sossusvlei — iconic red dunes including Big Daddy, Dune 7 (one of the tallest dunes in the world), Big Mama. (1)

Kalahari Desert — eastern semi-arid expanse; Sperrgebiet National Park named for the diamond-mining 'forbidden zone'; omuramba ancient dry riverbeds. (2)

Caprivi Strip — narrow northeastern panhandle (now part of Kavango East/Zambezi Region); administered from Rundu; acquired by German South-West Africa in exchange for Zanzibar; main city Katima Mulilo. (3)

Etosha National Park — large salt pan and wildlife reserve. (1)

Fish River Canyon — Africa's largest canyon. (1)

Walvis Bay — main Atlantic port, formerly a South African enclave. (1)

Orange River — southern border with South Africa. (1)

Nauru 3
Republic of Nauru · Micronesia (Pacific Ocean) · Capital district: Yaren
Oceania

At a Glance

No official capital — government offices in the Yaren District by tradition. (1)

Smallest island country in the world (only Vatican City and Monaco are smaller). (1)

Former name: Pleasant Island before independence. (1)

Closest neighbor: Banaba (in Kiribati). (2)

Geography & History

Buada Lagoon — Nauru's only inland water body. (1)

Phosphate mining — dominated the economy in the 20th century; led to large Chinese immigration; 1948 strike led to a namesake massacre; the interior is now stripped pinnacled limestone. (1)

WWII: most of the population was deported to Truk (Chuuk) by the Japanese (1942-46). (2)

Australian detention center — controversial offshore migrant processing facility. (1)

Nebraska 24
'The Cornhusker State' · Great Plains · Capital: Lincoln
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Lincoln — University of Nebraska. (1)

Largest city: Omaha — Missouri River port; Joslyn Castle (mansion built by the Omaha World-Herald founder); Berkshire Hathaway HQ (Warren Buffett); the Lone Tree Ferry was Omaha's western-terminus crossing. (2)

Electoral oddity: splits electoral votes by congressional district; 2008 saw Obama win a single electoral vote here. (1)

Dannebrog — early center of Danish immigration to the US. (1)

Geography

Platte River — main river; the Lewis and Clark route. (1)

Missouri River — eastern border. (1)

Sand Hills — vast central dune region; the Elkhorn River rises here. (1)

Scotts Bluff — historic Oregon Trail landmark. (1)

Chimney Rock — another iconic Oregon Trail landmark. (1)

Nepal 24
Federal Democratic Republic of Nepal · South Asia (Himalayas) · Capital: Kathmandu
South Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Kathmandu — Newar valley capital; landmarks Boudhanath Stupa (Tibetan eyes painted on top), Swayambhunath ('Monkey Temple'), Pashupatinath Hindu temple complex, Durbar Square. (1)

History: civil war ended a Maoist insurgency and abolished the monarchy in 2008. (1)

Lowlands: the Terai is the most densely populated region. (1)

Himalayas

Mount Everest (Sagarmatha) — world's highest peak; on the Tibet border; Sagarmatha National Park contains it; common Lhotse-Face route via the Western Cwm; Sir George Mallory died on the mountain in 1924. (4)

Annapurna Massif — eight peaks; site of the world's deadliest 8000m climb. (1)

Kanchenjunga — third-highest mountain; on the Sikkim (India) border. (1)

Sagarmatha NP features Cho Oyu, Lhotse, Mount Everest, and the Gokyo Lakes; the Dudh Kosi River flows through; trekkers start at Namche Bazaar. (1)

Culture & People

Newar — Kathmandu Valley people who built many of the country's temples. (1)

Lumbini — birthplace of the Buddha in the southern Terai. (1)

Netherlands 39
Kingdom of the Netherlands · Western Europe · Capital: Amsterdam (de facto The Hague is seat of govt.)
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Amsterdam — name from a dam on the Amstel; 165-km canal system; Rijksmuseum, Van Gogh Museum, Anne Frank House. (1)

Seat of government: The Hague (Den Haag) — ICJ, ICC, and Dutch government; Binnenhof parliamentary complex. (1)

Other major cities: Rotterdam (Europe's busiest port; Erasmus Bridge, Cube Houses, Euromast tower); Utrecht; Eindhoven (Philips/ASML). (2)

Geography

Below sea level: about 26% of the country lies below sea level; protected by dikes, polders, and the Delta Works storm-surge barriers. (1)

Rhine River Delta — empties into the North Sea through the Netherlands; channels include the Waal, Lek, and IJssel. (1)

IJsselmeer — created by the Zuiderzee Works enclosing the Zuider Zee. (1)

Wadden Sea — UNESCO tidal sea behind the Frisian Islands (with Germany and Denmark); islands like Texel. (1)

Limburg — southern panhandle; only hill country. (1)

Caribbean Netherlands

ABC Islands — constituent countries Aruba and Curaçao plus the special municipality of Bonaire. (1)

SSS Islands — Sint Maarten (constituent country, shares island with French St. Martin), Saba, Sint Eustatius. (1)

Heritage

Tulips & windmills — iconic Dutch symbols; Keukenhof Gardens. (1)

Dutch East India Company (VOC) — first true multinational corporation; founded modern Indonesia. (1)

Afrikaners — Dutch-descended South African settlers (Boers); founded the Stellaland and Goshen republics; Orange Free State. (1)

Nevada 45
'The Silver State' · Mountain West · Capital: Carson City
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Carson City — home of the Sears-Ferris House (inventor of the Ferris Wheel); buried cowboy showman Cuba Crutchfield in Lone Mountain Cemetery. (1)

Largest city: Las Vegas — actually in the Paradise township; iconic 'Welcome to Las Vegas' sign in Googie style; mob origins via Bugsy Siegel and Meyer Lansky; Luxor, Venetian, Bellagio casino-hotels. (1)

Burning Man Festival — annual gathering at Black Rock Desert. (1)

Silver State — Comstock Lode (1859) launched the silver-mining era. (1)

Geography

Great Basin — covers most of Nevada; endorheic basin between the Sierra Nevada and Wasatch. (1)

Lake Tahoe — large alpine lake shared with California. (1)

Hoover Dam — on the Colorado River at the Arizona border; created Lake Mead; Oskar J.W. Hansen monument 'They died to make the desert bloom' commemorates the 112 construction workers killed. (1)

Death Valley National Park — extends into Nevada; Racetrack Playa mysterious moving stones; Greenland Ranch holds the official world high-temperature record. (1)

Area 51 — secretive military test site at Groom Lake. (1)

Cities

Reno — 'Biggest Little City in the World'; on the Truckee River. (1)

New Hampshire 24
'The Granite State' · Northeast US · Capital: Concord
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Concord. (1)

Largest city: Manchester. (1)

'First in the Nation' primary — every presidential election cycle. (1)

Russo-Japanese War treaty was signed at the Portsmouth Naval Shipyard (1905, Treaty of Portsmouth). (1)

Geography

White Mountains — northern range including the Presidential Range; Mount Washington is the highest peak in the Northeast (and famous for extreme weather); Old Man of the Mountain rock face collapsed in 2003; Franconia Notch climbing area; Crawford Notch leads to ski areas. (4)

Bretton Woods — site of the 1944 conference that created the World Bank and IMF. (2)

Connecticut River — forms the western border with Vermont; source in Coos County; once defined the Republic of Indian Stream. (2)

Merrimack River — flows south into Massachusetts; passes through Concord and Manchester. (1)

New Jersey 28
'The Garden State' · Northeast US · Capital: Trenton
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Trenton. (1)

Largest city: Newark (home to Newark Liberty International Airport). (1)

Cities & towns: Hoboken (birthplace of Frank Sinatra), Paterson, Princeton (with the P-Rade parade and a cemetery holding both Aaron Burrs). (1)

Cuisine: the 'disco fries' (poutine-like) and ripper hot dogs are state specialties. (1)

Geography

Kittatinny Mountains — northern range; High Point is the state's literal highest point; the Picatinny Arsenal is the US military's explosives R&D facility. (2)

Ramapo Mountains — northern Highlands; home of the Ramapo Mountain people. (1)

Delaware River — forms the western border with Pennsylvania. (2)

Hudson River — northern border with New York; tunnels and bridges into NYC. (1)

Meadowlands — wetlands turned sports complex (MetLife Stadium). (1)

Cape May — southern peninsula tip; Victorian seaside resort. (1)

Atlantic City & Shore

Atlantic City — on Absecon Island; basis for the property names in Monopoly; closures of the Revel resort (2014) and Trump Taj Mahal (2016); Ventnor City is up the coast. (2)

Six Flags Great Adventure (Jackson) — home of Kingda Ka, the world's tallest roller coaster (456 ft). (1)

New Mexico 18
'Land of Enchantment' · Mountain West / Southwest · Capital: Santa Fe
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Santa Fe — oldest US state capital (founded 1610); UNESCO-recognized adobe architecture. (1)

Largest city: Albuquerque — on the Rio Grande; Sandia Mountains; Balloon Fiesta. (1)

Roswell — alleged 1947 UFO crash site; International UFO Museum; home of Walker Air Force Base; takeoff site of the Red Bull Stratos Felix Baumgartner skydive. (1)

Taos — northern art town; Taos Pueblo UNESCO Tiwa-speaking village; Blue Lake sacred site; Kachina Peak ski resort. (2)

Geography

Rio Grande — main river; bisects the state north-south. (1)

Sangre de Cristo Mountains — northern range; southern terminus of the Rockies. (1)

Chihuahuan Desert — covers the south. (1)

Pecos River — flows through Roswell. (1)

White Sands National Park — pure white gypsum dunes; Alkali Flat and Lake Lucero formed from the evaporation of Lake Otero; near Alamogordo. (2)

Carlsbad Caverns National Park — vast Permian-age caves in the southeast. (1)

Heritage

Trinity Site — first atomic bomb test (1945). (1)

Los Alamos National Laboratory — Manhattan Project birthplace. (1)

New South Wales 13
State of Australia · Capital: Sydney
Australia (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Sydney — Australia's largest city; named after a constituent country of the United Kingdom; lies between Victoria and Queensland. (4)

Encloses the Jervis Bay Territory as an enclave. (2)

Sydney

Port Jackson / Sydney Harbour — the world's largest natural harbor; spanned by the Sydney Harbour Bridge (steel arch nicknamed 'The Coathanger', made partly of steel from Newcastle, climbable by tourists). (5)

Sydney Opera House — designed by Danish architect Jørn Utzon; concentric concrete shells resembling sails; on Bennelong Point. (5)

Botany Bay — south of the city; HMS Endeavour landed here in 1770; Royal National Park lies nearby. (4)

Beaches & suburbs: Bondi Beach, Manly Beach, Darling Harbour, The Rocks (first European settlement site), Hyde Park, Downing Centre, the Lane Cove National Park (extending to Pennant Hills/Wahroonga). (4)

Parramatta River — crossed by the sandstone Lennox Bridge; flows into Port Jackson; Cockatoo Island at its mouth is a former prison. (3)

Sydney Tower Eye — annual 1,500-step stair challenge. (1)

Sydney hosted the 2000 Summer Olympics and has the largest foreign-born population of any Southern-Hemisphere city. (2)

State Geography

Blue Mountains — part of the Great Dividing Range; west of Sydney; bounded by the Nepean and Hawkesbury Rivers. (3)

Snowy Mountains ('The Snowies') — contain Mt. Kosciuszko, Australia's highest peak. (3)

River deltas: the Hastings and Clarence Rivers form deltas along the coast. (2)

Newcastle — northern city; source of steel for the Harbour Bridge. (1)

New York 97
'The Empire State' · Northeast US · Capital: Albany
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Albany. (1)

Largest city: New York City (NYC) — largest in the US; five boroughs (Manhattan, Brooklyn, Queens, Bronx, Staten Island). (2)

New York City

Manhattan — borough of Times Square, Central Park, Empire State Building, Wall Street. (2)

Statue of Liberty — on Liberty Island in New York Harbor; gift from France. (1)

Columbus Circle — intersection where the C-2 visa restricted-travel zone is centered (25-mile radius); home to USS Maine National Monument, Time Warner Center, and Trump International Hotel and Tower. (2)

One World Trade Center — tallest building in the Western Hemisphere; on the former 9/11 attack site. (1)

Staten Island — borough; synonymous with Richmond County; Todt Hill is the highest point of the Atlantic Coastal Plain; St. George Terminal anchors the busiest US ferry route; Verrazzano-Narrows Bridge. (1)

Brooklyn, Queens, Bronx — the other outer boroughs. (1)

Long Island

Long Island — eastern barrier island; Hempstead is the largest town in the US; Port Jefferson and Oyster Bay ports; Peconic Bay adjoins Montauk; Nassau County (named for the Bahamas capital, since both honor William of Orange). (3)

Gold Coast — affluent north shore that inspired The Great Gatsby. (1)

Upstate

Catskill Mountains — eastern Allegheny escarpment; Hunter Mountain; highest peak Slide Mountain; runs alongside the Poconos. (2)

Adirondack Mountains — northern range; Mt. Marcy is the state's highest peak; vast state forest preserve. (1)

Hudson River — flows south from the Adirondacks to NYC; major early colonial corridor. (1)

Mohawk River — major Hudson tributary; route of the Erie Canal. (1)

Finger Lakes — narrow glacier-carved lakes including Seneca, Cayuga, Skaneateles. (1)

Niagara Falls — straddles the Ontario, Canada border on the Niagara River. (1)

Thousand Islands — archipelago on the St. Lawrence River between New York and Ontario; Boldt and Singer Castles; Wolfe, Howe, and Grindstone Islands; Just Room Enough Island is the world's smallest inhabited island. (1)

Cities: Buffalo (Niagara/Erie), Rochester (Genesee River), Syracuse, Albany, Yonkers. (1)

New Zealand 67
Aotearoa · South Pacific · Capital: Wellington
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Wellington — at the southern tip of the North Island; world's southernmost national capital. (1)

Largest city: Auckland — on the North Island; Sky Tower; Art Gallery Toi o Tāmaki; bordered by the Hauraki Gulf with Rangitoto Island. (2)

Two main islands separated by the Cook Strait plus Stewart Island (Rakiura) in the south. (1)

Language: English, Māori (Te Reo), and NZ Sign Language all official. (1)

North Island

Hauraki Gulf, Hawke Bay, Bay of Plenty indent the coast; northernmost point at Cape Reinga on the Aupouri Peninsula. (1)

Lake Taupo — country's largest lake; caldera of a massive volcano. (1)

Tongariro National Park — three active volcanoes; Mount Ruapehu, Ngauruhoe (Mt. Doom in LOTR), Tongariro. (1)

Rotorua — geothermal capital with mud pools, geysers, and Maori cultural sites. (1)

Hobbiton — film set near Matamata. (1)

South Island

Primary Māori iwi: the Ngāi Tahu. (1)

Southern Alps — mountainous spine; Aoraki / Mount Cook is the highest peak. (1)

Lake Wakatipu — Z-shaped lake near Queenstown (Peter Thiel notably bought an estate here). (1)

Fiordland National Park — Milford Sound and Doubtful Sound. (1)

Canterbury Plain — wheat-growing eastern lowland centered on Christchurch. (1)

Pacific Realm

Cook Islands — 15-island self-governing nation in free association with NZ; capital Avarua on Rarotonga; Pukapukan language is spoken on Pukapuka; Atiu sells tivaevae quilts. (2)

Niue & Tokelau — other Pacific territories in association with NZ. (1)

Culture & Wildlife

Kiwi — flightless national bird (and the colloquial demonym for New Zealanders). (1)

All Blacks — national rugby team famous for the pre-match haka. (1)

Nicaragua 32
Republic of Nicaragua · Central America · Capital: Managua
Central America

At a Glance

Capital: Managua. (1)

León — former capital on the Chiquito River; overlooked by the Momotombo volcano. (2)

Mosquito Coast — eastern Caribbean lowland; Puerto Cabezas and Bluefields are the main ports. (2)

Geography

Lake Nicaragua (Cocibolca) — largest in Central America; fed by the Tipitapa River from Lake Managua; outflows via the San Juan River to the Caribbean; contains Ometepe (Concepción and Maderas volcano island) and the Solentiname Islands; populated by bull sharks that swim up the San Juan. (5)

Lake Managua (Xolotlán) — second lake, north of Lake Nicaragua. (1)

Rivas Isthmus — narrow neck between Lake Nicaragua and the Pacific; lowest point of the Continental Divide. (1)

Amerrisque Mountains — central range separating the two lakes. (1)

Heritage & Politics

Granada — colonial city on Lake Nicaragua; pirate target. (1)

Sandinistas (FSLN) — leftist movement that overthrew Somoza in 1979; Daniel Ortega still rules. (1)

Proposed Nicaragua Canal — Bryan-Chamorro Treaty would have allowed a US-built canal across the country; concept revived multiple times. (1)

Niger 26
Republic of Niger · West Africa (Sahel) · Capital: Niamey
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Niamey. (1)

Government: 2023 coup ousted President Mohamed Bazoum; aligned in the Alliance of Sahel States with Mali and Burkina Faso against ECOWAS. (1)

Distinction: not to be confused with Nigeria. (1)

Geography

Niger River — country's namesake river; flows through Niamey. (1)

Sahara Desert — covers the north (>80% of the country). (1)

Aïr Mountains — northern desert highlands. (1)

W National Park — tri-national park (Niger/Benin/Burkina Faso) UNESCO site at the Niger Bend. (1)

Termit Massif — central highlands. (1)

Cities & Heritage

Agadez — Saharan oasis city; UNESCO-listed; gateway for trans-Saharan caravan trade and migration. (1)

Zinder — second-largest city; once the seat of the Sultanate of Damagaram. (1)

Agadez Mosque — tallest mud-brick structure in the world; built in the 16th century. (1)

Resources

Uranium — top global producer; mines at Arlit in the north. (1)

Nigeria 49
Federal Republic of Nigeria · West Africa · Capital: Abuja
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Abuja — purpose-built central capital since 1991; Aso Rock towers over the presidential villa; Zuma Rock on the 100 Naira note; Maitama District with Millennium Park. (2)

Population: most populous African country (~220 million). (1)

Middle Belt — divides the country into a Muslim north and a Christian south; Abuja sits within it. (1)

Cities

Lagos — largest city in Africa; former capital; on the Ogun River and the Bight of Benin (Gulf of Guinea); the NECOM House is the tallest building; Five Cowrie Creek separates the mainland from Victoria Island (on the Lekki Peninsula); the Lagos Lagoon; Nollywood film industry; ceremonial Oba's Palace; Tafawa Balewa Square. (4)

Kano — historic Hausa northern emirate capital. (1)

Ibadan — major Yoruba city west of Lagos. (1)

Geography

Niger River — main river; namesake of the country; delta empties into the Bight of Bonny. (1)

Niger Delta — oil-producing region in the southeast; states Abia, Ondo, Edo, Rivers, Bayelsa; the Ogoni people launched the MOSOP movement against Shell. (2)

Benue River — main tributary of the Niger. (1)

Mambilla Plateau — in Taraba State; continues as the Bamenda Highlands in Cameroon. (1)

Sungbo's Eredo — 100-mi-long ancient earthwork attributed to a Yoruba queen; encircles the kingdom of Ijebu. (1)

History & People

Three major ethnic groups: Hausa-Fulani (north), Yoruba (southwest), Igbo (southeast). (1)

Biafra (1967-70) — secessionist Igbo republic; bloody civil war. (1)

Boko Haram — Islamist insurgency in the northeast. (1)

North Carolina 29
'The Tar Heel State' · South Atlantic · Capital: Raleigh
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Raleigh — part of the Research Triangle with Durham and Chapel Hill. (1)

Largest city: Charlotte — major banking center (Bank of America HQ). (1)

Geography

Outer Banks — long Atlantic barrier-island chain; Jockey's Ridge State Park has large sand dunes; Kitty Hawk (Wright Brothers' first flight 1903) and Kill Devil Hills; Ocracoke Island (Blackbeard the pirate's hideout); Cape Hatteras lighthouse; Cape Lookout. (3)

Appalachian Mountains — western mountains include the Blue Ridge and the Great Smoky Mountains (national park shared with Tennessee). (1)

Mount Mitchell — highest peak east of the Mississippi. (1)

Lake Drummond — at the heart of the Great Dismal Swamp (mostly in Virginia). (1)

Cities & Heritage

Asheville — Blue Ridge mountain city; Biltmore Estate (largest private home in the US). (1)

Durham — Duke University. (1)

Chapel Hill — University of North Carolina (oldest US public university). (1)

Wilmington — Cape Fear River port. (1)

'The Peace Garden State' · Upper Midwest · Capital: Bismarck
United States (States)

At a Glance

North Korea 29
Democratic People's Republic of Korea (DPRK) · East Asia · Capital: Pyongyang
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Pyongyang — on the Taedong River; residency restricted to 'core' classes; Ryugyong Hotel with pyramid facade; Arch of Triumph 10m taller than Paris's Arc de Triomphe; Juche Tower dominates the skyline. (4)

Government: Kim dynasty totalitarian state; ruled by Kim Jong Un; ideology Juche. (1)

Future Scientists Street — planned tech district in Pyongyang. (1)

Border & Resorts

Yalu River (Amnok) — northern border with China; nicknamed 'MiG Alley' during the Korean War; Supung Dam; crossed by the 'friendship bridge' from Dandong (China); source on Mount Paektu. (4)

Tumen River — northeastern border with China and Russia. (1)

Mount Paektu (Baekdu) — sacred volcano on the China border; Heaven Lake in its caldera. (3)

Sinuiju & Dadong — twin cities at the mouth of the Yalu. (1)

Masikryong Ski Resort — on Taehwa Peak; built ahead of the 2018 Winter Olympics in the south. (2)

DMZ — heavily fortified buffer zone with South Korea. (1)

North Macedonia 17
Republic of North Macedonia · South Balkans · Capital: Skopje
Balkans

At a Glance

Capital: Skopje — birthplace of Mother Teresa; controversial Skopje 2014 monument-building project. (1)

Name dispute: renamed in 2019 from 'Republic of Macedonia' to 'North Macedonia' under the Prespa Agreement, ending a 27-year dispute with Greece. (1)

Flag: red field with a stylized golden eight-rayed sun. (1)

Geography

Lake Ohrid — UNESCO ancient lake shared with Albania; one of the oldest and deepest lakes in Europe; town of Ohrid on its shore. (1)

Lake Prespa — shared with Albania and Greece. (1)

Šar Mountains — northwestern border with Kosovo. (1)

Vardar River — main river; flows south into Greece (where it becomes the Axios). (1)

History

Greek Macedonia — northern Greek region of the same historic name; capital Thessaloniki; contains the ancient capitals Pella and Aigai (near Vergina); the issue caused the long name dispute. (1)

Ohrid Framework Agreement (2001) — ended ethnic Albanian insurgency. (1)

Northern Territories 18
Yukon · Northwest Territories · Nunavut
Canada (Provinces & Territories)

Yukon

Capital: Whitehorse — on the Yukon River. (2)

Dawson City — 'Paris of the North'; Diamond Tooth Gertie's Gambling Hall is Canada's oldest casino; site of the Klondike Gold Rush at Bonanza Creek. (3)

Yukon River — originates from Atlin Lake on the Llewellyn Glacier; flows past Whitehorse, Dawson City, into Alaska, discharging at Kusilvak south of Norton Sound; called 'Kuigpak' in Yup'ik. (2)

Mount Logan — Canada's highest peak (2nd in North America); in the Saint Elias Mountains of Kluane National Park; first reported by Israel Russell; first summited by Albert MacCarthy's team; named peaks include Tudor and Saxon. (3)

Kluane National Park — UNESCO; Dall sheep habitat. (1)

Ivvavik & Vuntut National Parks — northern Yukon parks. (1)

Carcross Desert — near a town once called Caribou Crossing. (1)

Northwest Territories

Capital: Yellowknife — on Great Slave Lake. (1)

Great Bear Lake — Canada's largest lake; arms named McTavish, Dease, McVicar, Keith; main settlement Deline (formerly Fort Franklin); former uranium mine at Port Radium; Bloody River flows from its Dease Arm; record 72-lb trout caught here. (4)

Mackenzie River — North America's second-longest river; flows from Great Slave Lake to the Beaufort Sea; Sans Sault Rapids; receives the Liard at Fort Simpson. (2)

Franklin Mountains — run along the Mackenzie. (1)

Nunavut

Capital: Iqaluit — on the southern coast of Baffin Island; St. Jude's Cathedral is igloo-shaped; became capital after a 1995 plebiscite (beating Rankin Inlet); replaced 'Frobisher Bay' as the town's name. (4)

Created in 1999 — carved out of the NWT to give Inuit self-government; absorbed much of the Arctic Archipelago. (2)

Baffin Island — co-extensive with the Qikiqtaaluk Region; world's 5th-largest island; named (along with Frobisher Bay) for 16th-century English navigators; Cumberland Peninsula contains Auyuittuq National Park ('land that never melts') with Mount Asgard and Mount Odin; separated from Melville Peninsula by the Foxe Basin. (5)

Hans Island — shared with Denmark (whisky-and-schnapps tradition until 2022 split). (2)

Other islands: Akimiski Island (in James Bay), Devon Island (largest uninhabited island), Ellesmere Island, Victoria Island. (1)

Cape Dorset — names the prehistoric Dorset culture (displaced by the Thule). (1)

Flag — North Star and a red inukshuk stone marker. (1)

Northern Territory 11
Territory of Australia · Capital: Darwin · 'The Top End'
Australia (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Darwin — on the Arafura Sea; the territory is sandwiched between Queensland and Western Australia. (5)

Nicknamed 'the Top End'; roughly half is under Aboriginal administration. (2)

Stuart Highway — connects Katherine and Alice Springs (the territory's second-largest metro, on the Todd River). (2)

Uluru & the Centre

Uluru / Ayers Rock — sacred sandstone Bornhardt formation; sacred to the Anangu (Pitjantjatjara) people; created in a Dreaming story of two boys fighting on their way to Mount Conner; first reported by William Gosse. (3)

Kata Tjuta ('the Olgas') — adjacent rock-dome group in the same national park as Uluru; southwest of the McDonnell Ranges. (3)

Lake Amadeus & Lake Neale — collectively the Pantu ('salt lakes') of the territory. (1)

Arnhem Land & the Top End

Arnhem Land — northern Aboriginal-autonomy region (shares its name with a Dutch city); home to the Yolngu people; largest settlement Nhulunbuy founded for the Nabalco bauxite mine; the Yirrkala bark petition (1963) protested the mine. (2)

Kakadu National Park — partially in Arnhem Land; UNESCO-listed; contains the Ranger uranium mine and Ubirr rock art site; near the Alligator Rivers region. (3)

Twin Falls & Jim Jim Falls — on the Crocodile River system within Kakadu. (1)

Surrounding Waters & Islands

Arafura Sea — north of the territory, separating it from New Guinea. (2)

Gulf of Carpentaria — borders the territory's northeast; receives the Boyne and McArthur Rivers (the latter via Borroloola); largest island Groote Eylandt. (2)

Van Diemen Gulf — separates the mainland from Melville and Bathurst Islands. (1)

Joseph Bonaparte Gulf — to the northwest. (1)

Goulburn Islands & Wessel Islands — offshore island groups. (1)

Norway 51
Kingdom of Norway · Northern Europe (Scandinavia) · Capital: Oslo
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Oslo — at the head of the Oslofjord; Vigeland Sculpture Park, Akershus Fortress, Munch Museum (home of The Scream). (1)

Flag: Nordic Cross — red field with a navy-and-white cross. (1)

Government: constitutional monarchy under King Harald V. (1)

Geography

Fjords — Norway's iconic glacial inlets; Geirangerfjord and Nærøyfjord are UNESCO-listed; Sognefjord is the longest in Europe. (1)

Galdhøpiggen — Norway's highest peak (in the Jotunheimen range). (1)

North Cape (Nordkapp) — most northerly point of continental Europe. (1)

Lofoten Islands — dramatic Arctic archipelago. (1)

Svalbard — Arctic archipelago administered by Norway; Longyearbyen is the world's northernmost town; Global Seed Vault preserves crop diversity; the Beerenberg volcano lies on Jan Mayen island. (1)

Cities

Bergen — second city; UNESCO-listed Bryggen wharf; gateway to the fjords. (1)

Trondheim — third city; medieval Nidaros Cathedral. (1)

Stavanger — oil-industry capital. (1)

Tromsø — Arctic-circle city; aurora-viewing destination. (1)

Heritage & Exploration

Vikings — Norse seafarers; reached Greenland and L'Anse aux Meadows (Newfoundland). (1)

Roald Amundsen — first to the South Pole (1911); used the ship Fram; companions Helmer Hanssen and Oskar Wisting. (1)

Sami people — indigenous Arctic herders shared with Sweden, Finland, and Russia. (1)

Ohio 31
'The Buckeye State' · Midwest US · Capital: Columbus
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Columbus. (1)

Major cities: Cleveland (Lake Erie, Rock and Roll Hall of Fame, Cuyahoga River caught fire in 1969 — spurring the EPA), Cincinnati (on the Ohio River), Toledo, Akron, Dayton (Wright Brothers). (1)

Geography

Ohio River — forms the southern border with Kentucky and West Virginia. (1)

Lake Erie — northern border. (1)

Cuyahoga Valley National Park — between Cleveland and Akron. (1)

Great Serpent Mound — pre-Columbian effigy mound; 1,348 ft long. (1)

Heritage

Rock and Roll Hall of Fame — Cleveland, designed by I.M. Pei. (1)

Pro Football Hall of Fame — in Canton. (1)

Birthplace of seven US Presidents — Grant, Hayes, Garfield, Benjamin Harrison, McKinley, Taft, Harding. (1)

'The Sooner State' · South-Central US · Capital: Oklahoma City
United States (States)

At a Glance

Cities

Tulsa — on the Arkansas River; largest US city completely on Indian land (split between Osage, Creek, Cherokee Reservations); Reservoir Hill has the Aviator's Arrow that helped guide Charles Lindbergh; suburbs Sapulpa and Broken Arrow. (2)

Geography

Panhandle (No Man's Land) — narrow western strip; once a 'Neutral Strip'; Guymon is the most populous city. (1)

Red River — southern border with Texas. (1)

Ouachita Mountains — southeastern range shared with Arkansas. (1)

Wichita Mountains — southwestern range; popular wildlife refuge. (1)

Lake Eufaula — largest Oklahoma lake. (1)

Oman 18
Sultanate of Oman · Arabian Peninsula · Capital: Muscat
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Muscat — on the Gulf of Oman; Sultan Qaboos Grand Mosque. (1)

Government: sultanate ruled until 2020 by Qaboos bin Said, succeeded by Haitham bin Tariq. (1)

History: former colonial power; controlled Zanzibar (Sultanate moved its capital there in the 19th century) and Gwadar (Pakistan) until 1958. (2)

Geography

Strait of Hormuz — Oman controls the eastern shore; vital oil chokepoint. (1)

Musandam Peninsula — northern exclave separated by the UAE; the tip is called 'head of the mountains' (Ras Al Jibal). (2)

Al Hajar Mountains — northern range; highest peak Jebel Shams. (1)

Dhofar Governorate — southern region with monsoon climate; capital Salalah. (1)

Masirah Island — large but mostly deserted island off the south coast. (1)

Empty Quarter (Rub' al Khali) — western Saharan-like desert shared with Saudi Arabia, UAE, and Yemen. (1)

Cities

Sur — historic dhow-building port on the Gulf of Oman. (1)

Nizwa — interior oasis city, former capital of the Imamate. (1)

Ontario 14
Most populous Canadian province · Capital: Toronto · National capital: Ottawa
Canada (Provinces & Territories)

At a Glance

Provincial capital: Toronto — also Canada's largest city; provincial legislature at Queen's Park. (6)

National capital: Ottawa (sits in Ontario on the Rideau Canal, connected to Gatineau, Quebec). (2)

Motto: 'Yours to Discover' (license plates); 'A Place to Stand, a Place to Grow' (anthem). (1)

Toronto

CN Tower — Toronto's signature skyline landmark. (5)

Old York / Old Town — Toronto was originally York; suburbs include Brampton, Mississauga, Scarborough. (4)

Lake Ontario — Toronto sits on its northern shore. (3)

Pearson International Airport — in Mississauga; named for PM Lester B. Pearson. (1)

Toronto Raptors — only NBA team outside the USA. (1)

Provincial Geography

Bruce Peninsula — angles toward Manitoulin Island, separating Georgian Bay from Lake Huron. (1)

Manitoulin Island — the world's largest lake island; contains Treasure Island (the world's largest island in a lake on an island in a lake). (1)

Point Pelee National Park — southernmost point on mainland Canada. (2)

Windsor — automotive city across the Ambassador Bridge from Detroit. (2)

Lake Nipigon — contains the Shakespeare and Caribou Islands. (1)

Kingston — historic 'Limestone City'; on the Cataraqui River and the southern end of the Rideau Canal. (1)

Thunder Bay — major north-shore port on Lake Superior. (1)

Oregon 43
'The Beaver State' · Pacific Northwest · Capital: Salem
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Salem. (1)

Largest city: Portland — on the Willamette River; Powell's City of Books; food carts; Nike HQ in Beaverton. (1)

Other cities: Eugene (University of Oregon), Bend, Salem, Medford. (1)

Geography

Cascade Range — volcanic mountains bisect the state; Mount Hood is the highest peak; hosts Timberline Lodge (the US's only year-round skiing); also called Wy'east in Multnomah; Lolo Pass. (2)

Crater Lake National Park — deepest lake in the US; formed by the eruption of Mount Mazama. (1)

Columbia River — northern border with Washington; site of nuclear contamination at the Hanford Site (across the border in WA); Bateman Island in the Tri-Cities; Bonneville Dam. (1)

Willamette River — main interior river; flows north through Portland; valley formed the bed of glacial Lake Allison; the oldest vertical-lift bridges in North America; End of the Oregon Trail. (1)

Oregon Coast — entire Pacific coastline is publicly owned (no private beaches). (1)

Mount St. Helens is across the border in Washington but ashfall reached Oregon. (1)

Hells Canyon — deepest river-cut canyon in North America (Snake River, Oregon-Idaho border). (1)

Heritage

Oregon Trail — historic westward migration route; terminus near Oregon City. (1)

Lewis and Clark — wintered at Fort Clatsop near the mouth of the Columbia. (1)

Pakistan 60
Islamic Republic of Pakistan · South Asia · Capital: Islamabad
South Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Islamabad — purpose-built planned capital since 1960; Faisal Mosque (one of the world's largest); replaces Karachi as administrative capital. (1)

Largest city: Karachi — Sindh capital; first national capital and largest port. (1)

Other cities: Lahore (Punjab cultural capital), Faisalabad, Rawalpindi. (1)

Government: parliamentary federal Islamic republic; military has historically been very influential. (1)

Provinces & Regions

Punjab — most populous province; capital Lahore. (1)

Sindh — southern province; capital Karachi. (1)

Khyber Pakhtunkhwa (KPK) — northwestern Pashtun province; capital Peshawar. (1)

Balochistan — largest province by area; capital Quetta; contains the Hinglaj Mata Mandir (the largest Hindu pilgrimage center outside India); Brahui Dravidian language is spoken; Gwadar port on the Makran Coast (China's One Belt One Road); south of the Bolan Pass. (2)

Azad Kashmir & Gilgit-Baltistan — Pakistan-administered Kashmir. (1)

Geography

Indus River — Pakistan's lifeline; tributaries the Sutlej, Jhelum, Chenab, Ravi, and Beas name the Punjab ('Five Rivers'); the Hydaspes of Alexander's wars is the Jhelum. (2)

K2 (Mount Godwin-Austen) — second-highest peak in the world; in the Karakoram. (1)

Karakoram & Hindu Kush — northern mountain ranges; the Khyber Pass crosses into Afghanistan; Tirich Mir and Nowshak are highest Hindu Kush peaks. (2)

Thar Desert (Cholistan) — eastern desert shared with India; contains the Derawar Fort. (1)

Indus Valley Civilization — ancient Bronze-Age centers at Mohenjo-Daro and Harappa. (1)

Heritage

Lahore — Mughal capital; Badshahi Mosque, Lahore Fort, Shalimar Gardens (all UNESCO). (1)

Taxila — UNESCO ancient Gandharan Buddhist site. (1)

Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Ngerulmud — moved in 2006 from Koror to Melekeok state on Babeldaob; the world's least-populated national capital. (1)

Largest city: Koror — connected by bridge to Babeldaob; contains traditional bai meeting houses. (2)

Status: in Compact of Free Association with the United States. (1)

Parliament: the Olbiil Era Kelulau (House of Whispered Decisions). (1)

Geography

Babeldaob (Babelthuap) — largest island; site of Ngerulmud. (2)

Rock Islands — UNESCO marine archipelago of ~300 mushroom-shaped coral islands. (1)

Jellyfish Lake — saline marine lake teeming with millions of harmless golden jellyfish; scuba diving banned. (2)

Peleliu — WWII Pacific battle site. (1)

Ngederrak Reef — protected since 2005. (1)

Palestine 13
State of Palestine · Eastern Mediterranean · De facto capital: Ramallah
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

De facto capital: Ramallah (West Bank); claims East Jerusalem as the official capital. (2)

Two non-contiguous territories: the West Bank and the Gaza Strip. (3)

Government: the Palestine Liberation Organization (PLO) was officially established by Yasser Arafat; the Palestinian Authority runs the West Bank; Hamas controls Gaza. (2)

Historical occupation: Egypt occupied Gaza, and Jordan occupied the West Bank, from 1948 to 1967. (1)

West Bank

Ramallah — de facto capital and Palestinian Authority HQ. (2)

Bethlehem — Christian pilgrimage city, birthplace of Jesus; Church of the Nativity. (2)

Hebron — site of the Tomb of the Patriarchs; divided into Israeli and Palestinian zones (H1/H2). (1)

Jericho — one of the oldest continuously inhabited cities in the world. (1)

Nablus — Northern West Bank city; site of Joseph's Tomb. (1)

Gaza Strip

Gaza City — largest urban area in Gaza. (1)

Erez Crossing — northern crossing into Israel; Salah al-Din Highway is the main road; Yasser Arafat International Airport abandoned in 2001. (1)

Crazy Water Park — amusement park burned by arsonists in 2010. (1)

Proposed Tunnel — would connect the West Bank and Gaza, with the eastern end near Hebron. (1)

Panama 43
Republic of Panama · Central America · Capital: Panama City
Central America

At a Glance

Capital: Panama City — Heron's Palace presidential residence; historic Casco Viejo district (UNESCO); Panama-Pacifico special economic area. (2)

Geographic note: uniquely an east-west isthmus where the sun rises over the Pacific and sets over the Atlantic. (1)

Panama Canal

Panama Canal — connects Atlantic and Pacific; opened 1914 after French and US construction; Culebra Cut carved through the continental divide; Centennial Bridge and the Bridge of the Americas cross it. (3)

Gatun Lake — artificial reservoir that supplies the canal; surrounded by Chagres National Park. (2)

2016 expansion — new Agua Clara and Cocolí locks accommodate Neopanamax vessels. (1)

Geography

Darién Gap — 70-mile roadless jungle on the Colombian border; interrupts the Pan-American Highway. (1)

San Blas Islands (Guna Yala) — Caribbean archipelago of the indigenous Guna people. (1)

Volcán Barú — country's highest peak (a stratovolcano in the west). (1)

Economy

'Panama Papers' (2016) — leak from the Mossack Fonseca law firm exposed a global offshore-tax-haven industry. (1)

Currency: the balboa (pegged 1:1 to the US dollar, which circulates). (1)

Papua New Guinea 24
Independent State of Papua New Guinea · Melanesia · Capital: Port Moresby
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Port Moresby — contains the abandoned Marea Haus ('Pineapple Building') government structure. (1)

Linguistic diversity: most linguistically diverse country on Earth (~840 languages). (1)

Position: occupies the eastern half of the New Guinea island (western half is Indonesian); separated from Australia by the Torres Strait. (2)

Geography

Bismarck Archipelago — includes New Britain, New Ireland, and Manus; the Tunnels of Rabaul built by the Japanese during WWII. (2)

Mount Wilhelm — country's highest peak. (1)

Trobriand Islands — coral atolls studied by Bronisław Malinowski. (1)

Sepik River — major river of the north, famed for tribal art. (1)

Bougainville

Autonomous Region of Bougainville — large copper deposit at Panguna; site of a 10-year civil war; 2019 referendum voted overwhelmingly for independence; Allied liberation in WWII was Operation Cherryblossom (Cape Torokina fighting). (1)

Culture

Tok Pisin — English-based creole and lingua franca. (1)

Raggiana bird-of-paradise — national bird; depicted on the flag. (1)

Paraguay 30
Republic of Paraguay · Landlocked South America · Capital: Asunción
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Asunción. (2)

Second-largest city: Ciudad del Este — near the former Guaíra Falls (the world's most voluminous falls until submerged by the Itaipu Dam). (2)

Borders: Argentina, Brazil, and Bolivia; one of only two landlocked South American countries (with Bolivia). (2)

Languages: Spanish and Guaraní (the only South American country where an indigenous language is co-official; the dialect blend is called Jopará). (1)

Geography

Paraguay River — the country's namesake river; sources in Brazil's Mato Grosso; flows south through Asunción into the Paraná. (3)

Paraná River — forms the southeastern border with Argentina; namesake of Alto Paraná Department. (1)

Gran Chaco — vast semi-arid lowland in the west; largest department Boquerón; main town Loma Plata (Mennonite Menno Colony). (2)

Itaipu Dam — shared with Brazil; largest hydropower producer in the world by output. (2)

History & People

Chaco War (1932-35) — fought with Bolivia over the Gran Chaco. (1)

Department named for Rutherford B. Hayes — Pres. Hayes settled a 19th-century border dispute in Paraguay's favor. (2)

Mennonite colonies — established in the Chaco by Mennonites from Canada and Russia (Fernheim, Menno). (1)

Lake Ypacaraí — namesake of a banned festival in the 1980s. (1)

Pennsylvania 31
'The Keystone State' · Northeast US · Capital: Harrisburg
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Harrisburg — on the Susquehanna River; suburbs Mechanicsburg, Steelton, Lancaster, York. (1)

Centralia — village seized by the state in 1992 over an underground coal fire that has burned since 1962. (1)

Philadelphia

Philadelphia — largest city; on the Schuylkill and Delaware rivers; Independence Hall & Liberty Bell; Reading Terminal Market; Logan Circle with Alexander Calder's Swann Memorial Fountain; the Philadelphia Museum of Art (Rocky steps). (3)

Pennsylvania Avenue / Mother Bethel AME Church — Philly is home of the African Methodist Episcopal Church. (1)

Pittsburgh

Pittsburgh — at the confluence of the Allegheny and Monongahela rivers forming the Ohio; named for William Pitt the Elder. (1)

Other Cities

Erie — on Lake Erie; Presque Isle peninsula; Fort LeBoeuf (haunted by Eagle Hotel ghosts); 'Gauge War' history. (1)

Lancaster — heart of Pennsylvania Dutch / Amish country. (1)

Geography

Susquehanna River — longest river entirely in the eastern US. (1)

Appalachian Plateau / Allegheny Mountains — cover much of the western half. (1)

Poconos — northeastern resort mountains. (1)

Thaddeus Kosciuszko National Memorial — smallest unit of the US National Park Service. (1)

Molly Maguires — secret labor society active in the coal regions. (1)

Peru 56
Republic of Peru · Western South America · Capital: Lima
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Lima — coastal capital; Plaza de Armas with the Cathedral and Government Palace; Barranco is a bohemian district; Museo de la Nación holds a re-creation of the Lord of Sipán Moche tomb. (1)

Indigenous heritage: large Quechua population; Aymara in the south; the Shining Path insurgency was led by 'Chairman Gonzalo' (Abimael Guzmán); Fujimori's regime forcibly sterilized many Quechua speakers. (1)

Geography

Andes Mountains — the eastern half of the country. (1)

Cordillera Blanca / Huascarán National Park — contains Mount Huascarán in Yungay Province, the country's highest point. (1)

Lake Titicaca — shared with Bolivia; world's highest navigable lake; floating Uros reed islands; the Aymara people inhabit the shores. (1)

Sechura Desert — coastal desert in the rain shadow of the Andes. (1)

Colca Canyon — one of the world's deepest canyons. (1)

Amazon Basin — covers the eastern lowlands. (1)

Cities

Cusco — former Inca capital in the Andes; Sacsayhuamán fortress; Cathedral of Cusco with the famous Last Supper featuring guinea pig; Hatun Rumiyuq twelve-angled stones; gateway to Machu Picchu. (2)

Iquitos — largest Amazon-jungle city; capital of Loreto at the confluence of the Marañón, Ucayali, and Amazon; Ayahuasca tourism hub. (1)

Arequipa — colonial 'White City' in the southern Andes; near the Misti volcano. (1)

Trujillo — northern coastal city near the Moche ruins. (1)

Heritage

Machu Picchu — UNESCO Inca citadel high in the Andes; Room of the Three Windows; built using ashlar masonry. (2)

Nazca Lines — geoglyphs in the southern desert (monkeys, spiders, etc.). (1)

Sipán — Moche burial site near Chiclayo. (1)

Chan Chan — vast pre-Inca adobe city near Trujillo (UNESCO). (1)

Philippines 42
Republic of the Philippines · Maritime Southeast Asia · Capital: Manila
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Manila — on Manila Bay, Luzon; metro area is the world's most densely populated. (1)

Position: archipelago of over 7,000 islands; the South China Sea is to the west, Philippine Sea to the east. (2)

Language: Filipino (Tagalog-based) and English are official. (1)

Disputed waters: the Spratly and Scarborough Shoal are claimed against China. (1)

Major Islands

Luzon — largest northern island; contains Manila and Mount Pinatubo (massive 1991 eruption); Banaue Rice Terraces in Ifugao Province (UNESCO); Spanish colonial name Nueva Castilla. (2)

Visayas — central island group; includes Cebu, Leyte (where Tacloban was devastated by Typhoon Haiyan), Bohol (famous Chocolate Hills), Samar, Negros, and Panay. (2)

Mindanao — southern island; largest city Davao; overlooked by Mount Apo; grouped with the Sulu Archipelago; north of the Celebes Sea. (2)

Volcanoes & Geography

Taal Volcano — small island volcano with a lake on it on its larger lake. (1)

Mount Mayon — perfectly conical active volcano in Luzon. (1)

Mount Pinatubo — 1991 eruption was the second-largest volcanic eruption of the 20th century; cooled global climate ~0.5°C. (1)

Philippine Trench — ocean trench off the eastern coast; one of the world's deepest. (1)

Heritage

Intramuros — Spanish-walled old town of Manila. (1)

Vigan — UNESCO colonial Spanish-era town on northwestern Luzon. (1)

Catholic majority — only Christian-majority country in Asia (~80% Catholic). (1)

Poland 35
Republic of Poland · Central Europe · Capital: Warsaw
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Warsaw — almost entirely rebuilt after WWII destruction; Old Town Market Place (UNESCO faithful reconstruction); Palace of Culture and Science (Stalin-era). (1)

Currency: the złoty. (1)

Borders: Germany (W), Czech Republic and Slovakia (S), Ukraine and Belarus (E), Lithuania and Russia/Kaliningrad (N). (1)

Cities

Kraków — former royal capital; UNESCO Old Town; Wawel Castle & Wawel Cathedral; on the Vistula. (1)

Gdańsk — Baltic port; birthplace of the Solidarity movement; Long Market & Crane waterfront. (1)

Wrocław — Silesian city of bridges and dwarf statues. (1)

Łódź — central industrial city. (1)

Lublin — eastern city. (1)

Geography

Vistula (Wisła) — longest river; flows through Kraków and Warsaw to Gdańsk on the Baltic Sea; receives the Bug, Narew, and San. (1)

Oder River (Odra) — forms the western border with Germany. (1)

Carpathian Mountains — southern border range; Tatra Mountains (subrange) contain Rysy, Poland's highest peak. (1)

Białowieża Forest — UNESCO primeval forest shared with Belarus; European bison habitat. (1)

Masurian Lake District — northeastern lakeland. (1)

History

Auschwitz-Birkenau — largest Nazi concentration and extermination camp; located in occupied southern Poland during WWII. (1)

Solidarity (Solidarność) — Lech Wałęsa-led labor movement that toppled Communism (1989). (1)

Wieliczka Salt Mine — UNESCO mine near Kraków with subterranean chapels and salt sculptures. (1)

Portugal 30
Portuguese Republic · Iberian Peninsula · Capital: Lisbon
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Lisbon — on the Tagus (Tejo) River; Belém Tower, Jerónimos Monastery (UNESCO); the historic Alfama district; 25 de Abril Bridge. (1)

Second city: Porto — gives its name to Port wine; UNESCO Ribeira district. (1)

Position: westernmost mainland country in continental Europe; Cabo da Roca is the westernmost point. (1)

Regions

Algarve — southern beach region. (1)

Alentejo — south-central cork-tree and wine region. (1)

Madeira — autonomous archipelago in the Atlantic; capital Funchal; famous fortified wine and Cristiano Ronaldo's birthplace. (1)

Azores — autonomous mid-Atlantic archipelago of 9 volcanic islands; capital Ponta Delgada. (1)

Geography

Tagus River — longest in the Iberian Peninsula; rises in Spain. (1)

Douro River — runs through Porto; flanked by terraced vineyards. (1)

Serra da Estrela — highest mainland mountain range; Torre is the highest peak. (1)

Heritage & Empire

Lusophone world — Portuguese is spoken in Brazil, Angola, Mozambique, Cape Verde, Guinea-Bissau, São Tomé and Príncipe, East Timor, and Macau. (1)

Age of Discovery — Henry the Navigator led 15th-century exploration; Vasco da Gama reached India; the Padrão dos Descobrimentos monument in Lisbon honors them. (1)

Fátima — site of the 1917 Marian apparitions; major Catholic pilgrimage destination. (1)

Pastéis de nata — egg-tart pastry; became the dan ta in former colonies like Macau. (1)

Prairie Provinces 5
Saskatchewan · Manitoba (Alberta covered separately)
Canada (Provinces & Territories)

Saskatchewan

Capital: Regina — geometric provincial capital. (1)

Cities: Saskatoon, Prince Albert, Moose Jaw, Lloydminster (split with Alberta). (1)

Shape: the only Canadian province with completely rectangular borders. (1)

Lakes: Reindeer Lake and Lake Athabasca; Lac La Ronge overflows into the Churchill River. (1)

Qu'Appelle Valley — site of Emily Pauline Johnson's poem 'Legend of the Qu'Appelle Valley'; the river emerges from Elbow Lake. (1)

Borders: North Dakota (south), Northwest Territories (north). (1)

Manitoba

Capital: Winnipeg — at the confluence of the Red and Assiniboine rivers. (1)

Duck Mountain Provincial Park — contains Baldy Mountain, the province's highest point. (1)

Lake Winnipeg — Manitoba's largest lake; receives the mouth of the Red River of the North. (1)

Hudson Bay — northeastern coast; Churchill is the polar-bear-tourism town on the bay, served by the Hudson Bay Railway. (1)

Lake Agassiz — prehistoric glacial lake that once covered most of Manitoba. (1)

Lake of the Woods — shared with Ontario and the US. (1)

Punjab (Indian) 11
Northwestern India · Capital: Chandigarh
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Chandigarh — shared between the Indian states of Punjab and Haryana. (3)

Larger 'Punjab' region: Divided in 1947 between India and Pakistan. The Pakistani Punjab is governed from Lahore; the Indian Punjab and Haryana are both governed from Chandigarh. (4)

Etymology: 'Punjab' = 'land of five waters' — the rivers Beas, Jhelum, Chenab, Ravi, Sutlej. (2)

Language: Punjabi is the only tonal Indo-European language; used to write the Sikh scripture Adi Granth. (1)

Sikhism

Amritsar — second-largest city in the Indian Punjab; home of the Golden Temple (Harimandir), holiest site in the Sikh faith. (2)

Holy sites — sacred ponds called sarovars; holy cities at Tarn Taran and Anandpur; gurdwaras include Kartarpur and Sultanpur Lodhi. (1)

Vegetarian McDonald's — the world's first opened in Amritsar. (1)

Wider Punjab Region

Masrur Temples — rock-cut Hindu temples in the Kangra Valley at Punjab's northern end. (1)

Dharamshala — town in the wider Punjab region; in-exile residence of the Dalai Lama. (1)

Cuisine — origin of sarson da saag, dal makhani, and Tandoori chicken. (1)

Ancient history — Alexander the Great's army turned back from Punjab after the Battle of the Hydaspes. (1)

Cholistan Desert — extends into the southern (Pakistani) Punjab; Derawar Fort lies within. (1)

Qatar 12
State of Qatar · Arabian Peninsula · Capital: Doha
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Doha — landmarks include the Museum of Islamic Art (designed by I.M. Pei), Aspire Tower, the artificial Pearl-Qatar island (only place foreigners can own property), Hamad International Airport (with Urs Fischer's iconic bronze teddy-bear lamp sculpture), Khalifa International Stadium. (3)

Government: absolute monarchy under the House of Thani (Al Thani dynasty). (1)

Wealth: highest GDP per capita in the Muslim world. (1)

Hosted the 2022 FIFA World Cup (Lusail Stadium hosted the final, won by Argentina). (1)

Geography

Position: small peninsula jutting into the Persian Gulf from the Arabian Peninsula; sole land border with Saudi Arabia. (1)

Khawr al Udayd ('Inland Sea') — proposed site of the Salwa Canal that would turn Qatar into an island. (2)

Dukhan oil field — major hydrocarbon source. (1)

West Bay Lagoon — under construction as planned Lusail City. (1)

Politics

2017-21 blockade — Saudi Arabia, UAE, Bahrain, and Egypt blockaded Qatar over policy disputes. (1)

Quebec 16
Largest Canadian province by area · French-speaking · Capital: Quebec City
Canada (Provinces & Territories)

At a Glance

Capital: Quebec City — only walled city north of Mexico in North America; contains the Plains of Abraham. (2)

Largest city: Montreal — on the Island of Montreal at the confluence of the Ottawa and St. Lawrence rivers. (6)

Flag: the Fleurdelisé — white cross with four fleurs-de-lis at the corners on a blue field. (2)

Native language: French is the official language; Jersey Norman is also spoken; cuisine includes poutine. (2)

Borders: Newfoundland & Labrador, New Brunswick (E), Ontario (W). (1)

Montreal

Original name 'Ville-Marie'; nickname 'The City of a Hundred Steeples' (la ville aux cent clochers). (2)

Mount Royal — wooded hill at the city's center. (2)

RESO 'Underground City' — half a million people daily; connects Bell Centre and Place Bonaventure. (1)

Habitat 67 — modular housing complex by Moshe Safdie; built for Expo 67 on Île Sainte-Hélène. (1)

Biosphere — Buckminster Fuller's transparent geodesic sphere on St. Helen's Island. (1)

Olympic Stadium (Stade Olympique) — built for the 1976 Summer Olympics. (1)

Hochelaga Archipelago — Montreal sits on the largest of these islands east of the Lake of Two Mountains. (1)

Laval — largest suburb of Montreal. (1)

Provincial Geography

Laurentian Mountains — source of the Montmorency and St. Maurice rivers. (1)

Ungava Peninsula — extreme north; juts into Hudson Bay; contains Cape Wolstenholme. (2)

Gaspé Peninsula — south of the St. Lawrence estuary; contains the Chic-Choc Mountains and Chic-Chocs Wildlife Preserve. (2)

Anticosti Island — large island at the mouth of the St. Lawrence. (1)

Manicouagan Reservoir / 'Eye of Quebec' — circular impact-crater lake with a central island. (2)

Hydropower — dams on the Eastmain and La Grande rivers. (1)

Gatineau & Saguenay — other major cities. (1)

Queensland 11
State of Australia · Capital: Brisbane
Australia (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Brisbane — Australia's third-largest city; lies on the Brisbane River. (4)

Named for Queen Victoria — the northernmost of two such-named states. (1)

Coastline & Great Barrier Reef

Great Barrier Reef — extensive coral system off the eastern coast in the Coral Sea; protected by a marine park; flights to Lady Elliot Island depart from Bundaberg Airport; affected by sludge dumping and bleaching. (4)

Whitsunday Islands — popular diving archipelago; lived on by the Juru people. (2)

Fraser Island — large sand island administered by the state. (1)

Great Keppel Island — site of the 2010 Jia Yong oil spill. (1)

Cape York & North

Cape York Peninsula — northern tip; borders the Torres Strait (separating Australia from New Guinea) and the Gulf of Carpentaria; eastern shore features rainforests. (4)

Daintree Rainforest — UNESCO rainforest including Mossman Gorge, north of Cairns. (1)

Townsville — major access point to the Great Barrier Reef. (2)

Inland & Southeast

Gold Coast — resort city just north of the NSW border; contains Surfers Paradise beach and the Q1, Australia's tallest building; theme parks like Dreamworld and Wet'n'Wild. (3)

Glass House Mountains — chain of isolated volcanic monadnocks. (1)

Lamington National Park — contains the northernmost Antarctic Beech trees; in the southeast. (1)

Mt. Warning — southern peak; remnant of an ancient caldera. (1)

Warrego River — drains much of the interior; receives runoff from the Carnarvon Range. (1)

Darling Downs / Toowoomba / Lockyer Valley — inland agricultural region; 2011 floods devastated Toowoomba; also includes the Granite Belt wine region. (1)

Republic of Congo 13
Congo-Brazzaville · Central Africa · Capital: Brazzaville
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Brazzaville — across the Congo River from Kinshasa; pair of capitals is the closest such pair in the world; was the capital of French Equatorial Africa. (3)

Pool Department — surrounds the capital; named for the Malebo Pool widening of the Congo River that includes Mbamou Island. (2)

Brazzaville Declaration (1944) — Charles de Gaulle's speech here led to many French colonies gaining autonomy. (1)

Cities & Landmarks

Pointe-Noire — second city and major Atlantic port; connected to Brazzaville by the Congo-Ocean Railway that bypasses Livingstone Falls. (1)

Nabemba Tower (Elf Tower) — Brazzaville's tallest building; named for Mount Nabemba, the country's highest peak; financed by Elf Aquitaine. (2)

Geography

Mount Nabemba — highest point in the country, in the northern Sangha Region. (1)

Congo River — the country sits north and west of the river; Malebo Pool widens at Brazzaville-Kinshasa. (1)

Sangha Trinational — trans-border UNESCO protected area shared with the CAR and Cameroon (includes Nouabalé-Ndoki National Park). (1)

Rhode Island 13
Officially 'Rhode Island and Providence Plantations' · Smallest US state · Capital: Providence
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Providence — on the Woonasquatucket River; Westminster Arcade (oldest enclosed shopping mall in the US); the giant Nibbles Woodaway termite ('Big Blue Bug'). (1)

Smallest US state by area; also has the longest official name. (1)

Pirate heritage: birthplace of Thomas Tew, who helped found a semi-mythical pirate republic in Madagascar. (1)

Geography

Narragansett Bay — large central bay that nearly bisects the state. (3)

Aquidneck Island — largest island in the bay; site of Newport and Portsmouth. (3)

Block Island — south of the mainland; popular summer destination. (1)

Jerimoth Hill — highest point; was infamously inaccessible for years due to a strict landowner. (1)

Blackstone River — designated the most polluted US river in 1990; flows through Woonsocket and Providence. (1)

Newport

Newport — yacht-haven city; Gilded Age 'cottages' by Richard Morris Hunt including The Breakers, Marble House, The Elms. (2)

Touro Synagogue — oldest surviving synagogue in the US; annual reading of George Washington's letter to Moses Seixas. (1)

White Horse Tavern — oldest tavern in the US. (1)

Fort Adams State Park — contains the Commandant's Residence used by Eisenhower. (1)

Cliff Walk — three-mile scenic seaside walk. (1)

Rio de Janeiro 8
City & State of Brazil · Former national capital
Brazil (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Rio de Janeiro — second-most populous city in Brazil (after São Paulo); name translates to 'river of January'; capital of Brazil until 1960 when Brasília was built. (5)

Suburb of Niterói — once a separate state; site of a deadly 1961 circus fire. (1)

Hosted the first South American Summer Olympics (2016); 2016 events were hampered by Zika-virus concerns. (2)

Bay & Mountains

Guanabara Bay — large bay around which the city is built; pollution and 'super-bacteria' are major issues. (5)

Sugarloaf Mountain — granite-quartz peak; connected by cable car to Morro da Urca. (3)

Corcovado Mountain — site of the iconic Christ the Redeemer (Cristo Redentor) statue. (4)

Tijuca National Park — world's largest urban forest (status disputed with Johannesburg). (2)

Neighborhoods & Beaches

Copacabana Beach — iconic crescent strand. (5)

Ipanema — famous neighborhood and beach. (1)

Barra da Tijuca — wealthy modern neighborhood along Ayrton Senna Avenue. (2)

Zona Sul — affluent southern zone containing the Rodrigo de Freitas Lagoon. (1)

Escadaria Selarón — colorful mosaic-tiled stairway. (1)

Favelas & Society

Rocinha — largest favela; between São Conrado and Gávea. (2)

Complexo do Alemão ('German Complex') — favela with one of the world's highest murder rates. (2)

Cidade de Deus ('City of God') — favela made famous by the 2002 film. (1)

Galeão / Governador Island — main international airport site. (1)

Events & Culture

Carnival — world's largest celebration. (2)

Maracanã Stadium — Brazil's most famous football venue. (1)

Romania 26
Southeastern Europe (Balkans/Eastern Europe border) · Capital: Bucharest
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Bucharest — on the Dâmbovița River; Palace of the Parliament (world's heaviest building, built under Ceaușescu). (1)

Riviera: the Black Sea coast resort Mamaia; the port of Constanța. (1)

Flag: vertical blue-yellow-red triband, very similar to Chad's. (1)

Historic Regions

Transylvania — northwestern region; defended by Teutonic Knights under Andrew II of Hungary in 1211; includes the Szekely Land and the legendary Dracula's Castle (Bran Castle). (1)

Wallachia — southern region; Poenari Citadel (true 'Dracula's Castle') east of the Olt River; Vlad III ruled here. (1)

Moldavia — eastern region; northern part of historic Moldavia is in Ukraine. (1)

Dobruja / Dobrogea — Black Sea region shared with Bulgaria. (1)

Banat — western region shared with Serbia. (1)

Geography

Carpathian Mountains — arc-shaped range crossing the country; contains Lake Saint Anne, the country's only crater lake (near Mohoș). (2)

Iron Gate — Danube gorge on the border with Serbia; town of Orșova lies just upstream. (1)

Danube Delta — UNESCO wetland where the river enters the Black Sea. (1)

Prut River — northeastern border with Moldova. (1)

Cities

Cluj-Napoca — largest Transylvanian city. (1)

Iași (Jassy) — Moldavian cultural capital. (1)

Timișoara — site of the 1989 revolution that toppled Ceaușescu. (1)

Russia 234
Russian Federation · Eastern Europe / Northern Asia · Capital: Moscow
Former Soviet Bloc

At a Glance

Capital: Moscow — Kremlin, Red Square, St. Basil's Cathedral (Pokrovsky Sobor), GUM department store, Lenin's Mausoleum. (8)

Largest country in the world by area — spans 11 time zones from Kaliningrad to the Bering Strait. (4)

Government: federal state with 85 federal subjects (oblasts, republics, okrugs, krais, federal cities). (1)

Major Cities

Saint Petersburg — second city; founded by Peter the Great on the Neva River; former capital; Hermitage Museum / Winter Palace; canals nicknamed 'Venice of the North'. (3)

Volgograd — formerly Stalingrad; site of the WWII battle; on the Volga River. (3)

Nizhny Novgorod — Volga-Oka confluence; former 'Gorky' under Soviet rule. (3)

Novosibirsk — largest Siberian city. (2)

Yekaterinburg — Urals city where the Romanovs were executed. (1)

Vladivostok — Pacific Far East port; eastern end of the Trans-Siberian. (1)

Murmansk — largest city north of the Arctic Circle; main warm-water Arctic port. (3)

Rivers, Lakes & Mountains

Volga River — Europe's longest river; flows through Moscow region, Nizhny Novgorod, Kazan, Volgograd into the Caspian. (6)

Amur River — forms the border with China. (5)

Ural Mountains — divide Europe from Asia; run north-south. (5)

Lake Baikal — world's deepest and largest by volume; in Siberia; contains 20% of unfrozen surface fresh water; home to the unique Baikal seal. (3)

Lake Ladoga — Europe's largest lake; west of St. Petersburg. (3)

Caucasus Mountains — southern border range; contains Mount Elbrus, Europe's highest peak. (2)

Altai Mountains — southern Siberian range; meet Mongolia, China, Kazakhstan. (3)

Kamchatka Peninsula — volcanic Far Eastern peninsula; contains Mount Kronotsky and Klyuchevskaya Sopka (highest active volcano in Eurasia). (1)

Disputed & Federal Subjects

Kaliningrad Oblast — Russian exclave on the Baltic between Poland and Lithuania; formerly Königsberg; Yantarny mines contain 8% of the world's amber reserves. (6)

Crimean Peninsula / Crimea — annexed from Ukraine in 2014; capital Simferopol; Sevastopol naval base. (5)

Chechnya — North Caucasus republic; Grozny capital; bloody 1990s/2000s wars. (3)

Republic of Abkhazia & South Ossetia — Georgian breakaway regions recognized by Russia. (2)

Tatarstan — Volga republic; capital Kazan. (1)

Sakhalin Island & Kuril Islands — Far Eastern islands; Kurils disputed with Japan. (3)

Arctic & Northern

Siberia — vast region east of the Urals to the Pacific; home of the boreal taiga, gulags, and the Trans-Siberian Railway (longest in the world); the Baikal-Amur Mainline is a parallel route. (8)

Novaya Zemlya — Arctic archipelago between Barents and Kara Seas; Soviet nuclear test site (including the Tsar Bomba). (3)

Franz Josef Land — Arctic island archipelago named for the Habsburg emperor. (1)

Wrangel Island — Arctic UNESCO site; last refuge of woolly mammoths. (1)

Lake Vostok — subglacial lake under the Antarctic ice; Russian research station above. (3)

History & Politics

Aleutian Sale (1867) — Russia sold Alaska to the United States, including the former capital of Russian America, Sitka. (2)

Trans-Siberian Railway — Moscow to Vladivostok; defended in the Russian Civil War by the Czech Legion of Alexander Kolchak; the Baikal-Amur Mainline is a parallel route; Chita and Ulan-Ude grew around it. (1)

Invasion of Ukraine (2022-) — annexed Crimea (2014); full-scale invasion in 2022. (4)

Rwanda 19
Republic of Rwanda · East Africa (Great Lakes) · Capital: Kigali
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Kigali — recently hosted the Kigali Amendment convention banning HFC refrigerants. (1)

Nickname: 'Land of a Thousand Hills'. (1)

Government: ruled by Paul Kagame (RPF) since the end of the genocide. (1)

1994 Genocide — Hutu extremists killed ~800,000 Tutsis and moderate Hutus. (1)

Geography

Lake Kivu — western border with the DRC; CO₂-saturated 'killer lake' that could experience limnic eruptions; largest island Idjwi; ports Goma (DRC) and Bukavu (DRC). (2)

Lake Muhazi — eastern lake; Gahini mission founded by the Church Missionary Society. (1)

Kagera River — northern tributary of Lake Victoria; namesake Akagera National Park is on the Tanzanian border. (1)

Volcanoes National Park (formerly Kagera NP) — site of Dian Fossey's mountain-gorilla research in the Virunga Mountains. (2)

People

Hutu majority and Tutsi minority — both speak Kinyarwanda. (2)

Banyamulenge — Rwanda-Burundi Tutsis in the eastern DRC (South Kivu). (1)

Federation of Saint Christopher and Nevis · Caribbean (Leeward Islands) · Capital: Basseterre
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Basseterre — on Saint Kitts. (1)

Two islands: Saint Kitts (Saint Christopher) and Nevis, separated by a 2-mile channel. (1)

Geography

Brimstone Hill Fortress — UNESCO World Heritage Site; nicknamed the 'Gibraltar of the Caribbean'; overlooked by Mount Liamuiga. (1)

Mount Liamuiga — Saint Kitts' highest peak; offers views of Sint Eustatius and Saba. (1)

Nevis — sister island; Pinney Beach; the legend of Jamestown destroyed by a tsunami; parishes including Saint James Windward and Saint George Gingerland; birthplace of Alexander Hamilton. (1)

Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Castries. (1)

Nickname: 'Helen of the West Indies' — for changing hands between Britain and France 14 times. (1)

Geography

The Pitons — twin volcanic plugs (Gros Piton and Petit Piton); UNESCO World Heritage Site. (1)

Vieux Fort — southern town; home of Hewanorra International Airport. (1)

Saint Vincent and the Grenadines 4
Caribbean (Windward Islands) · Capital: Kingstown
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Kingstown — on the main island of Saint Vincent. (1)

Composition: the main island plus the northern Grenadines chain (Bequia, Mustique, Canouan, Mayreau, Union Island, Petit Saint Vincent); southern Grenadines are part of Grenada. (1)

Geography & Heritage

La Soufrière — active stratovolcano dominating Saint Vincent; Chateaubelair fishing village lies south of it. (1)

'Black Caribs' (Garifuna) — historically sailed from Bequia to Saint Vincent; in 1797 ~5,000 were exiled to Honduras after fighting the British. (1)

Mustique — private island resort popular with British royalty and celebrities. (1)

Samoa 15
Independent State of Samoa · Polynesia (South Pacific) · Capital: Apia
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Apia — on Upolu island. (1)

Two main islands: Savai'i (largest, contains Mt. Silisili highest peak) and Upolu. (1)

Date line jump: moved across the International Date Line in 2011 to align trading days with NZ/Australia. (1)

Drives on the left: in 2009 Samoa controversially switched from right- to left-hand driving (the People's Party formed to oppose it). (1)

Geography & Politics

American Samoa — separate US unincorporated territory east of Samoa proper; capital Pago Pago on Tutuila; Swains Island is administratively part of American Samoa though geographically with Tokelau. (2)

1918 flu — under Governor John Poyer, American Samoa recorded no Spanish Flu deaths. (1)

Culture

Robert Louis Stevenson — author lived in Vailima and is buried on Mount Vaea. (1)

Manu Samoa — national rugby team; pre-match Siva Tau dance. (1)

Most Serene Republic of San Marino · Italian enclave microstate · Capital: San Marino
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: San Marino — atop Monte Titano. (1)

Government: the world's oldest republic (founded 301 AD by St. Marinus); led by two Captains Regent elected every 6 months; formerly led by the Arengo assembly of powerful families. (1)

Enclave — surrounded entirely by Italy. (2)

Geography

Monte Titano — UNESCO-listed; three peaks each crowned by a tower (Guaita, Cesta, Montale) depicted on the flag. (1)

Saudi Arabia 47
Kingdom of Saudi Arabia · Arabian Peninsula · Capital: Riyadh
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Riyadh — Kingdom Centre with the spectacular bridge SkyDeck. (1)

Government: absolute monarchy under the Al Saud dynasty; current King Salman, de facto ruler Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman. (1)

Holy cities: custodian of Mecca (Makkah) and Medina (Madinah) — Islam's two holiest cities; Mecca houses the Kaaba at the Grand Mosque. (1)

Cities

Jeddah — Red Sea port; once held the world's tallest flagpole (surpassing Dushanbe, Baku, and Panmunjom); the Jeddah Tower is planned as the world's first 1-km building; world's highest fountain (King Fahd's Fountain). (1)

Dhahran & Khobar — Eastern Province oil-industry cities; connected to Bahrain via the King Fahd Causeway. (2)

Neom — planned futuristic megacity in the northwest; includes 'The Line' linear city project. (1)

Geography

Rub' al Khali ('Empty Quarter') — world's largest contiguous sand desert; Liwa Oasis Y-shaped oasis belt; home of the Bani Yas and Al Murrah Bedouin. (1)

Nafud Desert — northern desert. (1)

Hejaz — western coastal region containing Mecca and Medina. (1)

Najd — central plateau containing Riyadh. (1)

Asir Mountains — southwestern range bordering Yemen; only forested area. (1)

Red Sea coast — long western coastline; Bab al-Mandab Strait at the southern end. (1)

Resources

Aramco — world's largest oil company; Ghawar Field is the world's largest conventional oil field. (1)

Almarai — major dairy company; world's largest vertically integrated dairy operation. (1)

Senegal 32
Republic of Senegal · West Africa (Atlantic) · Capital: Dakar
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Dakar — on the Cap-Vert Peninsula (westernmost point of mainland Africa); southern terminus of the historic Paris-Dakar Rally; Ouakam suburb contains the 49-meter African Renaissance Monument built by North Korea's Mansudae company; nearby Gorée Island has the House of Slaves museum. (3)

People: the only country where Wolof are a majority ethnic group; home of the historic Wolof Confederacy. (2)

Government: former French colony; the Casamance region in the south seeks independence. (1)

Geography

Senegal River — northern border with Mauritania; rises in Guinea's Fouta Djallon; nicknamed 'River of Gold'; Langue de Barbarie sandspit at the mouth; Faidherbe Bridge crosses to Saint-Louis (Ndar); Djoudj National Bird Sanctuary at the delta. (2)

Gambia — the country almost entirely encloses The Gambia along the Gambia River. (1)

Saint-Louis — UNESCO former colonial capital on the Senegal River. (1)

Serbia 17

Balkans

At a Glance

Capital: Belgrade (Beograd) — built around the Roman settlement of Singidunum; at the confluence of the Sava and Danube rivers; Kalmegdan Fortress; Ada Ciganlija river island. (1)

Drina River — western border with Bosnia; spanned by the 16th-century Mehmed Paša Sokolović Bridge (UNESCO; setting of Ivo Andrić's The Bridge on the Drina). (1)

Đeravica — country's highest peak (in Kosovo's Prokletije range under Serbian view). (1)

Seychelles 16

Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Victoria — on Mahé, the largest island. (1)

Smallest African country by both area and population. (1)

Composition: 115 islands divided into the Inner Islands (granitic; Mahé, Praslin, La Digue) and the Outer Islands (coralline atolls including Aldabra). (1)

Flag: five brightly colored triangles diverging from the lower-left corner. (1)

Wildlife & Geography

Aldabra Atoll — UNESCO World Heritage Site; famous for its endemic Giant Tortoise species (rivals only the Galapagos'). (2)

Coco de Mer — endemic palm of Praslin; produces the world's heaviest seed (up to 65 lb). (1)

Jellyfish Tree — endemic critically endangered tree. (1)

Bird Island & Silhouette Island — major outlying islands. (1)

Capital: Jinan — on the Yellow River. (1)

Qufu — birthplace of Confucius. (1)

Hainan Province

Hainan Island — China's southernmost province; tropical island. (2)

Capital: Haikou. (1)

Nanwan Monkey Island — actually a peninsula despite the name. (1)

Sanya — tropical beach-resort city at the southern tip. (1)

Shanghai 7
Largest city in China · Direct-controlled municipality · Pudong financial hub
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Largest Chinese city and world's busiest container port. (2)

Huangpu River — flows through the city, separating historic Puxi (west) from modern Pudong (east); Suzhou Creek is a major tributary. (4)

Hangzhou Bay — south of the city. (1)

Lujiazui — Pudong financial district with the famous skyline. (2)

Shanghai World Financial Center — 'bottle-opener' supertall. (1)

Shanghai Tower — China's tallest building (2014), designed by Jun Xia; spiraling form. (1)

Heritage & Districts

The Bund — historic Zhongshan Road waterfront in the former International Settlement. (2)

Republic of Sierra Leone · West Africa · Capital: Freetown
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Freetown — descendants of the Nova Scotian settlers (freed African American Loyalists resettled by the British in 1792) still gather under the city's symbol of freedom, the Cotton Tree; John Clarkson helped found it. (1)

Civil War (1991-2002) — the Revolutionary United Front (RUF) funded the war with blood diamonds, backed by Liberia's Charles Taylor. (1)

Geography

Mano, Moro, and Moa rivers form the southeastern border with Liberia. (1)

Mount Bintumani — highest peak in West Africa west of Cameroon (in the Loma Mountains). (1)
