Sikkim 7
Northeast India · Capital: Gangtok
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Gangtok. (1)

Region: The 'brother' state of India's Seven Sister States of the NE. (1)

Highest point of India: Kangchenjunga — the world's 3rd-tallest mountain; partly in Sikkim. (3)

Language: A majority of residents speak Nepali. (1)

Distinction: Chief producer of cardamom in Asia. (1)

Geography

Kangchenjunga — delineated by the Tamur and Teesta Rivers; tourists view its SE face from the Goecha La pass; held the title 'highest in the world' until 1852. (2)

Nathu La — Sikkim's 'listening ears pass'; once traversed by the Ancient Tea Horse Road. (1)

The Brahmaputra basin (above Sikkim, in Tibet) feeds Kanchenjunga's drainage on the Indian side. (1)

Government & Environment

The state's traditional monarch was known as the Chogyal, who lived in Gangtok. (1)

Sikkim has a unilateral ban on styrofoam and has distributed bamboo water bottles to prevent plastic pollution. (2)

Singapore 26
Republic of Singapore · Southeast Asian city-state · Capital: Singapore
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

City-state: tip of the Malay Peninsula; separated from Malaysia by the Strait of Johor; near the Strait of Malacca. (2)

Population: highly multicultural — Chinese majority plus Malay, Indian, Eurasian communities. (1)

Currency: Singapore Dollar (the Brunei Dollar is pegged 1:1). (1)

Highest GDP per capita in Asia; HQ of Temasek Holdings sovereign wealth fund. (1)

Landmarks & Districts

Marina Bay Sands — Moshe Safdie-designed integrated resort with the iconic ship-shaped SkyPark. (1)

Gardens by the Bay — botanical complex with the Supertree Grove and Cloud Forest dome. (1)

Singapore Flyer — 165-m observation Ferris wheel. (1)

Raffles Hotel — colonial-era luxury hotel where the Singapore Sling was invented. (1)

The Pinnacle@Duxton — world's tallest public housing complex. (1)

Changi Airport — consistently rated the world's best airport. (1)

Little India — anchored on Serangoon Road; Tekka is its local nickname. (1)

Sentosa — resort island; site of the 2018 Trump-Kim summit. (1)

Geography

Sungei Buloh Wetland Reserve & Bukit Timah Nature Reserve — protected wildlife areas. (1)

Pulau Ujong — main island. (1)

Slovakia 14
Slovak Republic · Central Europe · Capital: Bratislava
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: Bratislava — on the Danube at the confluence with the Morava River; early coins by the Boii Gallic tribe depicted King Biatec; famous Čumil sewer-worker statue. (2)

Independence: peacefully separated from Czechia in 1993 in the Velvet Divorce. (1)

Geography

Tatras (High Tatras) — northern range shared with Poland; Gerlachovský štít is the highest peak; Mount Kriváň appears on the 1-euro coin. (2)

Demänovská Ice Cave (Dobšinská) — where folk hero Samuel Valko allegedly rescued royals. (1)

Danube — southern border with Hungary. (1)

Cities & Culture

Košice — second-largest city in eastern Slovakia. (1)

Prešov — third-largest city. (1)

Juraj Jánošík — folk Robin-Hood-like hero. (1)

Europe

At a Glance

Culture: Kurentovanje Festival in Ptuj features demon-costumed dancers chasing away winter. (1)

Geography

Karst region — gave its name to karst topography; the Škocjan Caves are UNESCO-listed; Postojna Cave is huge tourist draw; Lake Cerknica is a windsurfing destination on a karst polje. (2)

Soča River — flows through Slovenia's Alpine valley before joining the Adriatic in Italy. (1)

Adriatic coast — short coastline including the Gulf of Trieste; main port Koper. (1)

Regions

At a Glance

Cradle of Humankind — UNESCO site with hominid fossils. (1)

Wildlife & History

Apartheid — racial segregation regime (1948-1994); ended by Nelson Mandela. (1)

Afrikaners — Dutch-Boer descendants; founded the Orange Free State, Transvaal, Stellaland, and Goshen republics; led by Piet Cronjé in the Second Boer War. (1)

China (Regions)

Yunnan

Capital: Kunming — site of the 2014 East Turkestan Islamic Movement attack. (1)

Three Parallel Rivers — UNESCO-listed corridor where the Jinsha (upper Yangtze), Lancang (Mekong), and Nujiang (Salween) flow within ~80 km of each other. (1)

Tiger Leaping Gorge — one of the world's deepest river canyons (Jinsha River). (1)

Chengjiang fauna — Cambrian fossil bed at Maotianshan. (1)

Sichuan

Capital: Chengdu — site of the New Century Global Center, the world's largest building by floor area. (1)

Sichuan Cuisine — distinguished by mapo tofu, kung pao chicken, and the 'strange-taste' (guaiwei) spice mixture; broad-bean chili paste; Sichuan peppercorns. (1)

Giant Panda — endemic to Sichuan's bamboo forests (Wolong, Bifengxia reserves). (2)

Panzhihua — growing Christian minority. (1)

Chongqing

Direct-controlled municipality — separated from Sichuan in 1997; one of the four such municipalities (with Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin). (1)

Confluence of the Yangtze and Jialing rivers — the upper Yangtze flows past here. (2)

Great Hall of the People — modeled after Beijing's Temple of Heaven; the city's main political meeting hall. (1)

World's largest monorail system. (1)

Dazu Rock Carvings — UNESCO 7th-century Buddhist carvings ~100 mi west on Mount Baoding. (1)

WWII history — provisional capital of the Republic of China during the Second Sino-Japanese War. (1)

Tamil Nadu 19
Southernmost mainland Indian state · Capital: Chennai
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Chennai (historic Madras) — on the Coromandel Coast of the Bay of Bengal. (4)

Southernmost mainland point of India: Kanyakumari (Cape Comorin), in this state. (1)

Borders: Kerala (W), Karnataka (NW), Andhra Pradesh (N); the union territory of Puducherry is embedded within it. (3)

Strait: Palk Strait separates the state from Sri Lanka; Adam's Bridge (a chain of limestone shoals) once connected the two until a 1480 cyclone. (3)

Major cities: Chennai, Coimbatore, Madurai — Madurai nicknamed 'Thoonga Nagaram' ('the city that never sleeps'). (2)

Physical Geography

Rivers — the Kaveri (Cauvery) splits into distributaries such as the Kollidam; the Vaigai empties into the Palk Strait. (2)

Mountains — contains the junction of the Eastern and Western Ghats. (1)

Cauvery dispute — Tamil Nadu and Karnataka have feuded for decades over the river's waters. (1)

Telugu Ganga — a project from neighbouring Andhra Pradesh that diverts Krishna River water to Chennai. (1)

Chennai (Madras)

Fort St. George — historic British East India Company fort, foundational structure of Madras. (1)

George Town — historic neighbourhood; contains Parry's Corner port district, named for an 18th-c. Welsh merchant. (1)

Ripon Building (neoclassical, foundation laid by Lord Minto), Dr. M.G.R. Railway Station, ITC Grand Chola Hotel, Adyar Cancer Institute. (1)

Mahabalipuram — UNESCO temple complex just south of the city. (1)

Tamil cinema (Kollywood) — based in Chennai; produced political stars including Vijayakanth and Jayaram Jayalalithaa. (2)

People & Culture

Tamil people — Dravidian-speaking ethnic group of the south; built the absurdly colorful Meenakshi Temple at Madurai; literary Sangam period predates the Five Great Epics (incl. Ilango Adigal's 'Tale of an Anklet'). (2)

Historic empires — Chera, Chola, Pallava — Tamil-speaking states. (2)

'Eelam' — proposed Tamil homeland; LTTE insurgency in Sri Lanka was conducted by ethnic Tamils. (2)

Sri Ranganathaswamy Temple — on an island between the Kollidam and Kaveri rivers; the world's largest functioning Hindu temple. (1)

Puducherry (Pondicherry)

French colonial city embedded as a UT inside Tamil Nadu; landmarks include the Romain Rolland Library and the Notre Dame des Anges cathedral; royalist bastion under governor Venant de Durfort. (1)

Tanzania 62
United Republic of Tanzania · East Africa · Capital: Dodoma
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Dodoma — central capital since 1996. (1)

Largest city: Dar es Salaam — major Indian Ocean port; Kariakoo Market; districts include Temeke and Kinondoni; dala dala minibus transit; ferries to Stone Town on Zanzibar's Unguja Island. (2)

Formation: mainland Tanganyika united with the islands of Zanzibar in 1964 to form Tanzania. (1)

Geography

Mount Kilimanjaro — Africa's highest peak; Kibo, Mawenzi, and Shira are its three peaks; once named for Kaiser Wilhelm. (2)

Mount Meru — second-highest peak. (1)

Lake Victoria — northern border; world's 2nd-largest freshwater lake; source of the White Nile. (1)

Lake Tanganyika — western border; world's 2nd-deepest lake; receives the Malagarasi River; Kigoma rail hub; Ujiji is where Stanley met Livingstone. (2)

Lake Malawi (Nyasa) — southern border lake. (1)

Serengeti — vast plain; site of the Great Migration; bordering Maasai Mara (Kenya); contains the Ngorongoro Crater (formed by an exploded volcano collapsing). (2)

Zanzibar

Zanzibar Archipelago — comprises Unguja, Pemba, and Mafia Islands; Stone Town (UNESCO); House of Wonders; Beit al-Sahel palace; 38-minute war with Britain (shortest war in history). (3)

Tarambeta — historic Sultan-of-Oman residence. (1)

People

Maasai — pastoral people of the Serengeti. (1)

Swahili — main national language; widely spoken throughout East Africa. (1)

Tasmania 7
Island State of Australia · Capital: Hobart · Formerly Van Diemen's Land
Australia (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Hobart — on the Derwent River, beneath Mount Wellington. (7)

Originally named Van Diemen's Land (for a Dutch East India Company leader); renamed for Dutch explorer Abel Tasman. (3)

Smallest Australian state by area; lies south of the Bass Strait at the southern end of the Indian/Pacific Ocean boundary above the Southern Ocean. (4)

Cities: Launceston in the north; Penguin and Devonport on the north coast; Strahan is a west-coast fishing town; Clarence is on the Coal River. (2)

Physical Geography

Mount Ossa — Tasmania's highest point, in the Pellion Range. (2)

King David's Peak — in Walls of Jerusalem National Park. (1)

Derwent River — descends from Mt. Ossa to Storm Bay, passing Hobart and Montague Bay. (3)

Esk River — drains the north. (1)

Lake St. Clair — the country's deepest lake. (1)

Maria Island — off the east coast; Flinders Island lies in Bass Strait (Truganini and other natives were evacuated there by George Augustus Robinson); Savage River National Park in the west. (2)

Forestier Peninsula — site of the colonial-era 'Black Line'. (1)

Upper Florentine Valley — old-growth forest at the center of logging controversy. (1)

Wildlife

Tasmanian devil (Sarcophilus harrisii) — largest extant carnivorous marsupial; native to the island. (2)

Thylacine ('Tasmanian tiger') — Australia's largest carnivorous marsupial until extinction in 1936. (2)

Culture & History

Museum of Old and New Art (MONA) — the Southern Hemisphere's largest private collection; on the Derwent; houses the controversial Cloaca machine; accessed by ferry. (2)

Port Arthur — historic convict settlement; site of a 1996 mass shooting that led to Australia's strict gun-control laws. (2)

Incat — catamaran manufacturer based here. (1)

Par-Avion airline is based in the state. (1)

Murchison Highway crosses Hellyer Gorge; John Franklin briefly governed the colony. (1)

Tennessee 30
'The Volunteer State' · Upper South · Capital: Nashville
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Nashville — 'Music City'; Grand Ole Opry, Country Music Hall of Fame, Ryman Auditorium. (1)

Largest city: Memphis — on the Mississippi River; Graceland (Elvis's mansion); Lorraine Motel (where MLK was assassinated, now the National Civil Rights Museum); Mud Island peninsula in Harbor Town; the Memphis Pyramid (largest in America, owned by Bass Pro Shops). (3)

Other cities: Knoxville (1982 World's Fair), Chattanooga, Clarksville. (1)

Geography

Great Smoky Mountains National Park — most-visited US national park; shared with North Carolina; Clingmans Dome is the highest point in Tennessee. (2)

Cumberland Plateau — central uplands. (1)

Barkley Marathons — ultramarathon in Frozen Head State Park; inspired by an escape from the Brushy Mountain State Penitentiary. (1)

Reelfoot Lake — created by the 1811-12 New Madrid earthquakes. (1)

Mississippi River — western border. (1)

Tennessee River — main interior river; runs west into Kentucky. (1)

Industry & Heritage

Oak Ridge National Laboratory — site of WWII uranium enrichment for the Manhattan Project; home of the Summit supercomputer. (1)

Jack Daniel's — distillery in Lynchburg. (1)

Dollywood — Pigeon Forge theme park named for Dolly Parton. (1)

Texas 70
'The Lone Star State' · South-Central US · Capital: Austin
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Austin — largest US city without an MLB/NFL/NBA/NHL team; Dell HQ in Round Rock suburb; longest-running PBS music show is Austin City Limits. (1)

Largest city: Houston — Gulf port; NASA Johnson Space Center. (1)

Other major metros: Dallas-Fort Worth (Reunion Tower, Bank of America Plaza, AT&T Stadium, Sixth Floor Museum at Dealey Plaza), San Antonio (Alamo, River Walk, Fort Sam Houston), El Paso (across from Ciudad Juárez). (2)

Second-largest US state by area and population. (1)

Geography

Rio Grande — forms the entire southern border with Mexico. (1)

Lower Rio Grande Valley — at the southern tip; Playa Bagdad historic landing; SpaceX Boca Chica (Starbase) launch site; Tamaulipas is the Mexican counterpart. (1)

Big Bend National Park — Chihuahuan Desert park along the Rio Grande. (1)

Texas Panhandle — northern flat plains; Palo Duro Canyon (Texas's 'Grand Canyon'); the Red River's Prairie Dog Town Fork flows through. (1)

Gulf Coast — long Gulf of Mexico coastline; Galveston Bay; South Padre Island barrier. (1)

Hill Country — central scenic region; LBJ Ranch. (1)

Sabine River — eastern border with Louisiana. (1)

Guadalupe Peak — highest point in the state; in Guadalupe Mountains National Park. (1)

Industry & History

Oil & gas — Spindletop discovery (1901) launched the Texas oil industry; major refining at Houston, Beaumont, Port Arthur. (1)

Republic of Texas — independent from Mexico (1836-1845). (1)

Camp Verde — historic site of the US Army Camel Corps experiment. (1)

Thailand 41
Kingdom of Thailand · Southeast Asia · Capital: Bangkok
East & Southeast Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Bangkok — on the Chao Phraya River; Grand Palace with the Emerald Buddha; Wat Pho (Reclining Buddha); Lumpini Stadium for Muay Thai; CentralWorld mall. (1)

Government: constitutional monarchy under the Chakri dynasty. (1)

Distinction: the only Southeast Asian country never colonized by a European power. (1)

Geography

Mekong River — forms much of the eastern border with Laos. (1)

Phuket — large Andaman-coast island; Mai Khao Beach famous for close-up plane landings; on the Phang Nga Peninsula. (2)

Ko Samui & Ko Phangan — Gulf of Thailand resort islands. (1)

Isthmus of Kra — narrow southern land bridge linking the Malay Peninsula. (1)

Chiang Mai — northern cultural capital. (1)

Golden Triangle — opium-trade region at the meeting of Thailand, Laos, and Myanmar. (1)

Khao Lak — Andaman Sea resort area devastated by the 2004 Boxing Day Tsunami. (1)

Heritage

Ayutthaya — UNESCO ancient Siamese capital ruins north of Bangkok. (1)

Sukhothai — UNESCO 13th-century capital. (1)

Muay Thai — Thai national sport. (1)

Tibet 6
'Roof of the World' · Capital: Lhasa
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Lhasa — site of the Potala Palace, traditional residence of the Dalai Lama. (3)

Three historical regions: Ü-Tsang (centered around Lhasa, Shigatse), Kham, and Amdo (now mostly in Qinghai/Sichuan). (3)

Tibetan diaspora — government-in-exile led by the Dalai Lama is based in Dharamsala, India. (1)

Shigatse — historical capital of the Tsang region; seat of the Panchen Lama. (1)

Geography

Tibetan Plateau — average elevation > 4,500 m; 'Third Pole'. (2)

Mount Kailash — sacred peak in southwestern Tibet; holy to Hindus, Buddhists, Jains, and Bon practitioners; source of multiple major Asian rivers. (1)

Lake Manasarovar — sacred Bon lake fed by the Kailash glacier. (2)

Yarlung Tsangpo River — the upper portion of the Brahmaputra. (1)

Mount Everest (Chomolungma) — on the Tibet–Nepal border. (2)

Kunlun Mountains — separate Tibet from the Tarim Basin (Xinjiang). (1)

Pangong Tso — high-altitude lake disputed with India; site of bloody border clashes since 2020. (1)

Aksai Chin — China-administered region claimed by India. (1)

Buddhism & Culture

Vajrayana Buddhism — the Rimé movement unifies the Nyingma, Kagyu, Sakya, and Gelug schools. (2)

Ngöndro — preparatory tantric exercise ('secret mantra'). (1)

Pre-Buddhist Zhangzhung & Bon religion — Bon tradition centers on Mt. Kailash and Lake Manasarovar. (1)

Tsampa — staple food of roasted barley flour; guthuk is a traditional noodle soup. (1)

Xining-Lhasa railway — high-altitude railway connecting Tibet to the Chinese rail network. (1)

Togolese Republic · West Africa · Capital: Lomé
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Lomé — on the Bight of Benin coast. (1)

Former colony: German Togoland was split between France and Britain after WWI; the British portion became part of Ghana, the French portion became modern Togo. (1)

Cities & Geography

Sokodé — second-largest town; near the source of the Mono River, dammed by the Nangbéto. (1)

Aného — former capital; lagoon town in the southeast. (1)

Dapaong — major town in the far north. (1)

Vogan — lake town known for its Friday fetish market. (1)

Atakora Mountains / Togo Mountains — northern range running into Benin and Ghana; Mount Agou is the country's highest peak. (1)

Politics

Gnassingbé dynasty — Eyadéma Gnassingbé ruled 1967-2005, succeeded by his son Faure. (1)

ECOWAS — Togo is a member of the West African economic bloc. (1)

Tonga 11
Kingdom of Tonga · Polynesia (South Pacific) · Capital: Nuku'alofa
Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Nuku'alofa — on Tongatapu, the main island. (1)

Government: only constitutional monarchy in the Pacific; ruled by the House of Tupou (the only royal house in Polynesia never to be overthrown by a colonial power). (1)

Geography

Three island groups: Tongatapu (south, with the capital), Haʻapai (central), and Vavaʻu (north). (1)

Hunga Tonga–Hunga Haʻapai — submarine volcano whose massive January 2022 eruption was one of the largest of the 21st century; the namesake island gained hundreds of square meters of land from earlier eruptions. (1)

Republic of Minerva — failed 1972 libertarian micronation attempt on coral reefs claimed by Tonga. (1)

Culture

'Friendly Islands' — name given by Captain Cook. (1)

Manu Sipi rugby league team — historically strong international rugby. (1)

Republic of Trinidad and Tobago · Caribbean (Lesser Antilles) · Capital: Port of Spain
Caribbean

At a Glance

Capital: Port of Spain — on Trinidad. (1)

Position: southernmost Caribbean country, just off the Venezuelan coast; separated by the Gulf of Paria. (1)

Religion: Hinduism is the largest minority faith. (1)

Geography

Trinidad — larger southern island; separated from Venezuela by the Serpent's Mouth and Dragon's Mouth straits. (2)

Pitch Lake — largest natural asphalt deposit in the world; in southwestern Trinidad ('La Brea' / New Jersey). (1)

Tobago — smaller northern island. (1)

Culture

Calypso music — origin of the genre; Extempo Monarch competition at Carnival. (1)

Steel pan / steel drum — invented here. (1)

Carnival — second-largest in the world after Rio's. (1)

V.S. Naipaul — Trinidadian Nobel laureate; from the ethnically Indian Capildeo family of Lion House. (1)

New Courland — short-lived 17th-century Couronian colony on Tobago. (1)

Economy

Oil & natural gas — major exporter (the most industrialized Caribbean economy). (1)

At a Glance

Turkey 64
Republic of Türkiye · Transcontinental (Asia/Europe) · Capital: Ankara
Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Ankara. (1)

Largest city: Istanbul — transcontinental city spanning Europe and Asia; the Bosphorus Strait divides them; former capital of the Byzantine and Ottoman Empires. (1)

Three straits: the Bosphorus and Dardanelles flank the Sea of Marmara; together they're the Turkish Straits. (2)

Istanbul

Hagia Sophia (Ayasofya) — Byzantine cathedral / Ottoman mosque / museum / mosque again (2020). (1)

Blue Mosque (Sultan Ahmed Mosque) — Ottoman imperial mosque opposite Hagia Sophia. (1)

Topkapı Palace — Ottoman sultans' palace. (1)

Grand Bazaar — one of the world's oldest covered markets. (1)

Geography

Sea of Marmara — separates European Thrace from Asian Anatolia. (1)

Dardanelles — strait between Marmara and the Aegean; site of the WWI Gallipoli Campaign (ANZAC Cove, Cape Helles); flanked by Çanakkale; spanned by the new Çanakkale Bridge; historically the Sea of Helle. (2)

Bosphorus — strait between Marmara and the Black Sea; divides Istanbul. (1)

Black Sea coast — northern coast. (1)

Aegean Sea — separates Turkey from Greece; nearby islands Chios and Rhodes lie just off the Turkish coast (but belong to Greece). (1)

Mediterranean coast — southern Turkish Riviera; Lycian Way trail in the southwest; cities Antalya, Bodrum. (1)

Anatolian Plateau — central highlands of Asia Minor. (1)

Mount Ararat — eastern peak on the Armenian border; traditional resting place of Noah's Ark; in Ağrı and Iğdır Provinces. (1)

Lake Van — large saline lake; site of the historic Urartu kingdom; Aghtamar Island has the Armenian Cathedral of the Holy Cross. (1)

Cappadocia — central region of 'fairy-chimney' rock formations and cave dwellings. (1)

Eastern Thrace — Turkey's small European territory. (1)

Cities & Heritage

Ephesus — UNESCO ancient Greek city near Selçuk. (1)

Troy — Bronze-Age city excavated by Schliemann near Çanakkale. (1)

Göbekli Tepe — Neolithic temple complex (~9500 BC) in Şanlıurfa. (1)

Pamukkale — travertine thermal pools at ancient Hierapolis. (1)

People

Kurds — large minority in southeastern Turkey; PKK insurgent group led by Abdullah Öcalan (held on a prison island in the Sea of Marmara). (2)

Hizmet movement — Gülen-led group runs 100+ US charter schools. (1)

Turkmenistan 21
Central Asia · Capital: Ashgabat
Central Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Ashgabat — known as the 'White City' after being rebuilt from white marble after the 1948 earthquake under Saparmurat Niyazov; in the Ahal Region in the foothills of the Kopet Dag; on the Amu Darya basin; Oguzhan Presidential Palace. (2)

Government: post-Soviet dictatorship; the Rukhnama was Niyazov's required-reading 'spiritual guide'. (1)

Borders: Caspian Sea (west), Kazakhstan (NE), Uzbekistan (E), Iran and Afghanistan (S). (1)

Geography

Karakum Desert — covers ~70% of the country; contains the Uly Balkan range with Mount Arlan; the Sarygamysh Lake lies to the north. (2)

Darvaza ('Door to Hell') — natural-gas crater set on fire since 1971 in the Karakum. (1)

Caspian Sea — western coast; the Kara-Bogaz-Gol is a salty lagoon shared with Kazakhstan. (2)

Kopet Dag — mountain range on the Iranian border. (1)

Amu Darya — main river; ancient Oxus. (1)

Economy

Natural gas — one of the world's largest gas reserves (Galkynysh field). (1)

Akhal-Teke horses — prized breed; depicted on the national emblem. (1)

Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Funafuti. (1)

Former name: Ellice Islands (the Gilbert and Ellice Islands colony split into Tuvalu and Kiribati). (1)

Position: in free association with New Zealand for defense. (1)

Geography

One of the smallest countries by area and population; fourth-smallest country overall. (1)

Climate threat — extremely low elevation (max ~15 ft); future submersion is the central national concern. (1)

Economy

Domain name: the .tv ccTLD is heavily licensed (notably by Twitch and other media companies). (1)

Uganda 24

Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Kampala — on the northern shore of Lake Victoria. (1)

Government: ruled by Yoweri Museveni since 1986. (1)

Geography

Lake Kyoga, Lake Albert (shared with DRC, fed by the Semliki), Lake Edward — Great Lakes within Uganda. (1)

Queen Elizabeth National Park — famous for tree-climbing lions near the Ishasha River. (1)

Bwindi Impenetrable Forest — UNESCO; mountain-gorilla habitat. (1)

Ukraine 31

Former Soviet Bloc

At a Glance

Capital: Kyiv (Kiev) — on the Dnieper River; Saint Sophia Cathedral; Kyiv Pechersk Lavra; Maidan Nezalezhnosti (Independence Square). (1)

Russian Invasion (2022-) — full-scale invasion building on the 2014 annexation of Crimea and Russian-backed Donbas conflict. (1)

Geography

Dnieper River — major river bisecting the country; flows to the Black Sea. (1)

Black Sea coast — southern coastline; Odesa is the main port. (1)

Sea of Azov — secondary northern arm of the Black Sea; Mariupol sits on it. (1)

Carpathian Mountains — western extension into Ukraine. (1)

Crimean Peninsula — annexed by Russia (2014); connected by the Isthmus of Perekop; Feodosia (formerly Cafa) is a former Greek/Genoese colony; Gulf of Kerch and Strait of Kerch separate it from Russia. (2)

Cities

Lviv — western city in historic Galicia; Polish heritage; Rynok Square with the Black House; Potocki Palace. (1)

Kharkiv — second city in the northeast. (1)

Odesa — Black Sea cultural port with the Potemkin Stairs. (1)

Mariupol — Sea of Azov port; Illich Steel and Iron Works; site of the 2022 siege; claimed by Donetsk Pushilin 'people's republic'. (1)

Chernobyl

Chernobyl Nuclear Power Plant — 1986 meltdown; the Elephant's Foot corium mass; New Safe Confinement sarcophagus; the abandoned worker city of Pripyat; tourists became popular after Elena Filatova's motorcycle account. (2)

United Kingdom 36
United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland · Capital: London
Europe

At a Glance

Capital: London — on the Thames; Tower Bridge, Tower of London, Westminster Abbey, Palace of Westminster, Buckingham Palace, The Shard (Renzo Piano-designed Western Europe's tallest skyscraper). (1)

Composition: England, Scotland, Wales, and Northern Ireland form the UK; the British Isles also include the Isle of Man and Channel Islands as Crown Dependencies. (1)

Constituent Countries

Scotland — capital Edinburgh; Highlands; Loch Ness; Ben Nevis is the UK's highest peak (in the Grampians/Munros, climbed via the Tower Ridge); the Great Glen Fault; flag the St Andrew's Cross saltire; islands include the Shetland Islands and the Hebrides. (1)

Wales — capital Cardiff; Snowdon is the most-climbed mountain; eisteddfods cultural gatherings; Hay-on-Wye literary festival; Gower Peninsula Neolithic burial chambers (cromlechs); Offa's Dyke; landlocked counties Gwynedd, Powys. (1)

Northern Ireland — capital Belfast; Giant's Causeway (UNESCO basalt columns). (1)

England — by far the largest constituent country. (1)

Geography

Severn River — UK's longest river. (1)

Thames River — flows through London. (1)

White Cliffs of Dover — chalk cliffs in Kent; subject of Vera Lynn's WWII song; portion collapsed at Crab Bay. (1)

Scilly Isles — UK's southernmost point; largest is St. Mary's. (1)

Isle of Anglesey — separated from Wales by the Menai Strait; Holyhead port; Welsh name Ynys Môn. (1)

Isle of Man — Crown Dependency in the Irish Sea; Tower of Refuge; WWII airfield at Jurby; TT motorcycle race. (1)

Overseas Territories

Gibraltar — at the southern tip of Spain; namesake 'Rock' is one of the Pillars of Hercules; Barbary Macaques. (1)

Falkland Islands — disputed with Argentina; capital Stanley. (1)

British Indian Ocean Territory — Chagos Archipelago including Diego Garcia. (1)

Bermuda, Cayman Islands, Turks & Caicos, British Virgin Islands, Anguilla, Montserrat — Caribbean territories. (1)

Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha — Atlantic territories; Tristan da Cunha's settlement of 'Edinburgh of the Seven Seas' was evacuated after a volcano destroyed it. (1)

United States 143
United States of America · North America · Capital: Washington, D.C.
North America

At a Glance

Capital: Washington, D.C. — federal district between Maryland and Virginia; National Mall lined with monuments and the Smithsonian museums; Capitol, White House, Lincoln Memorial, Washington Monument. (2)

50 states + DC + 5 inhabited territories (Puerto Rico, US Virgin Islands, Guam, Northern Mariana Islands, American Samoa). (1)

Currency: US dollar — also legal tender in Ecuador, El Salvador, Panama, Zimbabwe, and various territories. (1)

Borders: longest international borders are with Canada (5,525 mi — the world's longest) and Mexico (1,933 mi). The US-Canada border is mostly the 49th parallel; the US-Mexico border is partly the Rio Grande. (2)

Major Cities (Cross-State)

New York City — largest US city; Empire State Building, Statue of Liberty, Central Park, five boroughs (Manhattan, Brooklyn, Queens, Bronx, Staten Island). (2)

Los Angeles — second-largest US city; Hollywood, Pacific gateway. (1)

Chicago — Great Lakes metropolis on Lake Michigan; Willis (Sears) Tower; the historically Czech Pilsen neighborhood; Magnificent Mile & Millennium Park. (1)

Houston, Phoenix, Philadelphia, San Antonio (largest US 'second city'; Alamo Mission, Fort Sam Houston), San Diego, Dallas, San Jose, Austin. (1)

National Geography

Rocky Mountains — long western range from Canada through New Mexico. (1)

Appalachian Mountains — eastern range from Maine to Georgia. (1)

Sierra Nevada — California range with Yosemite and Mount Whitney (lower-48 highest peak). (1)

Cascade Range — Pacific Northwest volcanic chain (Rainier, Hood, Shasta, St. Helens). (1)

Mississippi-Missouri — longest river system in North America. (1)

Great Lakes — Superior, Huron, Michigan, Erie, Ontario. (1)

Great Plains — central farmland belt. (1)

Death Valley — Mojave/California; lowest land elevation in North America. (1)

Denali (Mt. McKinley) — Alaska; highest peak in North America. (1)

Mauna Kea / Mauna Loa — Hawaii; from the seafloor Mauna Kea is the tallest mountain on Earth. (1)

Outlying Territories

Alaska — purchased from Russia in 1867; former Russian-America capital Sitka; Aleutian Islands (Catherine Archipelago). (1)

Hawaii — Pacific archipelago of eight main islands. (1)

Puerto Rico — Caribbean territory; El Yunque National Forest; Vieques island. (1)

US Virgin Islands — bought from Denmark in 1917; St. Thomas, St. John, St. Croix; Trunk Bay turtle beaches. (1)

Guam — Pacific territory; Mt. Mataguac; Dulce Nombre de Maria Cathedral; Sergeant Yokoi was found in Talofofo Cave in 1972. (1)

American Samoa — Pacific territory; capital Pago Pago on Tutuila; recorded zero deaths from the 1918 Spanish Flu under Gov. John Poyer. (1)

Northern Mariana Islands — Pacific commonwealth; Saipan, Tinian (where the Enola Gay launched). (1)

State Files

Each US state has its own breakout JSON. See the State entries grouped under 'United States (States)' in the index. (1)

Oriental Republic of Uruguay · South America · Capital: Montevideo
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Montevideo — on the Río de la Plata; Legislative Palace. (1)

Position: smallest Spanish-speaking country in South America (after Suriname); between Brazil and Argentina; east of the Río de la Plata; only Americas country entirely south of the Tropic of Capricorn. (2)

Río Negro — main interior river. (1)

Heritage

1930 FIFA World Cup — Uruguay hosted and won the very first World Cup; also won 1950. (1)

'La Cumparsita' — Uruguay's most famous tango. (1)

2013 marijuana legalization — first country in the world to legalize recreational cannabis. (1)

General Artigas Bridge — links Uruguay to Argentina across the Uruguay River. (1)

Punta del Este — exclusive Atlantic resort. (1)

Utah 34
'The Beehive State' · Mountain West · Capital: Salt Lake City
United States (States)

At a Glance

Capital: Salt Lake City — global HQ of the LDS (Mormon) Church; Temple Square. (1)

Other cities: Provo (BYU; LaVell Edwards Stadium; on the Provo River and Uintah Mountains), Ogden, St. George. (1)

Geography

Wasatch Range — runs north-south along the Wasatch Front; highest peak Mount Nebo; Little Cottonwood Canyon ski areas (Snowbird, Alta); northernmost extremity is the Bear River Range. (2)

Great Salt Lake — largest saltwater lake in the Western Hemisphere; a remnant of ancient Lake Bonneville; sits in a wet endorheic basin. (1)

Bonneville Salt Flats — site of land-speed records. (1)

Five National Parks ('The Mighty Five'): Zion, Bryce Canyon, Arches, Canyonlands, Capitol Reef. (1)

Canyonlands National Park — at the confluence of the Green and Colorado rivers (the Green is the Colorado's largest tributary). (1)

Lake Powell — vast reservoir on the Colorado River (shared with Arizona). (1)

Heritage

Golden Spike — site at Promontory Summit where the Transcontinental Railroad was joined in 1869. (1)

Sundance Film Festival — held in Park City annually. (1)

Uttar Pradesh 14
Largest state in India · Capital: Lucknow
India (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Lucknow. (1)

Status: The world's most populous national subdivision; the largest state of India. (1)

In 2000, Uttarakhand broke away from Uttar Pradesh as a separate state. (1)

Major cities: Lucknow, Agra, Varanasi, Allahabad (Prayagraj), Kanpur, Ayodhya, Chitrakoot. (2)

Setting: Lies in the Ganges Plain; the Ganges and Yamuna both flow through it. (4)

Sacred Geography

Varanasi — sacred Hindu city on the Ganges where pilgrims cremate their dead on the river's banks; one of the Saptapuri (with Ayodhya, Kanchipuram). (4)

Ayodhya — on the Sarayu River; considered the birthplace of Rama. (2)

Allahabad (Prayag/Prayagraj) — built on the plan of ancient Prayag; one of the four sites of the Kumbh Mela pilgrimage. (1)

Agra

Taj Mahal — Mughal-era mausoleum built by Shah Jahan for his wife; white-marble onion domes; the only New Seven Wonder in South Asia; sits on a platform along the Yamuna River with the Mehtab Bagh gardens opposite. (3)

Bibi Ka Maqbara — half-size replica built by Aurangzeb a decade after the Taj. (1)

Modern issues — green stains from Chironomus calligraphus insects swarming on the Taj, traced to pollution in the Yamuna. (1)

Lucknow

Rumi Darwaza — 'the Turkish Gate', once mistakenly believed identical to a gate in Constantinople. (1)

Ghanta Ghar — the tallest clock tower in India. (1)

Dilkusha Kothi — ruins of a British residence besieged during the Indian Rebellion of 1857. (1)

History & Other

Predecessor entity: United Provinces of Agra and Audh. (1)

Rihand River — power generated in part by a coal plant named for it. (1)

Jalesar — town in UP that produces cast brass bells popular with Swiss cow farmers. (1)

JRDU (Chitrakoot) — world's first university dedicated solely to teaching disabled students. (1)

Uzbekistan 26
Republic of Uzbekistan · Central Asia · Capital: Tashkent
Central Asia

At a Glance

Capital: Tashkent — hosts the Regional Anti-Terrorist Structure of the SCO; major Silk Road junction; hosted the 2022 SCO Summit. (1)

Government: post-Soviet republic; modernizing under Shavkat Mirziyoyev after Islam Karimov. (1)

Doubly landlocked — one of only two doubly landlocked countries (with Liechtenstein). (1)

Silk Road Cities

Samarkand — UNESCO ancient Silk Road city; Registan Square with three madrasas; Bibi-Khanym Mosque; the Gur-e Amir mausoleum (with corrugated blue dome) holds Tamerlane; Ulugh Beg's observatory. (2)

Bukhara — UNESCO ancient Silk Road city; Kalyan Minaret; Samanid Mausoleum. (2)

Khiva — UNESCO walled desert city. (1)

Andijan — 2005 massacre site in the Fergana Valley. (1)

Geography

Kyzylkum Desert ('Red Sand Desert') — covers much of the north. (1)

Aral Sea — shared with Kazakhstan; once the world's 4th-largest lake but mostly desiccated due to Soviet-era cotton irrigation. (1)

Karakalpakstan — autonomous republic in the northwest; governed from Nukus; on the southern Aral Sea. (1)

Fergana Valley — densely populated eastern valley shared with Kyrgyzstan and Tajikistan; Namangan city. (1)

Amu Darya & Syr Darya — historic Oxus and Jaxartes rivers; both ended in the (now desiccated) Aral. (1)

Oceania

At a Glance

Capital: Port Vila — on Efate island. (1)

National anthem: 'Yumi, Yumi, Yumi' — in Bislama, the English-based creole that is the main lingua franca. (2)

Religion: Presbyterianism is the largest Christian denomination; cargo cults on Tanna worship John Frum and Prince Philip as divine figures (the Yaohnanen people). (2)

Cyclones: Cyclone Pam (2015) was the worst recorded natural disaster. (1)

Geography

Espiritu Santo — largest island. (2)

Efate — second-largest island; contains the capital. (1)

Tanna — southern island; home of the John Frum / Prince Philip cargo cults. (1)

Mount Yasur (on Tanna) — often called the world's most accessible active volcano; on Sulphur Bay. (1)

Ambrym — twin-volcano island with active lava lakes. (1)

Europe

At a Glance

Smallest country in the world by area and population. (1)

Government: absolute ecclesiastical monarchy ruled by the Pope (currently the seat of the Catholic Church). (1)

Position: entirely enclosed within Rome, Italy; established by the 1929 Lateran Treaty. (2)

Landmarks

St. Peter's Square — Bernini's colonnade-ringed piazza. (1)

Sistine Chapel — Michelangelo's ceiling and Last Judgment; site of papal conclaves. (1)

Vatican Museums — Raphael Rooms, Pinacoteca, and the Sistine Chapel. (1)

Security & Symbols

Venezuela 42
Bolivarian Republic of Venezuela · Northern South America · Capital: Caracas
South America

At a Glance

Capital: Santiago de León de Caracas — on the Guaire River between the Maritime Andes and the Caribbean coast; Aula Magna at the central university; 2017 'Mother of All Marches' protests. (1)

Government: Hugo Chávez founded the modern Bolivarian Republic; successor Nicolás Maduro in office since 2013; major political and economic crisis since the mid-2010s. (1)

Currency: the bolívar, plagued by hyperinflation. (1)

Geography

Angel Falls — world's tallest waterfall; fed by the Churún River; tumbles from Auyán-tepui in Canaima National Park; named for aviator Jimmie Angel; in the Gran Sabana tabletop-mountain region. (2)

Lake Maracaibo — South America's largest lake; site of the persistent Catatumbo Lightning; Ciudad Ojeda on its shore; opens to the Gulf of Venezuela via the Tablazo Strait. (2)

Maracaibo — second city; on the Lake Maracaibo outlet; General Rafael Urdaneta Bridge. (1)

Orinoco River — main river; flows from the Parima Mountains into the Atlantic via the Delta Amacuro; receives the Meta and Caroni Rivers; connected to the Amazon via the natural Casiquiare Canal. (2)

Guayana Esequiba — vast region west of the Essequibo River, claimed against Guyana since 2023. (1)

Tepuis — table-top mountains of the Guiana Highlands. (1)

Heritage

Simón Bolívar — 'El Libertador' born in Caracas. (1)

Oil reserves — largest proven reserves in the world; PDVSA national oil company. (1)

Culture

At a Glance

Melbourne

Coop Shot Tower — 19th-century lead-bullet factory now encased in a giant metal cone. (1)

Coffee — second-largest producer in the world (after Brazil). (1)

Puget Sound — large inland sea; the Strait of Juan de Fuca connects it to the Pacific; cities Seattle, Tacoma, Olympia, Everett. (1)

Channeled Scablands — eroded landscape from Ice Age megafloods. (1)

Industry

Landmarks

Darjeeling

Sundarbans

Western Australia 6
State of Australia · Capital: Perth · Largest state
Australia (States & Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Perth — port city of 2.3 million; world's most isolated state capital; on the Swan River / Swan Estuary; named for a city on the Firth of Tay in Scotland. (4)

Flag: features a black swan — referencing Dutch explorers' 1697 discovery of black swans on the Swan River. (1)

Stamps: government accidentally issued the blue 'inverted swan' (1855), one of the world's earliest invert errors. (1)

Rabbit-proof fence: crossed entirely by the 2,000-mile fence since 1907. (1)

Perth & Surroundings

Rottnest Island — habitat of the smiley macropod quokka (also found on Albany's Bald Island). (3)

Fremantle — Perth's port, at the mouth of the Swan River. (3)

Suburbs & beaches: Mandurah, Kwinana, Welshpool; Cottesloe Beach; bounded east by the Darling Escarpment. (2)

National Parks: John Forrest and Walyunga in the Darling Range. (1)

Christmas Island — Indian Ocean territory accessed via Perth. (1)

State Geography & Mining

Pilbara — remote iron-ore region in the northwest. (1)

Great Sandy Desert — arid expanse in the state's north. (1)

Shark Bay — UNESCO-listed bay known for stromatolites and dugongs. (1)

Mines: Argyle Diamond Mine (world's largest), Woodie Woodie manganese mine; gold rushes at Halls Creek (1885) and Kalgoorlie (1893); the Goldfields Water Supply Scheme pipeline ran to Coolgardie. (2)

Xinjiang 7
Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region · Northwest China · Capital: Ürümqi
China (Regions)

At a Glance

Capital: Ürümqi. (1)

Largest Chinese autonomous region by area; borders Mongolia, Russia, Kazakhstan, Kyrgyzstan, Tajikistan, Afghanistan (Wakhan Corridor), Pakistan, and India. (2)

Bingtuan — paramilitary corps originally founded as a buffer against Soviet aggression. (1)

East Turkestan — historical name; site of separatist movements. (1)

Geography

Two main basins: the Tarim Basin (south, containing the Taklamakan) and the Dzungarian Basin (north). (2)

Taklamakan Desert — 'place of ruins'; contains the Bronze-Age Tarim mummies; bounded by the Kunlun (south) and Tien Shan (north); the Golmud–Korla railway crosses it; oasis towns include Dandan Oilik, Yarkand, Miran. (4)

Lop Nur — formerly Xinjiang's largest lake, now mostly desiccated; site of Chinese nuclear tests. (1)

Mountains: Tien Shan (north), Kunlun (south), Altun Shan (southeast), Pamirs (southwest). (2)

Cities & Heritage

Kashgar — ancient Silk Road oasis in the far west; northern terminus of the Karakoram Highway. (2)

Hotan / Khotan — Silk Road town; historic source of nephrite jade. (2)

Yangi Hissar — town known for knife production. (1)

Qira County / Hotan Prefecture — oil/petroleum supply centers; gnamesake of the trilobite genus Taklamakania. (1)

People & History

Uyghurs — Turkic-speaking Muslim majority of southern Xinjiang. (1)

Dzungar genocide — Qing-era extermination of the Dzungar Mongols. (1)

Middle East & North Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Sanaa — one of the world's oldest continuously inhabited cities; Mahwa Aser slum inhabited by Akhdam servants saw clashes in 2008; UNESCO Old City with iconic tower houses. (2)

Crisis: worst humanitarian crisis in the world; deepening water crisis worsened by water-intensive qat cultivation; former president Ali Abdullah Saleh was killed in 2017. (1)

Cities & Regions

Aden — southern port; former capital of South Yemen; on the Gulf of Aden. (1)

Al Hudaydah — main Red Sea port, targeted by Israeli airstrikes in 2024. (1)

Geography

Socotra — UNESCO 'Island of Poets'; archipelago including Samhah and Darsah; famous for the umbrella-shaped Dragon's Blood Tree; controlled by the UAE since 2018 occupation. (2)

Zimbabwe 23
Republic of Zimbabwe · Southern Africa (landlocked) · Capital: Harare
Sub-Saharan Africa

At a Glance

Capital: Harare — in the Mashonaland region; Eastgate Centre (uses natural cooling inspired by termite mounds); New Reserve Bank Tower (headquarters of the bank that printed the famous 2008 hyperinflation banknotes with the most zeros). (2)

Former name: Southern Rhodesia / Rhodesia; renamed Zimbabwe in 1980 after the medieval Great Zimbabwe. (1)

Gukurahundi — series of 1980s massacres against the Ndebele people in Matabeleland. (1)

Geography

Zambezi River — northern border with Zambia; Victoria Falls (Mosi-oa-Tunya) straddles the border. (2)

Eastern Highlands — mountainous border with Mozambique. (1)

Cities & Heritage

Bulawayo — second city; capital of Matabeleland (Northern Ndebele-speaking region). (1)

Great Zimbabwe — UNESCO medieval Shona stone-city ruins near Masvingo; namesake of the country. (1)

Politics

Robert Mugabe — ZANU-PF leader who ruled 1980-2017; ousted in 2017. (1)
